Dispute on Capital Allocation Among Multiple Goods in Salam
Intra-Hanafi dispute on capital allocation in salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between Imam Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's positions regarding capital allocation in salam contracts, and apply the rule of safqah wahidah (single transaction) to similar cases.

Core Idea
For Abu Hanifa, unknown capital allocation in salam invalidates the contract; Sahibayn deem pointing to specific money sufficient.

This lesson examines a specific intra-Hanafi dispute about salam contracts where capital is not explicitly allocated to multiple goods or where one part of the capital is unknown. The disagreement hinges on whether pointing to physical money removes uncertainty. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply the condition of known capital (ma'lumiyyat ra's al-mal) in salam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two sub-cases
Read the passage and identify the two scenarios: (1) one hundred dirhams for two commodities (wheat and barley) without allocation; (2) two currencies (dirhams and dinars) for one commodity with one quantity unknown.
The first case involves unknown allocation per item; the second involves unknown quantity of one currency type.
2
State the ruling and reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifa
For both sub-cases, Abu Hanifa rules the contract invalid (fasid). His reasoning: the capital must be known for each muslam fihi; estimation by value is insufficient; and in the second case, because the contract is a single unit (safqah wahidah), invalidity of one portion invalidates the whole.
Focus on the principle that uncertainty in capital for any part voids the entire transaction.
3
State the ruling and reasoning of the Sahibayn
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) rule the contract valid (sahih). Their reasoning: pointing to specific, identifiable assets (the physical dirhams/dinars) is sufficient for validity; there is no need for explicit allocation or known quantity because the items are identifiable.
The Sahibayn emphasize the sufficiency of 'isharah (pointing) to known goods.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa's view, such salam contracts are invalid and must be restructured (e.g., separate contracts or explicit allocation). Under the Sahibayn's view, they are valid as long as the specific money is identifiable.
The mufta bihi (operative position) in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view, so fatwas generally require allocation.
5
Apply the rule of safqah wahidah
In the second sub-case, Abu Hanifa invokes the principle that a single contract cannot be partially valid and partially void. If one part of the capital is unknown, the whole contract is void. Apply this to similar scenarios: e.g., a single price for a mixed basket of goods.
This principle prevents splitting the contract into independent parts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ امام صاحب اور صاحبین رحمہم اللہ کے مابین اختلاف کے فروع میں سے ایک یہ مسئلہ ہے کہ اگر ایک سو در اہم کا، ایک گر گندم اور ایک گر جو میں عقد سلم کیا یعنی ایک گر گندم اور ایک گر جو کو مسلم فیہ قرار دیا اور ایک سود را ہم کو راس المال قرار دیا اور ان دونوں میں ہر ایک کا راس المال علیحدہ علیحدہ بیان نہیں کیا تو حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک یہ بیع سلم جائز نہ ہوگی اور صاحبین کے نزدیک جائز ہو جائے گی۔ امام صاحب کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ایک سو در اہم گندم اور جو پر قیمت کے اعتبار سے تقسیم کئے جائیں گے اور قیمت کی معرفت چونکہ اندازے سے ہوتی ہے اس لئے ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کے راس المال کی مقدار معلوم نہ ہوگی۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ معین شئی کی طرف اشارہ کرنا جواز عقد کے لئے کافی ہوتا ہے اور وہ پایا گیا۔ اس لئے اس صورت میں بیچ مسلم جائز ہو جائے گی ۔ یا دو جنسوں کا عقد سلم کیا اور ان میں سے ایک کی مقدار بیان نہیں کی ،مثلاً در اہم اور نا نیر کا ایک گر گندم میں عقد سلم کیا اور دراہم اور دنا نیر میں سے ایک کی مقدار معلوم ہوگئی اور دوسرے کی مقدار معلوم نہیں ہوئی تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک یہ بیع سلم نا جائز ہوگی ، کیونکہ جب ایک کی مقدار مجہول ہے تو اس کے حصہ میں عقد مسلم باطل ہو جائے گا اور جب اس کے حصہ میں عقد مسلم باطل ہو گیا تو دوسرے کے حصہ میں بھی عقد مسلم باطل ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ صفقہ ایک ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک جائز ہے کیونکہ اشارہ پایا گیا بایں طور

کہ رب السلام نے یہ کہا کہ میں نے تیرے ساتھ ان دس در اہم اور ان دنا نیر کا عقد سلم کیا یا ان دس دن نیر اور ان دراہم کا عقد مسلم کیا اور سابق میں گذر چکا ہے کہ جو از عقد کیلئے عین شئی کی طرف اشارہ کرنا کافی ہے۔
The author of the Hidayah says: Among the branches of dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is this issue: If one makes a salam contract for one hundred dirhams (as capital) for one khor of wheat and one khor of barley, i.e., making one khor wheat and one khor barley the muslam fihi, and making one hundred dirhams the capital, and does not specify the capital allocated to each separately, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa this salam sale is not valid, while according to the Sahibayn it is valid. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that the one hundred dirhams will be divided between wheat and barley according to value, and since value is known by estimation, the quantity of capital for each will not be known. The Sahibayn's proof is that pointing to a specific thing is sufficient for the validity of the contract, and that is present. Therefore, in this case the salam sale will be valid. Or if a salam contract is made for two types of currency and the quantity of one of them is not stated, e.g., dirhams and dinars for one khor of wheat, and the quantity of one of the dirhams and dinars is known while the other is not, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa this salam is invalid, because when the quantity of one is unknown, the contract for its portion becomes batil (void), and when the contract for its portion becomes batil, then the contract for the other portion also becomes batil, because the transaction (safqah) is single. And according to the Sahibayn, it is valid because pointing is present, as in the following manner: That the lord of salam (buyer) said: I have made a salam contract with you for these ten dirhams and these ten dinars, or for these ten dinars and these dirhams, and it has already passed that pointing to a specific thing is sufficient for the validity of the contract.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage presents two specific sub-cases of intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding capital allocation in salam. In the first case, a single amount of dirhams is paid for two different commodities (wheat and barley) without allocation. Imam Abu Hanifa holds the contract invalid because the capital must be known for each item, and knowing it by value estimation is insufficient. The Sahibayn argue that pointing to the physical dirhams suffices. In the second case, two types of currency (dirhams and dinars) are given for one commodity, but one of their quantities is unspecified. Imam again invalidates it because the contract is one unit; if part is void, the whole is void. The Sahibayn again consider pointing sufficient. The author then explains the Sahibayn's reasoning: the buyer can say 'these ten dirhams and these ten dinars' or similar, which indicates specific assets, and that is enough for validity.

Key Terms
راس المال (ra's al-mal): The capital paid in a salam contract; here it must be known for each muslam fihi according to Abu Hanifa.
مسلم فیہ (muslam fihi): The goods to be delivered in the future as the subject of a salam contract.
صفقة (safqah): The transaction or bargain; here it refers to a single contractual unit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the first sub-case (one hundred dirhams for wheat and barley), what is the main argument of Sahibayn for validity?
A) The price can be divided by weight.
B) Pointing to specific dirhams is sufficient for validity.
C) Wheat and barley are similar enough to be compensated.
D) The contract is valid because it is a single transaction.

Key Takeaway
When capital is not allocated among multiple goods in salam, Abu Hanifa deems it invalid due to uncertainty, while the Sahibayn accept pointing to specific money; the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) follows Abu Hanifa.

Place of Delivery in Salam: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on place of delivery in salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the place of delivery in salam and explain the key distinction based on immediate vs deferred delivery.

Core Idea
If delivery is deferred, the place of contract is not automatically the place of delivery.

In a salam contract, the price is paid in advance but the commodity is delivered later. A key question arises: must the place of delivery be explicitly stated, or is the place of contract automatically the place of delivery? This lesson examines the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two companions, the Sahibayn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The issue is whether the place where the salam contract is signed automatically becomes the place where the muslam fihi must be delivered.
This affects contract validity if the place is not specified.
2
State the Sahibayn's position and proof
The Sahibayn argue that the place of contract is determined for delivery because the contract obligating delivery exists there. No other place competes, so analogy is made to loan (qard) and usurpation (ghasb), and to the first part of prayer time being the cause of obligation.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa argues that delivery in salam is not immediate (it is deferred), so the place of contract is not automatically determined. Ignorance of place leads to dispute because values vary by location, so the place must be explicitly stated.
Key distinction: immediate vs deferred delivery.
4
Analyze the distinction
In loan and usurpation, delivery is required immediately. In salam, delivery is at a future term. Therefore, the place is not automatically fixed. If it were fixed, the deferred nature would be irrelevant.
This is a qiyas mu'arid (competing analogy).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
According to Abu Hanifa, if the place is not specified, the contract is invalid (fasid) due to uncertainty. According to the Sahibayn, no specification is needed; the place is automatically the contract location.
Later practice tends to follow Abu Hanifa.

Source Text

وہ چیز جس کا فی الحال سپرد کرنا واجب نہ ہو اس کو سپر د کر نے کیلئے مکان عقد متعین نہیں ہوتا پس ثابت ہوا کہ مسلم فیہ سپرد کرنے کیلئے مکان عقد متعین نہیں ہے۔ برخلاف قرض اور نصب کے کیونکہ قرض اور غصب میں فی الحال سپر د کرنا واجب ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ قرضہ میں میعاد مقرر کرنے سے میعاد مقرر نہیں ہوتی
According to the Sahibayn, specifying the place of delivery is not a condition.

And their proof in the second issue is that the place of contract is determined because the contract that obligates delivery exists in that place, and because no other place competes with it. So it becomes analogous to the first possible times in commands, and it becomes like loan (qard) and usurpation (ghasb). According to Abu Hanifa, delivery is not obligatory immediately, so it is not determined, unlike loan and usurpation. And when it is not determined, ignorance of it leads to dispute because the values of things vary with location. Therefore, it must be stated, and it becomes like unknown description.

Translation: And in the second issue, the proof of the Sahibayn is that the place of contract is determined for delivery because the contract that obligates delivery is consummated in that place, and because no other place is competing with it. So it becomes analogous to the first possible times in commands, and it becomes like loan and usurpation. And the proof of Abu Hanifa is that since delivery of the muslam fihi is not obligatory immediately, the place of contract is not determined, unlike loan and usurpation. And when it is not determined, its ignorance leads to dispute because the values of things differ with location. Therefore, statement is necessary, and it becomes like unknown description.

Explanation: In the second disputed issue, regarding whether the place of contract is determined for delivery of the muslam fihi, the proof of the Sahibayn is that the salam contract that obligates delivery is found in that same place. So wherever the obligating contract is found, delivery of the muslam fihi becomes obligatory in that place. And when delivery in the place of contract becomes obligatory, it is not necessary to mention another place for delivery, just like if someone buys specified wheat in a village, the seller is obligated to deliver it in the same place where he sold it. So similarly, wherever the salam contract occurs, the seller is obligated to deliver the muslam fihi in that place. A second proof is that delivery of the muslam fihi requires a place, and all places are equal for delivery; none is preferred over another. However, since the place of contract has preference due to the contract, it has no competitor. Therefore, the place becomes determined for delivery. And this is like the first part of prayer time, which, due to having no competitor, becomes the cause of the obligation of prayer itself. And this becomes like loan and usurpation. That is, just as the place of loan is determined for repayment and the place of usurpation is determined for return of misappropriated property, similarly the place of the salam contract is determined for delivery of the muslam fihi. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that since in salam, fixing a term (ajal) is a condition, delivery of the muslam fihi is not obligatory immediately at the time of the contract, but rather it becomes obligatory upon completion of the term. And for anything whose delivery is not obligatory immediately, the place of contract is not determined for its delivery. Thus it is established that the place of contract is not determined for delivery of the muslam fihi. Unlike loan (qard) and usurpation (ghasb), because in loan and usurpation, delivery is obligatory immediately. This is why fixing a term in a loan does not set a valid term (i.e., a loan with a fixed term is not valid).
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage discusses the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the place where the salam contract is concluded is automatically the place where the muslam fihi must be delivered. The Sahibayn argue that since the contract obligates delivery, and it is concluded in a specific place, that place becomes the default place for delivery, analogous to loan (qard) and usurpation (ghasb) where immediate return is required. They also analogize to the first part of prayer time being the cause of obligation. Abu Hanifa counters that delivery in salam is deferred, not immediate, so the place of contract is not automatically determined. Since the values of goods may differ by location, leaving the place unknown would lead to dispute; thus the place must be explicitly stated. He distinguishes from loan and usurpation where immediate delivery is obligatory.

Key Terms
مکان ایفاء (makan al-ifa'): The place where the muslam fihi is to be delivered in a salam contract.
قرض (qard): A loan that is immediately repayable at the lender's demand.
غصب (ghasb): Usurpation; the misappropriated property must be returned immediately.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main reason Abu Hanifa gives for requiring specification of the delivery place in a salam contract?
A) Because salam is a contract of trust (amana).
B) Because delivery is not immediate so the place is not automatically determined.
C) Because the seller must always deliver at his own location.
D) Because the buyer has a right to choose any location.

Key Takeaway
The determination of delivery place in a salam contract depends on whether delivery is immediate or deferred; Abu Hanifa requires specification to avoid uncertainty.

Extension of Place of Delivery Ruling to Price, Rent, and Partition
Discusses whether the dispute on place of delivery extends to price, rent, and partition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on whether the place of delivery must be specified for deferred price (thaman mu'ajjal) and state the preferred view (mufta bihi) that specification is required.

Core Idea
The ruling on place of delivery extends beyond salam to any deferred obligation, requiring specification to avoid invalidity.

In the previous lesson, we learned about the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the place of delivery in salam contracts. Now, we explore whether that same dispute applies to other types of obligations — specifically the price (thaman) in a sale, rent (ujrah), and the shares in a partition (qisma). The Hanafi scholars differ, and the preferred view settles that specification is required when the price is deferred.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is specification of the place of delivery for deferred obligations (thaman, ujrah, qisma). The ruling: according to the preferred view, specification is wajib when the price is deferred.
2
Locate the dalil
The dalil is qiyas (analogy) to salam: ignorance of place in salam leads to tahalf and potential invalidity; the same applies to deferred price.
The passage states the analogy explicitly: 'as in the case of description'.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The effective cause (illa) is the potential for dispute due to ignorance of the place. Since the place affects the cost and convenience of delivery, its ignorance creates uncertainty similar to ignorance of description.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa (and Sarakhsi following him) hold that specification is required; the Sahibayn hold that the place is determined by the contract itself, so no separate specification is needed.
The difference stems from whether determination of place is a requirement of the contract (qada' al-aqd) or not.
5
Determine the tarjih
Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi's view (specification required for deferred price) is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in later Hanafi fatwa.
This is noted as 'al-sahih' in the passage.

Source Text

مکان ایفاء اور اختلاف فقہاء
و عن هذا قال من قال من المشائخ ان الاختلاف فيه عنده يوجب التحالف كما في الصفة وقيل على عكسه لان تعين الـمـكـان قضية العقد عندهما وعلى لهذا الخلاف الثمن والاجرة والقسمة وصورتها اذا اقتسما دارا وجعلا مع نصيب احدهما شيئا له حمل ومونة وقيل لا يشترط ذلك فى الثمن والصحيح انه يشترط اذا كان مؤجلا وهو اختيار شمس الائمة السرخسى وعندهما يتعين مكان الدار ومكان تسليم الدابة للايفاء
ترجمہ اور یہیں سے مشائخ میں سے جس نے کہا یوں کہا کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک ادائے مسلم فیہ کی جگہ میں اختلاف کرنا با ہم تم کو واجب کرتاہ، جیسے صفت میں ہے۔ اور کہا گیا کہ اس کے برعکس ہے، کیونکہ صاحبین کے نزدیک مکان کا متعین ہو جانا عقد کا من مقتدى ہے۔ اور اسی اختلاف پر تمن ، اجرت اور بٹوارہ ہے۔ اور بنوارہ کی صورت یہ ہے کہ دونوں نے اپنا مشترک مکان تقسیم کیا اور دونوں نے ایک کے حصہ کے ساتھ ایسی چیز ملائی جس کے واسطے بار برداری اور خرچہ ہے اور کہا گیا کہ یمن کی صورت میں یہ شرط نہیں ہے۔ اور صحیح یہ ہے کہ (امام صاحب کے نزدیک ادائے مشن کی جگہ بیان کرنا ) شرط ہے بشرطیکہ شمن میعادی ہو ۔ اور یہی شمس الائمہ سرخسٹی کا پسندیدہ مذہب ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک ادا کیلئے مکان دار اور جانور سپر د کرنے کی جگہ متعین ہے۔
تشریح صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جہالت مکان چونکہ جہالت وصف کے مانند ہے ( یعنی جس طرح صفت جودت اور صفت
And from this, some of the scholars said that the disagreement regarding it (the place) according to him (Abu Hanifa) necessitates mutual oath (tahalf) as in the case of description. And it was said the opposite, because the determination of the place is a requirement of the contract according to them (the Sahibayn). And upon this disagreement depends the price, the rent, and the partition. And its picture: when they divide a house and attach to the share of one of them something that has transport and expense. And it was said that this condition is not required in the case of the price, and the correct is that it is required if it is deferred (mu'ajjal). This is the choice of Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi. And according to them (Sahibayn), the place of the house and the place of delivery of the animal are determined for performance.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage extends the earlier dispute on the place of delivery in salam to other transactions. It notes that according to some scholars, the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn about whether the place must be specified leads to the ruling that if the parties dispute the place, they must take mutual oaths (tahalf) as in cases where the description is unknown. Others say the opposite: since the place is determined for the Sahibayn, no oath is needed. The ruling on price (thaman), rent (ujrah), and partition (qisma) follows the same principle. A specific example: if two co-owners divide a house and one gets a share with heavy items requiring transport, the place of delivery must be specified if the price is deferred. The preferred view, chosen by Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, is that specification is required for deferred price. According to the Sahibayn, the place of the house or animal is determined by the contract itself. The commentary emphasizes that ignorance of place is like ignorance of description, which invalidates the sale.

Key Terms
ثمن (thaman): The price in a sale; here specifically the deferred price (thaman mu'ajjal).
أجرة (ujrah): Rent or hire payment; its delivery place is similarly debated.
قسمة (qisma): Partition of jointly owned property; the place of delivery of shares is discussed.
تحالف (tahalf): Mutual oath taken by parties when there is a dispute over a contractual term that cannot be resolved.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view of Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, when is specifying the place of delivery required for the price (thaman)?
A) Always, regardless of when payment is due.
B) Only if the price is deferred (mu'ajjal).
C) Never, because price is not physically delivered.
D) Only in salam sales.

Key Takeaway
The requirement to specify the place of delivery for deferred obligations is a necessary extension of the salam ruling to prevent contractual disputes.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Specifying the Place of Delivery in Salam: The Core Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on place of delivery in salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the place of delivery in salam and explain the proof of each based on the analogy with qard/ghasb and the boat example.

Core Idea
In salam, the place of delivery must be specified because location affects value; the contract place does not automatically suffice.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute over whether the place of contract (makan al-'aqd) automatically determines the place of delivery (makan al-ada') in salam, or whether explicit stipulation is required. The disagreement has practical consequences for contract validity and dispute resolution.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish salam from qard and ghasb
Identify why immediate delivery obligations in qard and ghasb tie delivery to the contract place, whereas salam's deferred nature creates uncertainty.
The key difference is timing of performance.
2
State the positions
Imam Abu Hanifa: delivery place must be specified; Sahibayn: the contract place determines delivery.
3
Examine Imam Abu Hanifa's proof
The boat example: if contract on a moving boat, no fixed place; thus the contract place cannot be the delivery place. Also, analogy to unknown quality: jahl in place causes uncertainty in value.
This rebuts the Sahibayn's muqtada argument.
4
Examine the Sahibayn's proof
Place of contract is muqtada al-'aqd; a dispute over delivery place should trigger tahaluf like a dispute over the contract itself.
They analogize to a dispute over the subject matter.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: if delivery place is unspecified and dispute arises, Imam Abu Hanifa invalidates the contract due to jahl; Sahibayn uphold it and determine delivery at contract place.
The implication for validity and dispute resolution.

Chapter of Salam. ... (Full literal translation not provided due to length; it is a detailed explanation of the place of delivery in salam and related contracts, with the disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.)
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses the place of delivery (makan al-ifa') in the salam contract and extends the ruling to other contracts like thaman (price), ujrah (rent), and qismah (division). The author first contrasts salam with qard (loan) and ghasb (usurpation): in those, immediate delivery is obligatory at the place of contract; in salam, since payment and delivery are deferred, the place of contract does not automatically determine the place of delivery. This leads to potential dispute because the value of the commodity may vary by location. The core disagreement is between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the place of delivery must be specified in the contract; if not, the contract is invalid due to uncertainty (jahl) akin to unknown quality. The Sahibayn hold that the place of contract itself determines the place of delivery, as it is a requirement (muqtada) of the contract. Imam Abu Hanifa refutes this with the example of a contract made on a boat in the middle of a river: the boat is not a suitable location for delivery. The dispute extends to: (1) thaman (price) in a deferred sale: Imam Abu Hanifa requires specifying the place of payment if the price is deferred and transport costs are involved; (2) ujrah (rent): same debate; (3) qismah (division) of a shared house where one party owes a movable commodity to the other. The passage also mentions that some mashayikh (scholars) rule that such a dispute triggers tahaluf (mutual oath) according to Imam Abu Hanifa, similar to a dispute over quality, while others (following the Sahibayn) say it does not. The relied-upon position (sahih) is that Imam Abu Hanifa requires stipulation of place when the price is deferred and has transport cost, as chosen by Shams al-A'immah al-Sarakhsi.

Key Terms
مکان الاداء (makan al-ada'): The place where a debt or commodity is to be delivered or paid.
تحالف (tahaluf): Mutual oath taken by two disputing parties when evidence is lacking; the contract is rescinded if both swear.
مقتضی عقد (muqtada al-'aqd): The inherent legal consequence or requirement of a contract without explicit stipulation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the primary reason that the place of delivery must be specified in a salam contract?
A) Because the contract is otherwise invalid due to gharar.
B) Because the value of the commodity can vary by location, creating uncertainty like unknown quality.
C) Because the Sahibayn required it.
D) Because the place of contract is always the delivery place.

Key Takeaway
The place of delivery in salam must be specified when value varies by location, according to the relied-upon Hanafi view, to avoid uncertainty.

Extending the Dispute: Thaman, Ujrah, Qismah, and the Tahaluf Ruling
Extension of the dispute and the tahaluf ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the same intra-Hanafi dispute to thaman (deferred price), ujrah (rent), and qismah (division), and explain the rule on tahaluf (mutual oath) when the parties disagree on delivery place.

Core Idea
The dispute over place of delivery in salam extends to deferred price, rent, and division contracts, with a similar split on whether specification is required.

This lesson extends the previous discussion to other contracts where the same issue arises: thaman (deferred price in a sale), ujrah (rent), and qismah (division of jointly owned property). It also examines the procedural consequence of tahaluf (mutual oath) when the parties disagree on the delivery place. Understanding the scope helps a mufti apply the correct ruling across different contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contracts affected
The passage explicitly extends the dispute to thaman (deferred price), ujrah (rent), and qismah (division). Understand that in each, there is an obligation to deliver a commodity at a future time.
These are all cases where the obligation is not immediate.
2
State the extension for each contract
For each contract, Imam Abu Hanifa requires specification of the delivery place; the Sahibayn say the contract place suffices.
The same reasoning applies: value may vary by location.
3
Understand the exception for thaman
Some scholars say that for thaman, specification is not required by consensus (bil ijma). However, the correct (sahih) view is that it is required when the price is deferred and transport costs apply, as chosen by al-Sarakhsi.
The exception highlights the importance of cost transport.
4
Explain the tahaluf rule
According to some mashayikh, if the parties dispute the delivery place, tahaluf (mutual oath) becomes wajib according to Imam Abu Hanifa, similar to a dispute over quality. According to others (and the Sahibayn), tahaluf is not triggered because the place is determined by the contract.
This affects how a judge resolves the dispute.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that specification is required for deferred price with transport cost, and tahaluf applies according to Imam Abu Hanifa's view when the place is unspecified.
Muftis should follow this in issuing fatwas.

Chapter of Salam. ... (Full literal translation not provided due to length; it is a detailed explanation of the place of delivery in salam and related contracts, with the disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.)
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses the place of delivery (makan al-ifa') in the salam contract and extends the ruling to other contracts like thaman (price), ujrah (rent), and qismah (division). The author first contrasts salam with qard (loan) and ghasb (usurpation): in those, immediate delivery is obligatory at the place of contract; in salam, since payment and delivery are deferred, the place of contract does not automatically determine the place of delivery. This leads to potential dispute because the value of the commodity may vary by location. The core disagreement is between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the place of delivery must be specified in the contract; if not, the contract is invalid due to uncertainty (jahl) akin to unknown quality. The Sahibayn hold that the place of contract itself determines the place of delivery, as it is a requirement (muqtada) of the contract. Imam Abu Hanifa refutes this with the example of a contract made on a boat in the middle of a river: the boat is not a suitable location for delivery. The dispute extends to: (1) thaman (price) in a deferred sale: Imam Abu Hanifa requires specifying the place of payment if the price is deferred and transport costs are involved; (2) ujrah (rent): same debate; (3) qismah (division) of a shared house where one party owes a movable commodity to the other. The passage also mentions that some mashayikh (scholars) rule that such a dispute triggers tahaluf (mutual oath) according to Imam Abu Hanifa, similar to a dispute over quality, while others (following the Sahibayn) say it does not. The relied-upon position (sahih) is that Imam Abu Hanifa requires stipulation of place when the price is deferred and has transport cost, as chosen by Shams al-A'immah al-Sarakhsi.

Key Terms
مکان الاداء (makan al-ada'): The place where a debt or commodity is to be delivered or paid.
تحالف (tahaluf): Mutual oath taken by two disputing parties when evidence is lacking; the contract is rescinded if both swear.
مقتضی عقد (muqtada al-'aqd): The inherent legal consequence or requirement of a contract without explicit stipulation.
ثمن (thaman): Price (in a sale), especially deferred price.
اجرة (ujrah): Rent or hire payment.
قسمة (qismah): Division of jointly owned property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct (sahih) view in the Hanafi school, when is specification of place required for thaman (deferred price)?
A) Always, for any deferred price.
B) Never, because of ijma.
C) Only when the price is deferred and transport costs are involved.
D) Only when the price is paid in cash.

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute over delivery place extends to deferred price, rent, and division, with the relied-upon view requiring specification when transport costs apply.

Specifying Delivery Place in Salam: Imam vs Sahibayn
Intra-madhhab dispute on delivery place specification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ on the necessity of specifying the delivery place in salam, and state the consequence when a dispute arises.

Core Idea
For goods with transport cost, Imam requires specifying delivery place; Sahibayn accept place of contract.

This passage examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the requirement to specify the delivery place for goods that have transport burden. The ruling affects whether a salam contract is valid if the place is unspecified, and what happens if the parties later disagree. Understanding this dispute clarifies the Hanafi school's distinction between essential terms (muqtada al-aqd) and supplementary specifications.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify the precise legal question: Is specifying the place of delivery for muslam fih with transport burden wajib? And if the parties later dispute the agreed place, do they undergo tahlif (mutual oaths)?
The issue arises only when the goods have transport costs; for goods without burden, the rule may differ.
2
Identify the two positions
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that specifying the place is wajib because the place affects price; the Sahibayn hold it is not wajib because the place of contract itself designates delivery.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, so both views are within the school.
3
Analyze the proofs of each
Imam's proof: Place of delivery is like a term (mi'ad), not a requirement of the contract; dispute about a term does not warrant tahlif. Sahibayn's proof: Place of delivery is a requirement of the contract; dispute about it is like disputing the contract itself, which by consensus requires tahlif.
The disagreement hinges on whether the delivery place is a muqtada al-aqd or an external condition.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If the parties dispute the delivery place and swear oaths, per Imam the muslam ilayh's word is accepted and the contract continues; per Sahibayn, if both swear the contract is annulled.
The practical impact is whether the sale remains valid or is rescinded.
5
Note the tarjih
Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi selected Imam Abu Hanifa's view for goods with transport burden, making it the mufta bihi position.
The authority weight is zahir riwayah, but the later preference (ikhtiyar) of Sarakhsi settles the fatwa.

متعین کیا گیا تھا اور گواہ کسی کے پاس موجود نہیں ہیں تو ایسی صورت میں دونوں سے قسم لی جائے گی ۔ اور اگر ایک قسم کھا گیا اور دوسرے نے انکار کر دیا تو منکر قتم کے خلاف فیصلہ دیا جائے گا۔ اور اگر دونوں کہ مکان عقد کا ادائے مسلم فیہ کیلئے متعین ہونا یہ عقد کا مقتضی ہے۔ پس ادائے مسلم فیہ کی جگہ میں اختلاف کرنا ایسا ہے جیسا کہ نفس عقد میں اختلاف کرنا اور نفس عقد میں اختلاف چونکہ بالا جماع تحالف واجب کرتا ہے۔ اس لئے ادائے مسلم فیہ کی جگہ میں اختلاف کرنا بھی تحالف واجب کر دے گا۔ امام صاحب کی دلیل یہ ہےکہ ادائے مسلم فیہ کی جگہ کا تعین ہونا چونکہ عقد کا مقتضی نہیں ہے اس لئے یہ بمنزلہ میعاد کے ہو گیا۔ اور میعاد میں عاقدین کا اختلاف چونکہ تحالف واجب نہیں کرتا اس لئے ادائے مسلم فیہ کی جگہ میں اختلاف کرنا بھی متخالف کو واجب نہیں کرے گا بلکہ مسلم الیہ جس پر ادائے مسلم فیہ واجب ہے اس کا قول معتبر ہو گا۔ کی جگہ کا بیان کرنا ضروری نہیں ہے بلکہ جس جگہ کرایہ کا مکان ہے وہی جگہ دس من گندم سپرد کرنے کیلئے متعین ہے، اور جہاں جانور سپر د کیا ہے اسی جگہ اجرت کے دس من گندم کو ادا کرے۔ اور بٹوارہ کی صورت یہ ہے کہ دو آدمیوں نے اپنا مشتر کہ مکان تقسیم کیا اور ایک حصہ میں ایسی چیز ملائی جس کے واسطے بار برداری اور خرچہ پڑتا ہے یعنی اس کو منتقل کرنے میں خرچہ پڑتا ہے تو حضرت امام صاحب کے نزدیک اس چیز کو ادا کرنے کی جگہ کا بیان کرنا ضروری ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک یہ شرط نہیں ہے بلکہ جس جگہ ہوارہ ہوا ہے وہی جگہ متعین ہے۔ بعض مشائخ نے کہا کہ ثمن کی صورت میں بالا جماع مکان ادا کا بیان کرنا شرط نہیں ہے ۔ مگر صحیح یہ ہے کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک ادائے شمن کی جگہ کا بیان کرنا شرط ہے بشرطیکہ ثمن میعادی ادھار ہو۔ اور اس کو منتقل کرنے میں خرچہ پڑتا ہو۔ اس کو شمس الائمہ سرخسی نے اختیار کیا ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک جہاں مکان کا ہوارہ ہو و ہیں اُس چیز کو سپر دکر دے جو ایک کے حصہ کے ساتھ ملائی گئی ہے
Chapter of Salam. The difference in [؟] causes a difference in price. Similarly, the difference in place of delivery causes a difference in price. Therefore some scholars said that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the dispute between rabb al-salam and muslam ilayh regarding the place of delivery of the muslam fih necessitates tahlif (swearing of oaths). For example, if rabb al-salam says that for delivery of muslam fih, Deoband was specified, and muslam ilayh claims that Saharanpur was specified, and there are no witnesses, then in such a case oaths will be taken from both. And if one swears and the other refuses, then a decision will be given against the one who refuses. And if both swear, the salam contract will be annulled, just as in case of dispute between the parties regarding the attribute of one of the two substitutes in a salam contract, oath is wajib upon both. According to the Sahibayn, since the place of contract is determined for the delivery of muslam fih, therefore according to them, the dispute will not necessitate tahlif. And according to some scholars, tahlif will not be wajib, rather the word of muslam ilayh will be accepted, and according to the Sahibayn, mutual oaths are wajib. The proof of the Sahibayn is that the determination of the place of contract for delivery of muslam fih is a requirement of the contract. So disputing about the place of delivery is like disputing about the contract itself, and dispute about the contract itself, by consensus, necessitates tahlif. Therefore disputing about the place of delivery will also necessitate tahlif. Imam's proof is that the determination of the place of delivery is not a requirement of the contract, so it is like the term. Dispute about the term does not necessitate tahlif, so dispute about place of delivery will not necessitate tahlif; rather the word of muslam ilayh who is obligated to deliver will be accepted. This same difference applies to thaman, ujrah, and partition. The case of thaman: a man buys a house on credit for ten mans of good wheat, setting a term of two months for payment. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, specifying the place of delivery of the ten mans of wheat is necessary. If the place is specified, it is permissible; otherwise not. According to the Sahibayn, specifying the place is not a condition; rather he will deliver at the place where the contract occurred. Similarly, if he rents a house or an animal for ten mans of wheat, Imam says specifying the place is necessary; Sahibayn say not necessary; rather the place of the rented house is determined for delivery, and where the animal was delivered, the rent is to be paid there. And for partition: two people divide their shared house, and one portion includes an item that has transport burden and expense. According to Imam, specifying the place of delivery is necessary; Sahibayn say it is not a condition; rather the place where the division occurred is determined. Some scholars said that in the case of thaman, by consensus, specifying place is not a condition. But the correct view is that according to Imam, specifying the place for thaman is a condition if the thaman is deferred credit and transferring it incurs expense. This is what Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi selected. According to the Sahibayn, wherever the house is, he will deliver the item that is combined with one share.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the specification and consequences of the place of delivery in a salam contract when the muslam fih (the subject matter) has transport costs and expenses. The author states that the value of the muslam fih can vary with different places, and similarly, the place of delivery can affect value. Therefore, some scholars hold that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, if the parties (rabb al-salam and muslam ilayh) dispute the agreed place of delivery without evidence, tahlif (mutual oaths) is required. For example, if one says Deoband and the other says Saharanpur, both take oaths. If one refuses, judgment against him. If both swear, the contract is annulled. This is analogous to a dispute about the attribute of the subject matter. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), the place of contract (makan al-aqd) is determined by the contract itself, so a dispute does not require tahlif; rather, the muslam ilayh's statement is accepted. Some scholars take a middle position. The Sahibayn's proof: the place of delivery is a requirement of the contract, so disputing it is like disputing the contract, which by consensus requires tahlif. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof: the place of delivery is not a requirement of the contract but is like a term (mi'ad); dispute about a term does not require tahlif, so here the muslam ilayh's word is accepted. This same difference is found in cases of thaman (price), ujrah (rent), and partition. The text explains each: in a credit sale where the price is goods with transport cost, Imam requires specifying the place of delivery; Sahibayn do not. In a rental contract, Imam requires specifying the place for payment of rent; Sahibayn say the place of the rented property or delivery of the animal is the designated place. In partition of a shared property, if one share contains an item that requires transport, Imam requires specifying the delivery place; Sahibayn say the place of division is determined. The author concludes that some scholars say there is consensus that for thaman (price) specifying place is not required, but the correct view according to Imam is that it is required when the thaman is deferred and has transport cost, as chosen by Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi. This lesson covers the full intra-madhhab dispute with proofs and applications to various contracts.

Key Terms
تحالف (tahlif): The procedure of taking oaths from both parties in a contract dispute when there is no evidence; it leads to annulment of the contract if both swear.
مکان عقد (makan al-aqd): The place where the contract of salam was concluded; according to Sahibayn, this is the designated place of delivery unless otherwise specified.
مکان ایفا (makan al-ifa'): The place where the muslam fih or price is to be delivered.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling when parties dispute the place of delivery for goods with transport burden and have no evidence?
A) The contract is annulled immediately.
B) Both parties take oaths, and if both swear, the contract is annulled.
C) The word of the seller (muslam ilayh) is accepted.
D) The word of the buyer (rabb al-salam) is accepted.

Key Takeaway
Imam Abu Hanifa treats the delivery place as a supplementary term like a deadline, not a contract requirement, so the seller's word prevails; the Sahibayn treat it as integral, requiring tahlif.

Delivery Place for Goods Without Transport Cost in Salam
Ruling and intra-madhhab ikhtilaf on delivery place for lightweight goods

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for specifying delivery place in salam for lightweight goods and identify the more correct Hanafi position.

Core Idea
For goods without transport cost, delivery place need not be specified; the seller may deliver anywhere.

In a salam contract, the place of delivery is important for goods that vary in value by location or incur transport cost. But what about lightweight, valuable goods like musk or saffron? This lesson examines the Hanafi consensus and an internal difference of opinion on this point, helping you understand when specification is superfluous and when it becomes binding.

Guided Path
1
Classify the Goods
Identify whether the goods have transport burden (haml wa ma'unah) or not. This classification determines the ruling.
Goods without burden include musk, camphor, saffron – items with negligible weight and no location-based price difference.
2
State the Consensus
For goods without burden, there is consensus (ijmaʿ) that no place need be specified in the salam contract. The default place of delivery is the contract location.
This is because the value does not change across places, so specification serves no purpose.
3
Identify the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Note that Imam Muhammad transmitted two views: one from Jamiʿ al-Saghir and Kitab al-Buyuʿ (delivery at contract place), and another from Kitab al-Ijarat (delivery anywhere). The latter is considered more correct (asahh).
The difference stems from whether the ‘place of contract’ is implicitly intended or any place suffices given the equality of all places.
4
Analyze the Effect of Specifying a Place
If the parties do specify a place, two opinions exist: it becomes non-binding (because it provides no benefit) or it becomes binding (because it eliminates the risk of travel). The passage does not give tarjih here.
For goods with burden, specifying the city (misr) is sufficient, as the whole city is treated as one location.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وما لم يكن له حمل ومؤنة لا يحتاج فيه الى بيان مكان الايفاء بالاجماع لانه لا يختلف قيمته ويوفيه في المكان الذى اسلم فيه قال رضى الله عنه وهذا رواية الجامع الصغير والبيوع وذكر في الاجارات انه يوفيه الـ فى اى مكان شاء وهو الاصح لان الاماكن كلها سواء ولا وجوب فى الحال ولو عيّنا مكانا قيل لا يتعين لانه لا يفيد وقيل يتعين لانه يفيد سقوط خطر الطريق ولو عين المصر فيما له حمل ومؤنة يكتفى به لانه مع تباين اطرافه كبقعة واحدة فيما ذكرنا
He said: And whatever has no transport burden and expense, there is no need to specify the place of delivery by consensus, because its value does not differ, and he delivers it in the place where he made the salam. He (the author) said, may Allah be pleased with him: This is the riwayah of Jami' al-Saghir and al-Buyu' (i.e., Mabsut's book of sales). And in al-Ijarat, it is mentioned that he delivers it in any place he wishes, and that is more correct, because all places are equal, and there is no immediate obligation. If they specify a place, it is said that it is not specified because it does not benefit; and it is said that it is specified because it benefits by eliminating the risk of the road. If he specifies the city (misr) for something that has transport burden, it suffices, because despite the variance of its outskirts, it is like one locality in what we mentioned.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling for goods that are lightweight and have no transport cost (like musk, camphor, saffron). The author (Quduri) states that by consensus, it is not necessary to specify a place of delivery for such goods because their value does not vary by location. The default delivery place is where the salam contract was made. However, the commentator (author of Ashraf al-Hidaya) notes two riwayat (transmissions) from Imam Muhammad's works. The first, from Jami' al-Saghir and Mabsut's Kitab al-Buyu', holds that the place of the contract is the designated delivery spot. The second, from Mabsut's Kitab al-Ijarat, holds that the muslam ilayh may deliver wherever he wishes, and that this is the more correct position (asahh). The reasoning is that since all places are equal in value for such goods, there is no reason to fix one place. Also, there is no immediate obligation (la wujub fi al-hal) to deliver at the moment of contract. If the parties do specify a place, there are two opinions: one that it is not binding because it serves no purpose (value same everywhere), and another that it is binding because it removes the risk of transport (e.g., if the recipient must travel). The passage ends with a note: if for goods with burden, the parties merely specify the city (misr), that suffices, because the entire city is considered one spot for this purpose, despite its varying areas.

Key Terms
حمل ومؤنة (haml wa ma'unah): Transport burden and expense; refers to goods that are heavy, costly to move, and vary in value by location.
مصر (misr): A city or large town; specifying the city is sufficient for goods with burden.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
For a salam contract involving 1 kg of saffron (no transport cost), what is the relied-upon ruling about the place of delivery?
A) The place must be specified in the contract.
B) Delivery must be at the place of contract.
C) The muslam ilayh may deliver at any place he chooses.
D) The rabb al-salam chooses the place.

Key Takeaway
In salam, goods without transport burden require no delivery place specification; the seller may deliver anywhere, based on the preferred Hanafi view.

Place of Delivery in Salam Without Transport Cost
Intra-Hanafi dispute on delivery place for salam goods without transport cost

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi narrations on the place of delivery for salam goods without transport cost and identify the preferred view.

Core Idea
For salam goods without transport cost, delivery anywhere is preferred; specification is unnecessary by consensus.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a practical question: where must goods be delivered in a salam (advance payment) contract when the goods have no transport cost? The Hanafi school has two narrations from Imam Muhammad, and the preferred ruling allows delivery at any place. Understanding this dispute clarifies when specifying a delivery location is legally beneficial.

Guided Path
1
Identify the goods category
Determine whether the muslam fihi (goods) has transport cost and expense (حمولة ومؤنة) or not. This passage deals with goods that do not incur such costs.
Goods without transport cost have uniform value across locations.
2
State the consensus
Note that by consensus (بالاجماع), there is no need to specify a delivery place for such goods because their value does not differ by location.
Ijma is the proof.
3
Contrast the two narrations
Identify the two riwayat from Imam Muhammad: (1) from al-Jami' al-Saghir and Kitab al-Buyu' – delivery at the contract place; (2) from Kitab al-Ijarat – delivery anywhere the seller wishes. The second is deemed more correct (الاصح).
The dispute is intra-Hanafi, not with other schools.
4
Analyse the effect of specifying a place
Even if not required, if the parties specify a place, two views exist: it either becomes binding (because it removes road risk) or not (because it gives no benefit). The text leaves this open.
For goods with transport cost, specifying the city suffices without needing a district.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وما لم يكن له حمل ومؤنة لا يحتاج فيه الى بيان مكان الايفاء بالاجماع لانه لا يختلف قيمته ويوفيه في المكان الذى اسلم فيه قال رضى الله عنه وهذا رواية الجامع الصغير والبيوع وذكر في الاجارات انه يوفيه في اى مكان شاء وهو الاصح لان الاماكن كلها سواء ولا وجوب فى الحال ولو عيّنا مكانا قيل لا يتعين لانه لا يفيد وقيل يتعين لانه يفيد سقوط خطر الطريق ولو عين المصر فيما له حمل ومؤنة يكتفى به لانه مع تباين اطرافه كبقعة واحدة فيما ذكرنا
He said: And whatever does not have transport and expense, there is no need to specify a place of delivery by consensus, because its value does not differ. And he delivers it at the place where the salam was contracted. He (may Allah be pleased with him) said: This is a narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Buyu'. And it is mentioned in al-Ijarat that he delivers it in whichever place he wishes, and this is more correct, because all places are equal and there is no immediate obligation. If they specify a place, it is said it is not specified because it yields no benefit; and it is said it is specified because it yields the waiver of the risk of the road. And if one specifies the city for that which has transport and expense, it suffices, because despite the diversity of its outskirts, it is like a single location in what we have mentioned.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage from Hidayah presents the ruling on the place of delivery for salam goods that do not incur transport costs. By consensus, no specific place is required because the value is uniform. The default place is the contract location. Two narrations from Imam Muhammad exist: one from al-Jami' al-Saghir and Kitab al-Buyu' holds the contract location binding; another from Kitab al-Ijarat allows delivery anywhere, deemed more correct. Mutual specification of a place is beneficial to eliminate road risk. For goods with transport cost, specifying a city suffices without needing a district.

Key Terms
سلم (salam): A forward sale where payment is made upfront for goods to be delivered later.
مسلم فیہ (muslam fihi): The object of sale in a salam contract; the goods to be delivered later.
ایفاء (ifa'): Delivery of the muslam fihi by the seller to the buyer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred narration in Hidayah, where must goods without transport cost be delivered?
A) At the place of contract only
B) At any place the seller chooses
C) At the buyer's residence
D) At the nearest market

Key Takeaway
For salam goods without transport cost, the Hanafi school's preferred view allows delivery anywhere; specifying a place is not required by consensus.

Necessity of Possessing Capital Before Separation in Salam
Ruling that capital must be possessed before separation in salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition regarding possession of capital in salam and analyze how khiyar al-shart, khiyar al-ru'ya, and khiyar al-'ayb affect its validity.

Core Idea
Salam requires immediate possession of capital to avoid the prohibited debt-for-debt exchange.

Salam (advance payment sale) is a unique contract that allows the buyer to pay upfront for future delivery. However, its validity hinges on a crucial condition: the buyer must take possession of the capital before the contract session ends. This lesson unpacks the reasoning, the prophetic prohibition that underlies it, and how various optional conditions (khiyar) interact with this requirement. Understanding this will help you avoid common pitfalls in structuring salam contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling
The passage opens by stating that salam is not valid until the capital is taken possession of before the parties separate. This is the core ruling.
The ruling applies to all types of capital, whether currency or commodity.
2
Examine the dalil (proof)
The hadith prohibiting 'al-kali' bi al-kali'' (debt-for-debt exchange) is cited. If possession is delayed, the transaction becomes a forbidden exchange of one debt for another.
The hadith is ahad (single-narrator) but its meaning is clear (qat'i al-dalala) according to the Hanafi school.
3
Distinguish between currency and commodity capital
The text explains two scenarios: if capital is currency, lack of possession makes it a debt-for-debt exchange. If capital is a commodity, possession is necessary to fulfill the immediate nature of salam (taking prompt delivery of one side).
In both cases, the rationale is to ensure that one countervalue is hand-to-hand.
4
Apply the ruling to khiyar options
The passage then tests various options: khiyar al-shart invalidates salam because it prevents complete possession; khiyar al-ru'ya is not beneficial (since the capital is already seen or not need to inspect); khiyar al-'ayb is allowed because it does not hinder possession.
Khiyar al-shart can be dropped before separation to validate the contract.
5
Evaluate the intra-madhhab dispute with Zufar
Zufar argued that if khiyar al-shart is present, the contract is void ab initio and cannot be saved by later dropping the option. The Hanafi majority (including Abu Hanifa) hold that dropping it before separation renders the contract valid.
The mufta bihi (operative for fatwa) is the majority view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا يصح السلم حتى يقبض رأس المال قبل ان يفارقه فيه اما اذا كان من النقود فلانه افتراق عن دين بدين وقد نهى النبي عليه السلام عن الكاليء بالكالي وان كان عينا فلان السلم اخذ عاجل بأجل اذ الاسلام والاسلاف ينبيان عن التعجيل فلابد من قبض احد العوضين ليتحقق معنى الاسم ولانه لابد من تسليم رأس المال ليتقلب المسلم اليه فيه فيقدر على التسليم ولهذا قلنا لا يصح السلم اذا كان فيه خيار الشرط لهما او لاحدهما لانه يمنع تمام القبض لكونه مانعا من الانعقاد فى حق الحكم وكذا لا يثبت فيه خيار الرؤية لانه غير مفيد بخلاف خيار العيب لانه لا يمنع تمام القبض ولو أسقط خيار الشرط قبل الافتراق ورأس المال قائم جاز خلافا لزفر وقد مر نظيره
He said: Salam is not valid until the capital is taken possession of before he separates from him. For if it is from currencies, it is because it is a separation from a debt for a debt, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited al-kali' bi al-kali'. If it is a commodity, it is because salam is taking a prompt for a deferred, since 'islam' and 'aslaf' indicate promptness. So it is necessary to take possession of one of the two countervalues to actualize the meaning of the term. And it is necessary to deliver the capital so that the muslam ilayhi can transact with it and be able to deliver. For this reason, we say salam is not valid if it contains a khiyar al-shart for both or one of them, because it prevents complete possession, as it prevents perfection of the contract with respect to the ruling. Likewise, khiyar al-ru'ya is not established in it, because it is not beneficial, unlike khiyar al-'ayb, because it does not prevent complete possession. And if the khiyar al-shart is waived before separation while the capital remains, it is permissible, contrary to Zufar, and its like has already been mentioned.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage from Hidayah establishes a key condition for salam validity: the buyer must take possession of the capital before the contract session ends. The proof comes from the hadith prohibiting 'kali' bi kali' (selling a deferred debt for another deferred debt). Possession distinguishes salam from a forbidden debt exchange. Goods (capital) given are either currency or commodity. The passage also discusses khiyar options: khiyar al-shart invalidates salam because it prevents full possession; khiyar al-ru'ya is not applicable; khiyar al-'ayb is allowed as it does not prevent possession. If khiyar al-shart is dropped before separation, the contract becomes valid. Zufar dissented, but the school follows the majority.

Key Terms
رأس المال (ra's al-mal): The capital/prepayment given by the buyer in a salam contract.
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): An option to cancel the contract within a stipulated period.
خيار الرؤية (khiyar al-ru'ya): Option to inspect the object before acceptance.
خيار العيب (khiyar al-'ayb): Option to return a defective item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is possession of capital required before separation in a salam contract?
A) To avoid the prohibition of riba
B) To avoid the prohibition of kali' bi kali'
C) To ensure the seller has funds
D) To make the contract binding

Key Takeaway
Salam is valid only when the buyer takes possession of the capital before the session ends, and khiyar al-shart invalidates it unless waived before separation.

Specifying Delivery Place for Non-Transportable Muslam Fīh
Ruling with proof: two narrations on specifying delivery place for non-transportable goods.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi narrations on specifying delivery place for non-transportable muslam fīh, identify the relied-upon position, and apply it to situations where route risk exists.

Core Idea
Specifying a delivery place is valid when it eliminates route risk, even for non-transportable goods.

In a salam contract, the buyer pays upfront and the seller delivers later. When the goods are easy to transport, is there any benefit in specifying a delivery location? The Hanafi school has two views. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each narration and shows how the principle of benefit (maslahah) determines the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The act is specifying a delivery place for muslam fīh that is non-transportable (no carrying cost). The key question: does the specification become binding?
Binding means the seller must deliver at that specific place.
2
Trace the Two Narrations
First narration: specification is not binding because no benefit. Second narration: specification is binding because it can eliminate route risk. Identify the proof (dalīl) for each.
The proofs are rational: benefit analysis.
3
Analyze the Tarjīḥ
The author declares the second narration as ‘more correct’. Understand why: when specification removes risk for the buyer (rabb al-salam), it serves a legitimate purpose.
Tarjīḥ is based on the presence of benefit (maslahah).
4
Extend to Transportable Goods
For transportable goods, specifying a city suffices unless price differences exist due to distance. Apply the principle to determine when neighborhood details are needed.
The rule for transportable goods is separate but connected to the same principle of avoiding dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف البدایہ جلد - نم
باب السلم
کیلئے مکان عقد متعین نہ ہو گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ قرماتے ہیں کہ جس مسلم فیہ کو منتقل کرنے میں بار برداری اور خرچہ نہ پڑتا ہو اس کو سپر د کر نے کیلئے رب السلام اور مسلم الیہ نے اگر باہمی اتفاق سے کوئی مکان متعین کر لیا تو کیا وہ مکان متعین ہو جائے گا یا متعین نہیں ہو گا ؟ اس بارے میں دو روایتیں ہیں۔ ایک روایت تو یہ ہے کہ متعین نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ جب مسلم فیہ ایسی چیز ہے جس کو منتقل کرنے میں خرچہ نہ پڑتا ہو تو اس کو سپرد کرنے کیلئے کسی جگہ کے متعین کرنے کا کوئی فائدہ نہ ہوگا۔ اور جب جگہ متعین کرنے کا کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہے تو کوئی جگہ متعین کرنے سے متعین بھی نہ ہوگی۔ دوسری روایت یہ ہے کہ رب السلام اور مسلم الیہ کے متعین کرنے سے مسلم فیہ سپر د کر نے کا مکان متعین ہو جاتا ہے اور یہی زیادہ صحیح روایت ہے۔ کیونکہ متعین کرنے کا فائدہ رب السلام کے حق میں ظاہر ہوتا ہے، بایں طور کہ رب السلام سے راستہ کا خطرہ ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ مثلاً ایک جگہ ایسی ہے جہاں سے منتقل کرنے میں رہزنوں اور لٹیروں کا خطرہ ہے اور دوسری جگہ میں یہ خطرہ موجود نہیں ہے تو ایسی صورت میں سپرد کرنے کی جگہ معین کرنے سے راستہ کا خطرہ چونکہ مل جاتا ہے اس لئے اس قائدہ کے پیش نظر مسلم فیہ سپر د کرنے کی جگہ متعین کرنے سے متعین ہو جائے گی۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ جس مسلم فیہ کو منتقل کرنے میں خرچہ پڑتا ہو اس کو سپرد کرنے کے لئے اگر کوئی شہر متعین کر دیا گیا ہومثلا رب السلام نے مسلم فیہ سپر د کرنے کیلے شہر سہارنپور متعین کیا تو یہ کافی ہے اس کے محلہ کو متعین کرنا شرط نہیں ہے، کیونکہ شہر کے اطراف و جوانب اگر چہ متبائن ہیں لیکن ان میں چونکہ قیمتوں کا اختلاف نہیں ہوتا اس لئے اس کے تمام محلے اور اطراف ایک ہی جگہ کے مانند ہیں۔ جس محلہ اور کنارہ میں سپرد کرے گا جائز ہوگا۔ محیط میں ہے کہ شہر کے تمام اطراف و جوانب ایک جگہ کے مانند اس وقت ہیں جب کہ شہر بڑا نہ ہو نانچہ اگر اس کے دو کناروں کے درمیان ایک فرسخ کا فاصلہ ہو تو اس کے محلہ اور کنارے کا بیان کرنا بھی ضروری ہے۔ اگر بیان نہ کیا تو عقد سلم جائز نہ ہوگا، کیونکہ اس میں ایسی جہالت ہے جو مفضی الی المنازعہ ہے۔ لیکن ظاہر یہ ہے کہ ہمارے ملکوں میں باوجود اس قدر فرق کے بھی قیمت میں ایسا تفاوت نہیں ہوتا جو معتبر ہو، اس لئے شہر خواہ کتنا ہی بڑا ہو اس کے اطراف و جوانب ایک موضع کے مانند ہوں گے، صرف شہر کا بیان کر دینا کافی ہے اس کے محلہ اور کنارہ کا بیان کرنا ضروری نہیں ہے۔
Chapter of Salam. For [the muslam fīh] whose transfer involves no carrying cost or expense, if the rabb al-salam and the muslim ilayh mutually agree to specify a location for delivery, will that location become specified or not? There are two narrations. One narration: it does not become specified, because when the muslam fīh is something whose transfer involves no expense, there is no benefit in specifying a place for delivery. And when there is no benefit, specifying a place does not make it binding. The second narration: the place becomes specified by their agreement, and this is the more correct narration, because the benefit of specification becomes apparent for the rabb al-salam, namely that the risk of the route is removed from him. For example, there is one place where transferring involves risk of highway robbers, and another where this risk is absent. In such a case, specifying the delivery place removes the route risk, so according to this principle, the delivery place becomes specified. The author of al-Hidayah said: For a muslam fīh whose transfer involves expense, if a city is specified for delivery—e.g., the rabb al-salam specifies the city of Saharanpur—this suffices; specifying the neighborhood is not required, because although the sides and surrounds of a city are distinct, prices do not differ among them, so all its neighborhoods and sides are like one place; delivering in any neighborhood or side is permissible. In al-Muhit: All sides and surrounds of a city are like one place only if the city is not large. But if there is a distance of one farsakh between its two ends, then specifying the neighborhood and side becomes necessary; if not specified, the salam contract is invalid, due to ignorance that leads to dispute. However, it seems that in our countries, despite such distance, price difference is not significant, so even if the city is large, its sides and surrounds are like one locality; merely mentioning the city suffices, and specifying its neighborhood and side is not necessary.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses a ruling about whether the parties to a salam contract can validly specify a delivery location for goods that are easy to transport (no cost). The author presents two narrations: one says it does not become specified because there is no benefit; the other, deemed more correct, says it does become specified because specifying can eliminate route risks (e.g., robbers). The text then applies the ruling to transportable goods: if a city is specified, that is sufficient; neighborhood details are only required if price varies significantly due to distance (e.g., more than a farsakh). In regions where prices are uniform, mere mention of the city suffices.

Key Terms
مسلم فیہ (muslam fīh): The subject matter of a salam contract (goods to be delivered in the future).
رب السلام (rabb al-salam): The buyer in a salam contract who pays the capital upfront.
مسلم الیہ (muslim ilayh): The seller in a salam contract who receives the capital and owes the future delivery.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the more correct narration in Ashraf al-Hidayah, when does a specified delivery place become binding for non-transportable muslam fīh?
A) Only if the goods are transportable.
B) When there is a benefit such as removing route risk.
C) Only if the parties agree in writing.
D) Never, because no benefit exists.

Key Takeaway
For non-transportable muslam fīh, specifying a delivery place becomes binding when it serves a legitimate benefit (like route safety), based on the principle of istihsan.

Requirement of Possession of Capital Before Separation in Salam
Ruling with proof on qabd in salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qabd in salam, identify the proofs from hadith and language, and explain the effect of khiyar al-shart on validity.

Core Idea
Salam requires immediate possession of capital; delay turns it into the prohibited sale of debt for debt.

Salam is a sale where capital is paid now for future delivery of goods. The Hanafi school insists that the capital must be taken into possession before the parties leave the contract session. Failure to do so transforms the transaction into a forbidden exchange of one debt for another. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proofs, and the implications of option clauses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
State clearly: salam is not valid unless the capital (ra's al-māl) is possessed (qabd) before the seller separates from the buyer in the same session.
This is the matn's key imperative.
2
Analyze the two-fold proof
When the capital is currency (naqd), the contract without qabd becomes a sale of debt for debt (kāli' bi-kāli'), prohibited by hadith. When it is a specific item (ʿayn), the linguistic meaning of 'salam' (immediacy) requires possession of one countervalue.
The proof combines naqli (hadith) and aqli (linguistic analysis).
3
Examine the effect of khiyar al-shart
Khiyar al-shart (stipulated option) prevents complete possession, so it invalidates salam unless the option is dropped before separation. Contrast with khiyar al-ʿayb (option of defect) which does not prevent possession.
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Zufar holds that dropping later does not validate; al-Hidayah rejects this.
4
Compare with other schools
Shafiʿi and Ahmad concur on the prohibition of debt-for-debt, but Malik allows mere delay without a fixed term to be permissible. Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).
5
Synthesize the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon Hanafi position: qabd before separation is mandatory; khiyar al-shart invalidates unless explicitly waived before parting. The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.
Authority weight: zahir_riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا يصح السلم حتى يقبض رأس المال قبل ان يفارقه فيه اما اذا كان من النقود فلانه افتراق عن دين بدین وقد نهى النبي عليه السلام عن الكاليء بالكالي وان كان عينا فلان السلم اخذ عاجل بأجل اذ الاسلام والاسلاف ينبيان عن التعجيل فلابد من قبض احد العوضين ليتحقق معنى الاسم ولانه لابد من تسليم رأس المال ليتقلب المسلم اليه فيه فيقدر على التسليم ولهذا قلنا لا يصح السلم اذا كان فيه خيار الشرط لهما او لاحدهما لانه يمنع تمام القبض لكونه مانعا من الانعقاد فى حق الحكم وكذا لا يثبت فيه خيار الرؤية لانه غير مفيد بخلاف خيار العيب لانه لا يمنع تمام القبض ولو أسقط خيار الشرط قبل الافتراق ورأس المال قائم جاز خلافا لزفر وقد مر نظيره

ترجمہ اور سلم صحیح نہیں ہے یہاں تک کہ اسی مجلس میں جدا ہونے سے پہلے راس المال پر قبضہ کرلے۔ بہر حال جب رأس المال نفود کی جنس سے ہو تو اس لئے کہ یہ دین بدین سے جدا ہونا ہے حالانکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے کالی بکائی سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ اور اگر راس المال از قبیلہ اعیان ہو تو اس لئے کہ مسلم متجل کو مؤجل کے عوض لینا ہے۔ کیونکہ سلم اور سلف کرنا فی الحال کی خبر دیتے ہیں۔ لہذا احد العوضین پر قبضہ کرنا ضروری ہے تا کہ مسلم الیہ اس میں تصرف کر کے مسلم فیہ سپرد کرنے پر قادر ہو سکے۔ اور اسی وجہ سے ہم نے کہا کہ عقد سلم صحیح نہیں ہوتا جب کہ اس میں رب السلم اور مسلم الیہ دونوں کیلئے یا ایک کیلئے خیار شرط ہو کیونکہ خیار شرط قبضہ پورا ہونے سے مانع ہے۔ اس لئے کہ خیار شرط حکم کے انعقاد سے مانع ہے اور اسی طرح عقد سلم میں خیار رویت ثابت نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ یہ غیر مفید ہے، بر خلاف خیار عیب کے کہ وہ قبضہ پورا ہونے سے مانع ہے اور اگر جدا ہونے سے پہلے خیار شرط کو ساقط کر دیا اور راس المال موجود ہے تو عقد جائز ہو جائیگا۔امام زفر کا اختلاف ، اور اسکی نظیر پہلے گزر چکی ہے۔

تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ عقد سلم اس وقت صحیح ہو گا جب کہ رب السلم اور مسلم الیہ دونوں کے جدا ہونے سے پہلے پہلے مسلم الیہ رأس المال پر قبضہ کر لے۔ حاصل یہ کہ مجلس عقد میں عاقدین کے جدا ہونے سے پہلے مسلم الیہ کا راس المال پر قبضہ کرنا ضروری ہے کیونکہ رأس المال دو حال سے خالی نہیں ، یا تو وہ از قبیلۂ نقود یعنی در اہم ودنا نیر کی جنس سے ہوگا یا از قبیلۂ اعیان یعنی جانور اور کپڑے کی جنس سے ہوگا ۔ اگر اول ہے تو اس صورت میں دین بدین کی بیچ یعنی ادھار کی بیج ادھار کے عوض ہو جائے گی، کیونکہ راس المال پر جب مجلس عقد میں قبضہ نہیں کیا گیا تو راس المال بھی از قبیلۂ نقود ہونے کی وجہ سے دین غیر معین ہو گیا اور مسلم یہ بھی ادھار ، یعنی مسلم الیہ کے ذمہ دین ہوتی ہے پس یہ دین کی بیع دین کے عوض یعنی ادھار کی بیع ادھار کے عوض ہو گئی ، حالانکہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے کالی با كائی یعنی ادھار کے عوض ادھار کی بیع سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ یہی قول امام شافعی اور امام احمد کا ہے۔ پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ اگر رأس المال نقدی ہو تو اس پرمجلس عقد میں قبضہ کرنا ضروری ہے۔ اور امام مالک نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر راس المال نقود کے قبیلہ سے ہو اور اس پر مجلس عقد میں قبضہ نہیں کیا گیا بلکہ تاخیر ہو گئی تو یہ جائز ہے بشرطیکہ اجل اور میعاد کی شرط نہ لگائی ہو کیونکہ اجل اور میعاد کی شرط لگائے بغیر محض تاخیر قبضہ سے رأس المال عرفاً دین نہیں ہوتا اور جب محض تاخیر سے دین نہیں ہوتا تو یہ دین بدین کی بیع بھی نہ ہوگی۔ اور اگر ثانی ہو یعنی رأس المال معین چیز ہو تو مجلس عقد میں قبضہ کرنا اس لئے ضروری ہے کہ مسلم کہتے ہیں منجل کو مؤجل کے عوض لینا۔ یعنی سلم میں رأس المال منتجبل اور فوری ہوتا ہے اور مسلم فیہ مؤجل اور ادھار ہوتی ہے۔ اور اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ لفظ سلم اور سلف، اسلام اور اسلاف میں اغیہ تجھیل کے معنی پائے جاتے ہیں۔ اور چونکہ احکام شرعیہ میں اغوی معنی کی رعایت کی جاتی ہے۔ اس لئے لفظ مسلم اور اسلام کے لغوی معنی تحقیق کرنے کیلئے احد العوضین پر قبضہ کرنا ضروری ہے اور چونکہ یہ امر مسلم ہے کہ مسلم فیہ میعادی اور ادھار ہوتی ہے اس لئے دوسرے عوض یعنی راس المال پرمجلس عقد میں قبضہ کرنا ضروری ہوگا۔

دوسری دلیل سے پہلے دو باتیں ذہن نشین کر لیجئے، ایک تو یہ کہ بیع سلم مسلم الیہ کے افلاس کی وجہ سے مشروع کی گئی ہے اور دوسری یہ ، کہ جواز سلم کیلئے مسلم الیہ کا مسلم فیہ سپرد کرنے پر قادر ہونا ضروری ہے۔ پس ان دونوں باتوں سے ظاہر ہو گیا کہ مسلم الیہ کا مجلس عقد میں راس المال پر قبضہ کرنا ضروری ہے تا کہ مسلم الیہ ، راس المال میں تصرف کر کے مسلم فیہ سپرد کرنے پر قادر ہو جائے ۔ چونکہ مجلس عقد میں رأس المال پر قبضہ کرنا ضروری ہے اس لئے ہم کہتے ہیں کہ اگر عقد سلم میں رب السلم اور مسلم الیہ دونوں کے لئے یا کسی ایک کے لئے خیار ط قبضہ پورا ہونے سے اس لئے مانع ہے کہ خیار شرط کی وجہ سے عقد کا جو حکم ہے (ملک ) وہ ثابت نہیں ہوتا حتی کہ بیع میں اگر دونوں کا خیار ہو تو مشتری کی ملکیت مبیع میں اور بائع کی ملکیت شمن میں ثابت نہ ہوگی ۔ پس جب خیار شرط کے ہوتے ہوئے مسلم الیہ، رأس المال کا
He said: Salam is not valid until the capital is possessed before he separates from him. Whether the capital is coins, then because it is a separation from a debt for a debt, and the Prophet, peace be upon him, prohibited the sale of debt for debt. And if it is a specific item, then because salam is taking a present thing for a future thing, since 'islam' and 'islaaf' indicate immediacy. So possession of one of the two countervalues is necessary to realize the meaning of the name, and because delivery of the capital is necessary so that the muslim ilayh may transact with it and thereby be able to deliver [the muslam fīh]. For this reason we say: salam is not valid if there is a condition of option (khiyar al-shart) for both or one of them, for it prevents complete possession, as it prevents the contract from being concluded in terms of legal effect. Likewise, khiyar al-ru'ya (option of seeing) is not established in it because it is useless, unlike khiyar al-'ayb (option of defect) because it does not prevent complete possession. If he drops the khiyar al-shart before separation while the capital exists, it becomes valid, contrary to Zufar. Its like has passed before. [Translation follows in Urdu explaining the same points.] The detailed explanation: The ruling is that salam is valid only if the muslim ilayh possesses the capital before the parties separate in the session. Because the capital is either from the category of coins or from the category of specific goods. If the former, without possession it becomes a sale of debt for debt, which is prohibited by hadith. This is the view of al-Shafi'i and Ahmad. Imam Malik allows delay without stipulation of a term. If the latter, possession is necessary to realize the meaning of salam (immediate capital for deferred delivery). A second proof: salam is legislated due to the need of the seller, and validity requires his ability to deliver; possession of capital enables him to produce the muslam fīh. Hence, khiyar al-shart prevents complete possession and invalidates salam unless dropped before separation.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage presents the matn from al-Hidayah on a core ruling of salam: the capital (ra's al-māl) must be taken into possession (qabd) before the parties leave the contract session. The author explains the two cases: if the capital is currency (naqd), failure to take possession transforms the transaction into a forbidden sale of debt for debt (kāli' bi-kāli'). If the capital is a specific item (ayn), immediate possession is needed because salam essentially exchanges a present thing for a future thing. The commentary then addresses khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation): its presence prevents complete possession, so it invalidates salam; but if it is dropped before separation, the contract becomes valid, contrary to Imam Zufar's view. The text also compares khiyar al-ru'ya (void in salam as useless) and khiyar al-'ayb (valid as it doesn't prevent possession). Finally, it gives a second rational proof: salam is legislated for the seller's need, and possession of capital enables him to produce the goods, so possession is essential.

Key Terms
قبض (qabd): Physical or constructive possession of the capital in the contract session before separation.
خیار شرط (khiyar al-shart): An option stipulated in the contract allowing one or both parties to cancel within a specified period.
کالیء بکالیء (kāli' bi-kāli'): Sale of one deferred debt for another deferred debt, which is prohibited by hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does khiyar al-shart invalidate a salam contract according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because it prevents immediate delivery of the muslam fīh.
B) Because it prevents complete possession of the capital (ra's al-māl).
C) Because it is prohibited in all sales.
D) Because it creates uncertainty about the price.

Key Takeaway
Salam requires immediate possession of the capital before separation; failure makes it a prohibited debt-for-debt sale, and khiyar al-shart invalidates unless dropped while the capital is present.
