باطل ہو جائیگی ، کیونکہ اس صورت میں ان دونوں نے جان بوجھ کر بلاعین بیع منعقد کی ہے اور بلاعین بیع ابتداء ہی باطل ہوتی ہے اور جب بیع ابتداء باطل ہوگئی تو دین نہ ہونے پر اتفاق کر لینے کے بعد بھی درست نہ ہوگی ۔
بہر حال جب نقود یعنی دراہم ودنانیر متعین کرنے کے باوجود متعین نہیں ہوتے تو ان کو مطلق ذکر کرنا اور دین اور عین کے ساتھ مقید کرنا دونوں برابر ہیں۔ اور پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ راس المال یعنی دو سو درہم مطلق رکھنے کی صورت میں بیع سلم ابتداء صحیح ہو کر منعقد ہوتی ہے تو اسی طرح دین کے ساتھ مقید کرنے کی صورت میں بھی بیع سلم ابتداءً صحیح ہو جائے گی ۔ صرف اتنا لازم ہے کہ رب السلام اور مسلم الیہ کی جدائی سے پہلے مسلم الیہ دو سو درہم پر قبضہ کرلے تا کہ بیع الکالی بالکالی لازم نہ آئے لیکن جب رب السلم نے ایک سو درہم نقد ادا کئے اور ایک
سو درہم نہیں دیئے تو ایک سو درہم ادھار میں
قبضہ کی شرط فوت ہونے کی وجہ سے ان کا حصہ مسلم باطل ہو جائے گا، اور ایک سو درہم نقد کا حصہ سلم درست رہے گا اور چونکہ یہ فساد طاری ہے اس لئے پورا عقد سلم باطل نہ ہوگا۔
The argument is that in the council of contract, possession of the capital by the Muslim ilayhi is necessary, whereas for the portion that is a debt (i.e., one hundred dirhams), the Muslim ilayhi's possession was not found in the council, so the salam sale for the debt portion is not valid. As for the one hundred dirhams that were paid in the council, since all conditions of salam are present in them, the salam sale for their portion becomes valid. 'And invalidity does not spread' etc. is the response to Imam Zufar's statement. Imam Zufar said that when the salam sale for the debt portion (one hundred dirhams) is invalid, then the salam sale for the cash portion also becomes invalid, because due to the unity of the contract, invalidity spreads to all. But our response to this is that the invalidity in the salam sale of the debt portion is temporary (tari), and temporary invalidity is limited to the extent of the corrupting factor, and the corrupting factor (possession of the capital in the council) was found only in the debt portion, not in the cash portion, so only the salam sale of the debt portion is invalid, and the invalidity does not extend to the cash portion. As for why the invalidity of the debt portion's salam is temporary, the answer is that initially the salam contract for one measure of wheat for two hundred dirhams was concluded validly, because if the salam contract is attributed absolutely to two hundred dirhams, e.g., one said 'I made a salam contract with you for one measure of wheat for two hundred dirhams' then he paid one hundred dirhams cash and one hundred dirhams that were a debt owed to him by the other, then in this case the initial validity of the salam contract is clear. And if the salam contract is attributed to both debt and specifically cash, e.g., one said 'I made a salam contract with you for one measure of wheat for the one hundred dirhams that are owed to me by you and these one hundred dirhams that are present here,' then also the salam contract is initially valid. For this reason, if the rabb as-salam pays the entire capital (debt and cash) before separation from the council, the entire salam contract becomes valid. But if they separate from the council without possession of the capital, then the salam sale becomes invalid due to the same evidence that passed earlier, i.e., in the case of not paying the capital in the council, bay' al-kali' bi al-kali' occurs, whereas the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade this. As for how the salam sale becomes initially valid in the case of one hundred dirhams debt and one hundred dirhams cash, the author of al-Hidayah says in response: even though one designates the debt in the sale, it is not actually designated. That is, if within the sale one designates the debt owed by the seller as a specific object, it does not become designated. Rather, it is a general rule that in contracts, currencies are not designated when they are specific and pointed to. Similarly, when they are debts, they are not designated by designation. So if someone bought a slave from the seller in exchange for a debt that the seller owed him, then both agreed that the buyer does not owe the seller anything, the sale does not become invalid. This shows that a sale in exchange for a debt is initially valid, but if they agree that there is no debt, the sale does not become valid. However, if both the seller and buyer knew fully that there was no debt, but the buyer bought the slave in exchange for a debt, then this sale is invalid, because in this case they knowingly concluded a sale without consideration (bila 'ayn), and a sale without consideration is initially invalid, and when it is initially invalid, it does not become valid after agreeing that there is no debt. In any case, when currencies (dirhams and dinars) are not designated even if designated, mentioning them absolutely and restricting them with debt or cash is equal. And it has passed earlier that in the case of keeping the capital (two hundred dirhams) absolute, the salam contract is initially valid and concluded, so similarly in the case of restricting it with debt, the salam contract will also be initially valid. Only this is necessary: that before the separation of rabb as-salam and Muslim ilayhi, the Muslim ilayhi takes possession of the two hundred dirhams so that bay' al-kali' bi al-kali' does not occur. But when the rabb as-salam paid one hundred dirhams cash and did not give one hundred dirhams, then due to the loss of the condition of possession for the one hundred dirhams debt, their portion of the salam becomes invalid, and the portion of the one hundred dirhams cash remains valid. And since this invalidity is temporary, the entire salam contract does not become invalid.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute responding to Imam Zufar's objection that invalidity spreads in a single contract. The author defends the Hanafi position that when the capital in a salam contract is partly debt and partly cash, the invalidity is temporary (tari) and only affects the portion where the condition (possession in the council) is missing. The text explains the scenario: a person contracts salam for two hundred dirhams, paying one hundred dirhams cash and intending one hundred dirhams already owed by the Muslim ilayhi as debt. Since the debt portion was not possessed in the council, that part of the salam is invalid, but the cash portion is valid. This contradicts Imam Zufar's view that the entire contract fails. The author provides a detailed proof: currencies (gold and silver) are not effectively designated in contracts, even if explicitly named, because they are fungible and meant for value, not specific objects. Therefore, treating the debt as part of the capital does not make the contract initially invalid. The key is that possession must occur before separation from the council, and if only partial possession happens, the unpossessed portion is invalid, but this invalidity does not spread. The text also gives an analogy: buying a slave for a debt, then agreeing the debt does not exist – the sale remains valid. This illustrates that the debt is not a specified object.

Key Terms
فساد طاری (fasād tārī): Temporary invalidity that arises after the contract is initially valid, affecting only a portion due to a specific corrupting factor.
بیع الکالی بالکالی (bay' al-kālī bi al-kālī): Sale of debt for debt, where the consideration on both sides is deferred or not possessed in the council.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a salam contract where the capital is two hundred dirhams, one hundred dirhams cash paid in the council and one hundred dirhams already owed by the Muslim ilayhi, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The entire contract is invalid because the debt portion was not possessed in the council.
B) The contract is valid for the cash portion and invalid for the debt portion; the invalidity does not spread.
C) The contract is valid only if the debt portion is paid before separation from the council.
D) The contract is entirely valid because the debt is considered as if possessed.

Key Takeaway
In a salam contract, invalidity due to missing possession of part of the capital is temporary and limited to that specific portion; the remaining valid portion stands, and the buyer receives the commodity proportionally.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Prohibition of Disposal Before Possession in Salam
Ruling with proof on pre-possession disposal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that both the capital (ra's al-mal) and the commodity (muslam fīhi) in a salam contract cannot be disposed of before possession, and explain the qiyas proof for each.

Core Idea
Disposal before possession in salam is prohibited: capital is a right of the contract, commodity is a sold item.

In salam transactions, possession plays a crucial role. The Hanafi school strictly prohibits any disposal of the capital or the commodity before taking physical possession. This lesson unpacks the ruling from al-Hidayah, examining the rational proofs based on analogy (qiyas) and the consequences of violating this rule, including for partnerships and delegations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its two components
Locate the core statement: disposal before possession is not permissible for the capital (ra's al-mal) and the commodity (muslam fīhi). Note that the ruling applies to both parties—the Muslim ilayhi (seller) for the capital and the rabb as-salam (buyer) for the commodity.
The text uses 'ja'iz nahi' which indicates prohibition (haram) in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Analyze the proof for the capital (ra's al-mal)
The proof is that possession is a right established by the contract (and a condition for validity). Disposing of the capital before possession forfeits this right, which is not allowed. This is a rational argument (dalil aqli) based on the contract's requirements.
The capital must be taken possession of in the council of contract for the salam to be valid.
3
Analyze the proof for the commodity (muslam fīhi)
The commodity is analogized (qiyas) to a sold item (mabī'), and the general rule in Islamic commercial law is that one cannot sell or dispose of an item before taking possession. The effective cause ('illa) is that the risk of loss has not yet transferred to the buyer.
This is based on the hadith 'do not sell what you do not possess' and the principle of gharar (uncertainty).
4
Extend the ruling to partnership and delegation
The text states that shirkah (partnership) and tawliya (delegation) in the muslam fīhi before possession are also prohibited because they constitute disposal. Understand the specific forms as described: shirkah involves sharing the capital for a share in the commodity; tawliya involves giving the full capital for the entire commodity.
This shows that any transfer of interest in the commodity before possession is prohibited.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رأس المال اور مسلم فیہ میں قبل القبض تصرف جائز نہیں ہے
قال ولا يجوز التصرف في رأس مال السلم والمسلم فيه قبل القبض أما الأول فلما فيه من تفويت القبض المستحق بالعقد واما الثاني فلان المسلم فيه مبيع والتصرف فى المبيع قبل القبض لا يجوز ترجمہ اور قبضہ سے پہلے سلم کے راس المال اور مسلم فیہ میں تصرف کرنا جائز نہیں ہے بہر حال اول تو اس لئے کہ اس میں اس قبضہ کا فوت کرنا ( لازم آتا ہے ) جو قبضہ عقد کی وجہ سے واجب ہوا ہے اور ثانی تو اس لئے کہ مسلم فیہ میچ ہوتی ہے اور مبیع کے اندر قبضہ سے پہلے تصرف کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔
تشریحی صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ بیع سلم کے راس المال میں قبضہ کرنے سے
پہلے مسلم الیہ کے لئے تصرف کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح مسلم فیہ میں قبضہ سے پہلے رب السلام کے لئے تصرف کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ مثلاً خالد نے حامد سے دو سو درہم پر دو من گندم کی بیع سلم ٹھہرائی اور ابن عقد میں خالد رب السلام اور حامد مسلم الیہ ہے، پھر حامد ( مسلم الیہ) نے ان دوسو درہم کے عوض شاہد سے گھوڑا خریدا حالانکہ ابھی تک حامد نے ان دوسو دراہم پر قبضہ نہیں کیا ہے تو حامد یعنی مسلم الیہ کا یہ تصرف صحیح نہ ہو گا۔ اسی طرح اگر خالد یعنی رب السلم نے دو من گندم یعنی مسلم فیہ پر قبضہ کئے بغیر ان کو فروخت کر دیا تو بھی جائز نہیں ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ قبضہ سے پہلے نہ راس المال میں تصرف کرنا جائز ہے اور نہ مسلم فیہ میں تصرف جائز ہے۔ اول کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مجلس میں راس المال پر قبضہ کرنا بیع سلم صحیح ہونے کی شرط اور اللہ کا حق ہے اور تصرف کرنا اس کو باطل کر دیتا ہے اس لئے قبضہ سے پہلے راس المال میں تصرف کرنے کو جائز کہا گیا ہے۔ ثانی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مسلم فیہ مبیع ہوتی ہے اور قبضہ سے پہلے میچ میں تصرف کرنا نا جائز ہے اس لئے قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے مسلم الیہ کیلئے مسلم فیہ میں تصرف کرنا نا جائز ہوگا۔
مسلم فیہ میں قبل القبض شرکت اور تولیہ جائز نہیں ہے
ولا يجوز الشركة والتولية فى المسلم فيه لانه تصرف فيه ترجمہ اور مسلم فیہ میں شرکت اور تولیہ جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ مسلم فیہ میں قبضہ سے پہلے ) تصرف ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ قبضہ سے پہلے مسلم فیہ میں نہ شرکت جائز ہے اور نہ تولیہ جائز ہے ۔ شرکت کی صورت یہ ہے کہ رب السلام نے کسی سے کہا کہ تو مجھے میرا نصف رأس المال دے دے تا کہ تو مسلم فیہ میں میرا برابر کا شریک ہو جائے ۔اور تولیہ کی صورت یہ ہے کہ رب السلام نے کسی دوسرے سے کہا کہ تو اگر مجھے میرا پورا رأس المال دیدے تو پوری مسلم فیہ تیرے واسطے ہے۔ شرکت اور تولیہ کے
Disposal of the capital of salam and the commodity (muslam fīhi) before possession is not permissible. As for the first, because it involves forfeiting the possession that is established by the contract; and as for the second, because the muslam fīhi is a merchandise (mabī'), and disposal of merchandise before possession is not permissible. Translation: It is not permissible to dispose of the capital of salam and the muslam fīhi before possession. In any case, the first is because it necessitates the loss of that possession which became obligatory due to the contract, and the second is because the muslam fīhi is merchandise, and disposal of merchandise before possession is not permissible. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri said that it is not permissible for the Muslim ilayhi to dispose of the capital of the salam sale before taking possession. Similarly, it is not permissible for the rabb as-salam to dispose of the muslam fīhi before possession. For example, Khalid made a salam contract with Hamid for two hundred dirhams for two mans of wheat, and in the contract, Khalid is rabb as-salam and Hamid is Muslim ilayhi. Then Hamid (Muslim ilayhi) bought a horse from Shahid in exchange for those two hundred dirhams, even though Hamid had not yet taken possession of those two hundred dirhams. So this disposal by Hamid, i.e., the Muslim ilayhi, is not valid. Similarly, if Khalid, i.e., rabb as-salam, sold the two mans of wheat, i.e., the muslam fīhi, without taking possession of them, that is also not permissible. The summary is that before possession, neither disposal of the capital nor disposal of the muslam fīhi is permissible. The evidence for the first is that possession of the capital in the council is a condition for the validity of the salam sale and a right of Allah, and disposal nullifies it, so disposal of the capital before possession is not permissible. The evidence for the second is that the muslam fīhi is merchandise, and disposal of merchandise before possession is impermissible, so it is impermissible for the Muslim ilayhi to dispose of the muslam fīhi before possession. Partnership (shirkah) and delegation (tawliya) in the muslam fīhi before possession are not permissible. Translation: Partnership and delegation in the muslam fīhi are not permissible because it is a disposal in it (before possession). Explanation: The issue is that before possession, neither partnership nor delegation is permissible in the muslam fīhi. The form of partnership is that the rabb as-salam tells someone: 'Give me half of my capital so that you become an equal partner with me in the muslam fīhi.' The form of delegation (tawliya) is that the rabb as-salam tells another person: 'If you give me my full capital, then the entire muslam fīhi is for you.' (The text cuts off: 'Partnership and delegation...')
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage states a clear ruling from the Hanafi school: it is prohibited for the Muslim ilayhi (seller of the commodity) to dispose of the capital (the price) before taking possession of it, and prohibited for the rabb as-salam (buyer) to dispose of the commodity (the muslam fīhi) before taking possession of it. The reasoning is twofold: (1) For the capital: possession is a right established by the contract (and a condition for validity according to some), and disposing of it before possession amounts to forfeiting that right, which is not allowed. (2) For the commodity: it is considered a sold item (mabī'), and a general rule in Islamic commercial law is that one cannot sell or otherwise dispose of an item before taking possession of it (based on the hadith 'do not sell what you do not possess'). The text then provides examples to illustrate. Finally, it extends the ruling to partnership (shirkah) and delegation (tawliya) in the muslam fīhi before possession, explaining that these are forms of disposal and thus prohibited. The definitions of shirkah and tawliya in this context are given: shirkah is when the rabb as-salam offers a share in the commodity in exchange for a share of the capital; tawliya is when he sells the entire commodity to someone who pays the full capital. The passage cuts off but the ruling is complete.

Key Terms
مسلم فیہ (muslam fīhi): The commodity that is the subject of the salam contract, which the Muslim ilayhi (seller) must deliver at the future date.
تولیہ (tawliya): A form of sale where the seller (rabb as-salam) delegates the entire muslam fīhi to another person in exchange for the full capital amount, effectively transferring the contract.
شرکت (shirkah): Partnership in the muslam fīhi where the rabb as-salam offers a share of the commodity in return for a portion of the capital from a third party.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the Muslim ilayhi (seller) disposing of the capital (price) in a salam contract before taking possession?
A) It is permissible because he owns the money as soon as the contract is made.
B) It is not permissible until he takes possession.
C) It is permissible only if the rabb as-salam agrees.
D) It is permissible if he gives a guarantee.

Key Takeaway
In salam, both the capital and the commodity cannot be disposed of before possession; the commodity is analogized to a sold item, and the capital is a contractual right.

Disposition of Capital and Subject Matter Before Possession in Salam
Ruling with proof on prohibition of disposition before possession in salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the prohibition on disposing of the capital and subject matter in a salam contract before possession and explain the underlying proofs.

Core Idea
Before possession, neither capital nor subject matter of salam may be disposed; violation causes partial invalidity.

In salam contracts, the capital must be handed over immediately, and the subject matter (commodity) is delivered later. A key rule is that neither party may dispose of their respective rights before taking physical possession. This lesson examines the ruling and the reasoning behind it, based on the texts of Al-Quduri and the commentary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? Disposition (tasarruf) of the capital (ra's al-mal) by the seller (muslam ilayh) or of the subject matter (muslam fih) by the buyer (rabb al-salam) before taking possession (qabd). The ruling is that it is not permissible (la yajuz), i.e., prohibited (haram).
Disposition includes sale, gift, or any transfer of ownership.
2
Locate the dalil for each prohibition
For the capital: disposition forfeits the right of possession (qabd) that is established by the contract and considered a right of Allah. For the subject matter: it is analogized (qiyas) to a sold item (mabi'), and the general rule is that disposition in a mabi' before possession is not allowed.
The proof for the subject matter is qiyas on the general sale rule.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
In the case of capital, the legal link is that possession is a necessary condition for the validity of salam; disposing of the capital negates that condition. In the case of subject matter, the effective cause (illa) is that it is a debt to be delivered later, and treating it as mabi' preserves the prohibition of gharar.
This reasoning prevents uncertainty and protects both parties.
4
Identify the ikhtilaf
The Hanafi school strictly prohibits any disposition before possession. Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i or Maliki) may allow it under certain conditions, but the Hanafi position is that the contract requires immediate possession of the capital and no dealing with the subject matter before delivery.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different usul principles.
5
Determine the thamarah (practical consequence)
If the seller disposes of the capital before possession, the salam contract becomes partially void (the share of capital not possessed becomes invalid). If the buyer disposes of the subject matter before possession, that disposition is invalid and the buyer risks voiding the contract for that portion.
The contract remains valid for the portion where possession occurred.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب السلم
۴۸
اشرف البدایہ جلد نہم
سوڈر ہم نہیں دیئے تو ایک سو درہم ادھار میں
قبضہ کی شرط فوت ہونے کی وجہ سے ان کا حصہ مسلم باطل ہو جائے گا، اور ایک سو در ہم نقد کا حصہ سلم درست رہے گا اور چونکہ یہ فساد طاری ہے اس لئے پورا عقد سلم باطل نہ ہوگا۔
رأس المال اور مسلم فیہ میں قبل القبض تصرف جائز نہیں ہے
قال ولا يجوز التصرف في رأس مال السلم والمسلم فيه قبل القبض أما الأول فلما فيه من تفويت القبض المستحق بالعقد واما الثاني فلان المسلم فيه مبيع والتصرف فى المبيع قبل القبض لا يجوز ترجمہ اور قبضہ سے پہلے سلم کے راس المال اور مسلم فیہ میں تصرف کرنا جائز نہیں ہے بہر حال اول تو اس لئے کہ اس میں اس قبضہ کا فوت کرنا ( لازم آتا ہے ) جو قبضہ عقد کی وجہ سے واجب ہوا ہے اور ثانی تو اس لئے کہ مسلم فیہ میچ ہوتی ہے اور مبیع کے اندر قبضہ سے پہلے تصرف کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔
تشریحی صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ بیع سلم کے راس المال میں قبضہ کرنے سے
پہلے مسلم الیہ کے لئے تصرف کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح مسلم فیہ میں قبضہ سے پہلے رب السلام کے لئے تصرف کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ مثلاً خالد نے حامد سے دو سو درہم پر دو من گندم کی بیع سلم ٹھہرائی اور ابن عقد میں خالد رب السلام اور حامد مسلم الیہ ہے، پھر حامد ( مسلم الیہ) نے ان دوسو درہم کے عوض شاہد سے گھوڑ اخر یدا حالانکہ ابھی تک حامد نے ان دوسو درا ہم پر قبضہ نہیں کیا ہے تو حامد یعنی مسلم الیہ کا یہ تصرف صحیح نہ ہو گا۔ اسی طرح اگر خالد یعنی رب السلم نے دو من گندم یعنی مسلم فیہ پر قبضہ کئے بغیر ان کو فروخت کر دیا تو
بھی جائز نہیں ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ قبضہ سے پہلے نہ راس المال میں تصرف کرنا جائز ہے اور نہ مسلم فیہ میں تصرف جائز ہے۔ اول کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مجلس میں راس المال پر قبضہ کرنابیع سلم صحیح ہونے کی شرط اور اللہ کا حق ہے اور تصرف کرنا اس کو باطل کر دیتا ہے اس لئے قبضہ سے پہلے راس المال میں تصرف کرنے کو جائز کہا گیا ہے۔ ثانی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مسلم فیہ مبیع ہوتی ہے اور قبضہ سے پہلے میچ میں تصرف کرنا نا جائز ہے اس لئے قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے مسلم الیہ کیلئے مسلم فیہ میں تصرف کرنا نا جائز ہوگا۔
Chapter of Salam. 48. Ashraf al-Bidaya volume nine. If the dirhams were not given, then one hundred dirhams on credit: due to the loss of the condition of possession, their share of the subject matter becomes void, and the share of one hundred dirhams cash remains valid, and since this defect is incidental, the entire salam contract does not become void. Disposition in the capital of salam and the subject matter before possession is not permissible. He said: Disposition in the capital of salam and the subject matter before possession is not permissible. As for the first, because it involves forfeiting the possession that is due by the contract. As for the second, because the subject matter is a sold item and disposition in the sold item before possession is not permissible. Translation: And before possession, disposition in the capital of salam and the subject matter is not permissible. Anyway, the first is because it involves forfeiting the possession that became obligatory due to the contract. And the second is because the subject matter is a sold item and disposition in the sold item before possession is not permissible. Explanation: Imam Quduri said: In a salam sale, the seller (muslam ilayh) may not dispose of the capital before taking possession. Similarly, the buyer (rabb al-salam) may not dispose of the subject matter before taking possession. For example, Khalid agreed with Hamid on a salam sale of two mans of wheat for two hundred dirhams, where Khalid is the buyer and Hamid is the seller. Then Hamid (the seller) used those two hundred dirhams to buy a horse from Shahid, even though Hamid had not yet taken possession of those two hundred dirhams. Then Hamid's (the seller's) this disposition is not valid. Similarly, if Khalid (the buyer) sold the two mans of wheat (the subject matter) before taking possession, that is also not permissible. The conclusion is that before possession, neither disposition in the capital nor disposition in the subject matter is permissible. The proof of the first is that taking possession of the capital in the session is a condition for the validity of the salam sale and is a right of Allah, and disposing of it invalidates that, so disposition in the capital before possession is not considered permissible. The proof of the second is that the subject matter is a sold item and disposition in a sold item before possession is impermissible, so before possession, disposition in the subject matter by the seller is impermissible.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the chapter on Salam. It states that neither the seller (muslam ilayh) nor the buyer (rabb al-salam) may dispose of the capital or the subject matter before taking possession. The reason for the capital: possession is a right established by the contract, and disposing of it would forfeit that right. The reason for the subject matter: it is like a sold item (mabi'), and the general rule is that one cannot dispose of a sold item before taking possession. The text gives an example: if the seller uses the capital (dirhams) to buy something else before receiving them, the transaction is invalid. Similarly, if the buyer sells the subject matter (wheat) before taking delivery, it is not allowed. This prohibition is strict and any violation causes the salam contract to become partly void where possession was not given.

Key Terms
رأس المال (ra's al-mal): The capital or price paid in a salam contract; must be handed over in the session.
مسلم فيه (muslam fih): The subject matter of the salam contract; the commodity to be delivered later.
قبض (qabd): Physical possession or taking delivery; a necessary condition for the validity of salam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a salam contract, if the seller (muslam ilayh) uses the capital to buy something else before taking possession of it, what is the ruling?
A) The salam contract becomes completely void.
B) The seller's disposition is valid because the capital is his property.
C) The seller's disposition is invalid, and part of the salam contract may become void.
D) The seller must seek permission from the buyer.

Key Takeaway
Disposition of capital or subject matter before possession in salam is prohibited; any such act invalidates the contract to the extent of the undelivered portion.

Prohibition of Partnership and Tawliyah Before Possession in Salam
Subsidiary ruling derived from a general principle

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on partnership and tawliyah in salam subject matter before possession, explain the proof based on the prohibition of disposition before possession, and correctly identify the forms of each transaction.

Core Idea
Disposing of salam subject matter before possession is prohibited—whether through partnership or tawliyah.

This lesson expands the general principle that disposition of salam subject matter before possession is impermissible. It tackles two specific forms: partnership (shirkah) and tawliyah (sale at cost). Both seem like distinct contracts, but they are merely disguised disposals before delivery. The Hanafi school strictly prohibits them, as they involve transferring ownership of something not yet in your control.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Prohibited Actions
First, note the two specific transactions: partnership (shirkah) and tawliyah. Understand their forms as described in the text.
Partnership: buyer invites another to share capital and subject matter. Tawliyah: buyer transfers the entire subject matter for full capital.
2
State the Ruling
The ruling is that both are impermissible (haram), meaning the transactions are invalid (batil). This is a clear-cut prohibition, not just disliked.
3
Trace the Proof
The proof is not a direct text but a logical extension (qiyas) from the established principle that any disposition before possession is prohibited. Partnership and tawliyah both involve such disposal.
The precedent is from earlier discussions in the chapter that disposition before delivery is invalid.
4
Apply the Illa (Effective Cause)
The effective cause (illa) is the act of disposing of the subject matter before taking possession. Since partnership and tawliyah necessarily entail such disposal, they fall under the same prohibition.
5
Note the Absence of Intra-Hanafi Disagreement
The source indicates no disagreement among Abu Hanifa and his two main disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). All three hold the prohibition, making the mufta bihi unanimous.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسلم فیہ میں قبل القبض شرکت اور تولیہ جائز نہیں ہے
ولا يجوز الشركة والتولية فى المن سلم في ـه لانه تصرف فيه رف فيه
ترجمہ اور مسلم فیہ میں شرکت اور تولیہ جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ مسلم فیہ میں قبضہ سے پہلے ) تصرف ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ قبضہ سے پہلے مسلم فیہ میں نہ شرکت جائز ہے اور نہ تو یہ جائز ہے ۔ شرکت کی صورت یہ ہے کہ رب السلام نے کسی ں سے کہا کہ تو مجھے میر انصف رأس المال دے دے تا کہ تو مسلم فیہ میں میرا برابر کا شریک ہو جائے ۔اور تولیہ کی صورت یہ ہے کہ رب السلام نے کسی دوسرے سے کہا کہ تو اگر مجھے میرا پورا رأس المال دیدے تو پوری مسلم فیہ تیرے واسطے ہے۔ شرکت اور تولیہ کے

اشرف البدایہ جلد - نم
باب السلم
عدم جواز کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ شرکت کی صورت میں نصف مسلم فیہ میں اور تولیہ کی صورت میں پوری مسلم فیہ میں قبضہ سے پہلے تصرف کرنا لازم آتا ہے۔ اور سابق میں گذر چکا ہے کہ قبضہ سے پہلے مسلم فیہ میں تصرف کرنا نا جائز ہے۔ اس لئے مسلم فیہ میں نہ شرکت جائز ہے اور نہ تولیہ جائز ہے۔
Partnership and tawliyah in the subject matter [of salam] are not permissible. Because it is a disposition in it. Translation: And partnership and tawliyah in the subject matter are not permissible, because this is a disposition in the subject matter before possession. Explanation: The issue is that before possession, neither partnership nor tawliyah in the subject matter is permissible. The form of partnership: the buyer (rabb al-salam) says to someone: "Give me half of my capital so that you become an equal partner with me in the subject matter." And the form of tawliyah: the buyer says to another: "If you give me my full capital, then the entire subject matter is for you." The proof of impermissibility of partnership and tawliyah is that in the case of partnership, disposition in half of the subject matter, and in the case of tawliyah, disposition in the entire subject matter before possession necessarily occurs. And it has passed earlier that disposition in the subject matter before possession is impermissible. Therefore, neither partnership nor tawliyah in the subject matter is permissible.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage is a subsidiary ruling derived from the previous principle. It specifies two types of disposition—partnership (shirkah) and tawliyah (assignment at cost)—and declares them impermissible before possession of the subject matter. The reasoning is that both constitute a disposal of the subject matter before delivery, which is already prohibited. Partnership involves offering half the subject matter in exchange for half the capital; tawliyah involves transferring the whole subject matter in return for the full capital. Since the subject matter is not yet possessed, these transactions are invalid. This shows the strictness of the Hanafi position: even indirect disposals are not allowed.

Key Terms
شرکت (shirkah): Here, a partnership in the subject matter of salam before possession, where the buyer brings in a partner by offering half the capital in exchange for half the subject matter.
تولیہ (tawliyah): Assignment of the entire subject matter to another person in exchange for the full capital, before possession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a salam contract, the buyer (rabb al-salam) says to a third person: "Give me half the capital, and you become my equal partner in the subject matter before delivery." What is the ruling?
A) Valid because partnership is allowed in Islamic law.
B) Invalid because it involves disposition of half the subject matter before possession.
C) Valid if the third person takes possession of the subject matter immediately.
D) Invalid only if the seller objects.

Key Takeaway
Partnership and tawliyah in salam subject matter before possession are prohibited because they inherently involve a forbidden disposition before delivery.

Using Capital after Iqalah in Salam
Ruling that upon iqalah, buyer may only take back capital, not exchange it, until possession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on using capital after iqalah in salam and explain the condition of possession.

Core Idea
After iqalah, the buyer may not use capital until possession; it is treated as a sold item.

When a salam contract is mutually rescinded (iqalah), the capital debt remains. A common question is whether the buyer can immediately use that capital to purchase something else from the seller. This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies the prohibition based on a hadith and legal reasoning, and also addresses the timing of possession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and prohibition
After iqalah, the buyer is prohibited from buying anything from the seller using the capital until he takes full possession of the capital.
The prohibition applies to any purchase from the muslam ilayh using the capital.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith 'La ta'khudh illa salamaka aw ra'sa malik' restricts the buyer to either the subject matter (if contract stands) or the capital (if rescinded). Any other exchange is forbidden.
The hadith is from Daraqutni.
3
Understand the reasoning
Iqalah is treated as a new sale in the right of third parties. The subject matter (muslam fih) is extinguished, so the capital becomes the de facto sold item. Hence, it cannot be disposed of before possession.
This is based on the principle that selling before possession is prohibited.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Zufar held that possession must occur in the same session because iqalah is like a new sale. The majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) disagree, stating that iqalah is not entirely new.
The text says 'wa al-hujjah 'alayhi ma dhakarna', indicating the majority view is preferred.
5
Derive the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that possession of the capital is not required in the session, but it must be taken before using the capital for another purchase.
Practical consequence: the buyer can take possession at any time, but cannot use it until possession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بیع سلم کے اقالے کا حکم
فان تقايلا السلم لم يكن له ان يشترى من المسلم اليه برأس المال شيئا حتى يقبضه كله لقوله عليه السلام لا تأخذ الا سلمک او رأس مالک ای عند الفسخ ولانه اخذ شبها بالمبيع فلا يحل التصرف فيه قبل قبضه وهذا لان الاقالة بيع جديد في حق ثالث ولا يمكن جعل المسلم فيه مبيعا لسقوطه فجعل رأس المال مبيعا لانه دين مثله الا انه لا يجب قبضه فى المجلس لانه ليس فى حكم الابتدأ من كل وجه وفيه خلاف زفر والحجة عليه ما ذكرناه
ترجمہ پھر اگر دونوں نے سلم کا اقالہ کر لیا تو رب السلام کو یہ اختیار نہیں ہے کہ راس المال کے عوض مسلم الیہ سے کوئی چیز خریدے یہاں تک کہ پورے رأس المال پر قبضہ کرلے کیونکہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ مت لے مگر اپنی سلم کو یا اپنے راس المال کو ۔ یعنی عقد سلم فتح ہونے پر ۔ اور اس لئے کہ راس المال نے مبیع کے ساتھ مشابہت اختیار کر لی ہے اس لئے قبضہ سے پہلے اس میں تصرف حلال نہ ہو گا۔ اور یہ اس لئے کہ اقالہ تیسرے کے حق میں بھیج جدید ہوتا ہے اور مسلم فیہ کو بیع قرار دینا اس لئے ممکن نہیں کہ وہ ساقط ہے۔ پس راس المال پر قبضہ کرنا واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ من کل وجہ ابتدائی عقد کے حکم میں نہیں ہے اور اس میں امام زفر کا اختلاف ہے اور ان کے خلاف حجت وہ ہے جو ہم نے ذکر کیا ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر رب السلم اور مسلم الیہ نے بیع سلم کا اقالہ کر لیا تو رب السلام کو یہ اختیار نہیں ہے کہ وہ راس المال پر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے اس کے عوض مسلم الیہ سے کوئی چیز خریدے۔ ہاں جب پورے راس المال پر قبضہ کر لے گا تو اس کو اختیار ہے کو جو چاہے خریدے اور جس سے چاہے خریدے۔
دلیل رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا یہ قول ہے لا تأخذ الا سلمک او رأس مالک یعنی مت لے مگر مسلم فیہ یا راس المال یعنی اگر بیع سلم باقی ہے تو رب السلم مسلم الیہ سے مسلم فیہ وصول کرے گا اور اگر بیع سلم فسخ ہوگئی تو رب السلم مسلم الیہ سے اپنا دیا ہوار اس المال وصول کرے گا۔ اس کے علاوہ کوئی مبادلہ نہیں کر سکتا۔ دار قطنی کی حدیث کے الفاظ یہ ہیں " فلا یا خذ الا ما اسلم فيه او رأس ماله يعنى نہ لے مگر وہ چیز جس میں عقد سلم کیا ہے یا اپنار اس المال۔ حاصل یہ کہ رب السلم بقائے عقد کی صورت میں مسلم فیہ وصول کر سکتا ہے اور نسخ کی صورت میں راس المال وصول کر سکتا ہے۔ ان کے تبادلہ میں دوسری کسی چیز کے لینے کا اختیار نہ ہوگا۔
دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اقالہ کی صورت میں رأس المال ہیچ کے مشابہ ہو گیا ہے، کیونکہ اقالہ عاقدین کے علاوہ تیسرے آدمی کے حق میں بیج جدید ہوتا ہے اور بیج کے لئے معقود علیہ ( طبیع) کا موجود ہونا ضروری ہے اور مسلم فیہ چونکہ اقالہ کی وجہ سے مسلم الیہ کے ذمہ سے ساقط ہوگئی ہے اسلئے مسلم فیہ معقود عالیہ نہیں ہو سکتی اور جب مسلم فیہ معقود علیہ نہیں ہو سکی تو راس المال کو معقود علیہ لینی مبیع قرارد یناضروری
Ruling on iqalah (rescission) of salam. If they rescind the salam, it is not permissible for him (the buyer) to buy anything from the seller (muslam ilayh) in exchange for the capital until he takes possession of all of it, because of his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Do not take except your salam or your capital' — i.e., at the time of dissolution. And because the capital has become similar to a sold item, so disposition in it before possession is not lawful. And this is because iqalah is a new sale in the right of a third party, and it is not possible to make the subject matter a sold item because it is extinguished. So the capital is made a sold item because it is a debt like it, except that possession of it is not obligatory in the session because it is not in the ruling of an entirely new contract. And there is a difference of opinion of Zufar in this, and the proof against him is what we have mentioned. Translation: Then if both parties rescind the salam, the buyer (rabb al-salam) does not have the option to buy anything from the seller in exchange for the capital until he takes possession of all the capital, because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Do not take except your salam or your capital' — i.e., when the contract is dissolved. And because the capital has become similar to a sold item, so disposition in it before possession is not lawful. And this is because iqalah is a new sale in the right of a third party, and it is not possible to make the subject matter a sold item because it is extinguished. So it is not obligatory to take possession of the capital in the session because it is not in the ruling of an entirely new contract. And there is a difference of opinion of Imam Zufar in this, and the proof against him is what we have mentioned. Explanation: The scenario is that if the buyer and seller have rescinded the salam contract, then the buyer is not allowed to buy anything from the seller in exchange for the capital before taking possession of all the capital. Yes, when he takes possession of all the capital, then he has the option to buy whatever he wants and from whomever he wants. Proof: The saying of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): 'Do not take except your salam or your capital' — meaning do not take except the subject matter or the capital. That is, if the salam contract remains, the buyer will receive the subject matter from the seller; and if the salam contract is dissolved, the buyer will receive his paid capital from the seller. He cannot make any exchange other than this. The words of the hadith of Daraqutni are: 'He does not take except what he made salam upon or his capital' — meaning do not take except the thing for which the salam contract was made or his capital. The conclusion is that the buyer can receive the subject matter if the contract remains, and can receive the capital if it is annulled. He will not have the option to take anything else in exchange. The second proof is that in the case of iqalah, the capital has become similar to a sold item, because iqalah is a new sale in the right of a third party, and for a sale it is necessary that a subject matter (object of sale) exists, and since the subject matter is extinguished from the seller's liability due to iqalah, it cannot be the subject matter. So it becomes necessary to make the capital the subject matter (sold item)...
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on iqalah (mutual rescission) in a salam contract. After rescission, the buyer cannot purchase anything else from the seller in exchange for the capital until he actually receives the full capital. The proof is the hadith: 'Do not take except your salam or your capital,' meaning upon dissolution you take only the capital, not a substitute. The reason is that in iqalah, the capital becomes like a sold item (mabi') because the subject matter is no longer owed. Therefore, it cannot be disposed of before possession. However, possession of the capital is not required in the same session because iqalah is not a completely new contract. Imam Zufar disagreed on whether possession is required in the session, but the relied-upon position is that it is not obligatory in the session, though the buyer must still take possession before using it to buy something else. The practical consequence is that after iqalah, the buyer must physically receive his capital back before he can use it in any other transaction.

Key Terms
اقالہ (iqalah): Mutual rescission of a contract; here, the parties agree to cancel the salam contract.
مسلم فیہ (muslam fih): The subject matter of salam, which becomes extinguished upon iqalah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is true after iqalah of a salam contract?
A) The buyer may immediately use the capital to buy anything from the seller.
B) The buyer must take possession of the capital before using it for any purchase from the seller.
C) The buyer must take possession of the capital in the same session or the iqalah is invalid.
D) The buyer may never use the capital to buy from the seller again.

Key Takeaway
After iqalah in salam, the buyer cannot use the capital for any purchase until he physically receives the full capital.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on Iqala (Cancellation) in Salam Contract
Explains ruling of iqala in Salam with proofs and disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on iqala in salam, explain the hadith and analogy that support it, and identify the dispute with Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
After iqala of salam, the buyer cannot use capital before possession; it resembles a sold item.

In salam sales, when both parties mutually cancel the contract (iqala), a question arises: can the buyer immediately use the returned capital to buy something else from the seller? The Hanafi school, based on a hadith and legal analogy, rules that the buyer must first physically take possession of the capital. This lesson unpacks the proof and addresses the disagreement of Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act: the buyer (rabb al-salam) buying something from the seller (muslam ilayh) using the capital after iqala before possession. The ruling: it is not permissible (haram).
The ruling applies only to purchasing from the seller, not from a third party.
2
Locate the primary proof (hadith)
The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Do not take except your salam or your capital.' This restricts the buyer to taking back either the goods (muslam fih) if the contract stands, or the capital if it is cancelled. No other exchange is allowed.
The hadith is reported by Dar Qutni and others.
3
Understand the analogy (capital as sold item)
Because iqala is considered a new sale in the right of third parties, the capital takes on the legal resemblance of a sold item. Since disposing of a sold item before possession is prohibited, the capital cannot be disposed of before possession.
The muslam fih is dropped, so the capital becomes the subject matter for the new sale to a third party.
4
Note the question about session of iqala
An objection arises: if iqala is a new sale, why isn't immediate possession of capital required in the session like an original salam? The answer is that iqala is not a new sale in every respect; it only applies to third parties, and the condition of immediate possession was to avoid the prohibited sale of debt for debt (bay' al-kali' bi al-kali'), which is no longer a risk.
Thus, possession is required but not necessarily in the session.
5
Recognize the dispute with Zufar and Shafi'i
Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i argue that since the capital becomes a debt, it can be exchanged without immediate possession. The Hanafi response is that the hadith and the analogy override this general permissibility.
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad.

الا انه لا يجب قبضه الخ ۔ اس سے ایک سوال کا جواب ہے۔
سوال یہ ہے کہ جب اقالہ عاقدین کے علاوہ تیسرے کے حق میں بیچ جدید ہے تو بیع سلم کا اقالہ تیسرے کے حق میں بیع سلم ہوگا اور بیع مسلم میں مجلس بیع کے اندر راس المال پر قبضہ کرنا شرط ہے۔ پس اقالہ کے بعد اور بھی مجلس اقالہ میں رأس المال پر قبضہ کرنا شرط ہونا چاہئے تھا، حالانکہ اقالہ کے بعد مجلس اقالہ میں راس المال پر قبضہ کرنا شرط نہیں ہے؟
جواب اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اقالہ من کل وجہ ابتدائے بیج کے حکم میں نہیں ہے کیونکہ ابتدائے بیع تمام لوگوں کے حق میں بیج ہوتی ہے اور اقالہ عاقدین کے علاوہ تیسرے کے حق میں بیج ہوتا ہے۔ اور جو عقد ابتدا بیع سلم ہے اور تمام لوگوں کے حق میں بیع سلم ہے اس میں رأس المال پر قبضہ کی شرط لگانے سے لازم نہیں آتا کہ اس عقد سلم میں بھی قبضہ شرط ہو جو انتہا ، بیع سلم ہے اور عاقدین کے علاوہ تیسرے آدمی کے حق میں بیچ سلم ہے۔ اور وجہ یہ ہے کہ ابتدائے بیع سلم میں راس المال پر قبضہ کی شرط بیچ کالی بالکالی سے بچنے کے لئے تھی۔ اور اقالہ کی وجہ سے چونکہ مسلم فیہ مسلم الیہ کے ذمہ سے ساقط ہو گئی ہے اس لئے اگر مجلس اقالہ میں راس المال پر قبضہ نہ کیا گیا تو بیع الکالی بالکالی لازم نہ آئے گی اور جب بیع الکالی بالکالی لازم نہیں آئی تو اس صورت میں قبضہ بھی شرط نہ ہوگا۔
صاحب ہدایہ و فيه خلاف زفر سے فرماتے ہیں کہ اصل مسئلہ میں امام زفر اور امام شافعی کا اختلاف ہے۔ حضرت امام زفر اور امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اقالہ کے قرب السلام رأس المال پر قبضہ کئے بغیر اگر مسلم الیہ سے اس کے عوض کچھ خریدنا چاہے تو خرید سکتا ہے، کیونکہ اقالہ کے بعد راس المال مسلم الیہ کے ذمہ دین ہو گیا ہے۔ پس جس طرح دوسرے دیون کے عوض خرید نا جائز ہے اسی طرح راس المال کے عوض خرید نا بھی جائز ہوگا۔ لیکن امام زفر اور امام شافعی کے خلاف وہ حدیث اور عقلی دلیل حجت ہوگی جس کو ہم نے اپنے مذہب کی تائید میں پیش کیا ہے یعنی " لا تأخذ الا سلمك الحديث “ اور ” ولانه اخذ شبها بالمبيع“۔
Chapter of Salam. The proof of impermissibility is that in the case of partnership, it necessitates disposing of half of the muslam fih before possession, and in the case of delegation, disposing of the whole muslam fih before possession. It has already passed that disposing of muslam fih before possession is impermissible. Therefore, neither partnership nor delegation in muslam fih is permissible. The ruling on iqala of salam sale: If they make iqala of the salam, it is not permissible for him (the buyer) to buy anything from the seller (muslam ilayh) with the capital until he takes full possession of it, due to his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Do not take except your salam or your capital' i.e. upon rescission. And because the capital takes on the resemblance of the sold item, so disposal of it before possession is not lawful. And this is because iqala is a new sale in the right of a third party, and it is not possible to make the muslam fih the sold item because it is dropped, so the capital is made the sold item because it is a debt like it, except that taking possession of it is not obligatory in the session because it is not in the ruling of a new contract in every respect. And in it there is a disagreement of Zufar, and the proof against him is what we have mentioned. Translation: Then if both have made iqala of the salam, the buyer does not have the option to buy anything from the seller with the capital until he takes possession of the entire capital, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Do not take except your salam or your capital', i.e. upon rescission of the contract. And because the capital has assumed resemblance to the sold item, so it is not lawful to dispose of it before possession. And because iqala is a new sale in the right of a third party, and making the muslam fih a sale is not possible because it is dropped. So it is not obligatory to take possession of the capital, because it is not in the ruling of an initial contract in every respect, and in this there is a disagreement of Imam Zufar, and the proof against him is what we have mentioned. Explanation of the scenario: It is that if the buyer and seller have made iqala of the salam sale, then the buyer does not have the option to buy anything from the seller with the capital before taking possession of the capital. Yes, when he takes possession of the entire capital, he has the option to buy whatever he wants and from whomever he wants. Proof: The statement of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Do not take except your salam or your capital' i.e. do not take except the muslam fih or the capital. That is, if the salam sale remains, the buyer will receive the muslam fih from the seller, and if the salam sale is rescinded, the buyer will receive his paid capital from the seller. He cannot make any exchange besides this. The wording of Dar Qutni's hadith is: 'So do not take except what you gave salam for or your capital' meaning do not take except the thing for which the salam contract was made or your capital. Summary: The buyer may receive the muslam fih in case of the contract's survival, and the capital in case of cancellation. He will not have the option to take anything else in exchange. Second proof: That in the case of iqala, the capital has become similar to the sold item, because iqala is a new sale in the right of a third party, and for a sale, the existence of the subject matter is necessary. Since the muslam fih is dropped from the seller's liability due to iqala, the muslam fih cannot be the subject matter. And when the muslam fih cannot be the subject matter, then it is necessary to make the capital the subject matter (sold item) so that the contract can be executed; otherwise, what we have assumed to be the sold item would not be a sale, while it is invalid for iqala not to be a sale in the right of a third party. And the capital has the capacity to be a sold item because the capital is a debt like the muslam fih, and making a debt a sold item is not impossible. So it is established that the capital resembles the sold item. And it has already passed that disposing of the sold item before possession is impermissible. So when it is not permissible to dispose of the sold item before possession, then that which resembles it, i.e. the capital, is also not permissible to dispose of before possession. And when in the case of iqala, disposal of the capital before possession is not permitted, then after iqala, the buyer does not have the option to buy anything from the seller in exchange for the capital. 'Except that possession is not obligatory' etc. This is the answer to a question. Question: When iqala is a new sale in the right of a third party, then the iqala of a salam sale is itself a salam sale in the right of a third party, and in a salam sale, possession of the capital is a condition in the session of sale. So after iqala, it should be required that possession of the capital be taken in the session of iqala, whereas it is not a condition? Answer: The answer is that iqala is not, in every respect, in the ruling of an initial sale, because an initial sale is a sale in the right of all people, while iqala is a sale in the right of a third party. And for the contract which is an initial salam sale and is a salam sale in the right of all people, imposing the condition of possession of the capital in it does not necessitate that in this contract of salam (which is a termination, a salam sale in the right of a third party) possession is also a condition. The reason is that the condition of possession of the capital in the initial salam sale was to avoid bay' al-kali' bi al-kali' (sale of debt for debt). And because, due to iqala, the muslam fih is dropped from the seller's liability, if possession of the capital is not taken in the session of iqala, bay' al-kali' bi al-kali' does not occur, and when it does not occur, possession is not a condition in this case. The author of Hidayah says: 'And in it there is a disagreement of Zufar'. He says that in this fundamental issue, Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i have a disagreement. Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i say: If after iqala, the buyer wants to buy something from the seller in exchange for the capital without taking possession of the capital, he may do so, because after iqala, the capital has become a debt owed by the seller. So just as it is permissible to buy in exchange for other debts, likewise buying in exchange for the capital is also permissible. But against Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i, the hadith and rational proof that we have presented in support of our school will be the argument: i.e. 'Do not take except your salam...' hadith and 'And because it (the capital) takes on the resemblance of the sold item'.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from Ashraf al-Hidayah on the chapter of Salam. It begins by recalling that partnership and delegation in muslam fih before possession are impermissible because they involve disposal before possession. Then it presents the main ruling: when the buyer and seller mutually cancel the salam contract (iqala), the buyer cannot use the capital to buy anything from the seller until he physically takes possession of the entire capital. The proof is the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) which restricts the buyer to taking either the muslam fih (if the contract remains) or the capital (if cancelled). Additionally, the capital takes on the legal resemblance (shubbiha) of a sold item because iqala acts as a new sale regarding a third party. Since the muslam fih is cancelled, the capital becomes the subject matter, and it is a debt like the muslam fih. Because disposing of the sold item before possession is prohibited, the same applies to the capital. The text then addresses an objection: if iqala is a new sale for a third party, why isn't immediate possession of the capital required in the session as in an original salam? The answer is that iqala is not a new sale in every respect; it differs from an initial sale because it is a sale only for outsiders, and the condition of immediate possession in the original salam was to avoid the forbidden sale of debt for debt (bay' al-kali' bi al-kali'). Since the muslam fih is cancelled, the danger of debt-for-debt sale is eliminated, so immediate possession is not required. Finally, the disagreement of Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i is mentioned: they permit buying with the capital before possession because it is a debt and debts can be exchanged. The Hanafi school refutes this with the hadith and the analogy of the capital resembling a sold item.

Key Terms
إقالة (iqālah): Mutual rescission of a contract; cancellation by both parties.
رأس المال (ra's al-māl): The principal/capital paid by the buyer in a salam contract.
مسلم فيه (muslam fīh): The subject matter of the salam contract; the goods to be delivered in the future.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
After iqala of a salam contract, what must the buyer do before using the capital to buy from the seller?
A) Receive the muslam fih.
B) Take possession of the entire capital.
C) Have a witness present.
D) Write a new contract.

Key Takeaway
After iqala of salam, the buyer must take physical possession of the capital before using it to buy from the seller, per the hadith and the capital's resemblance to a sold item.

Ruling on Taking Possession of Wheat in Salam Settlement
Determining valid possession in salam settlement with third-party purchase

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between valid and invalid methods of taking possession in a salam settlement involving food, and apply the requirement of two separate measurements.

Core Idea
In salam settlements involving food, each transfer of ownership requires a separate measurement; two sales require two measures.

This passage addresses a common question in salam (forward sale) contracts: when the seller buys the commodity from a third party to fulfill the debt, how should the buyer take possession? The Hanafi school draws a critical distinction between direct possession as payment and a two-step agency process, based on a prophetic prohibition of selling food before it is measured. Understanding this ruling prevents invalid settlements and ensures the debt is properly satisfied.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Locate in the passage the two different instructions the seller can give to the buyer. Note which one is valid and which is not.
The first scenario: 'take as payment' – invalid. Second: 'take for me then for yourself' – valid.
2
State the Hanafi ruling for each
The first does not fulfill the debt; the second does. Explain why the second is valid because of agency and double measurement.
3
Extract the dalil
Find the hadith used as evidence: the Prophet prohibited selling food until two measures have been applied to it. Write the Arabic text and identify its source credibility.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but relied upon in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Analyze wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadith proves the need for two measurements. Discuss why two transactions require two measurements.
Each sale is a separate contract; each requires measurement to avoid gharar.
5
Apply to modern scenarios
Consider a similar case today: a salam for rice paid with rice from a third party. The same rule applies: two measurements needed.
Electronic weighing counts as measurement if each transfer is independently measured.

A person entered a salam contract for a kurr of wheat. When the term arrived, the seller bought a kurr from a man and ordered the buyer to take possession as payment. Was his right fulfilled by taking possession or not? He said: And whoever enters salam for a kurr of wheat, then when the term expires, the seller buys a kurr from a man and orders the buyer to take possession as payment; it is not payment. But if he orders him to take possession for him (the seller) and then take possession for himself, and he measures it [for the seller] and then measures it for himself, it is valid, because the two transactions have come together with the condition of measurement, so two measurements are necessary due to the Prophet's prohibition of selling food until two measures have been applied to it. And this is...

Commentary
This passage presents a specific case in salam. A buyer (rabb al-salam) had contracted to receive a kurr of wheat. At maturity, the seller bought a kurr from a third party and told the buyer to take it as payment. The ruling distinguishes two scenarios. (1) If the seller says 'Take it in satisfaction of my debt,' the buyer does not fulfill his right by taking possession because the wheat is not yet the seller's property to transfer as payment—it is still the property of the third party. (2) If the seller says 'Take it for me (as my agent), then take it for yourself,' the buyer first takes possession as the seller's agent (measuring it for the seller), and then takes possession for himself (measuring it again). This is valid because two separate transactions are involved: the seller's purchase from the third party and the settlement of the salam. Each requires its own measurement (kayl) due to the Prophet's prohibition of selling food before it is measured. The phrase 'until two measures are applied to it' indicates that when food is involved, each transfer of ownership must be accompanied by a distinct measurement to avoid uncertainty (gharar). The passage ends abruptly, but the ruling is clear: the proper method involves two measurements.

Key Terms
كُرّ (kurr): A measure of weight or volume for wheat, often 600 kg or variable; a specific unit in classical Hanafi texts.
صاع (ṣā'): A unit of measurement for food items; the hadith requires two measurements (ṣā'ān) for food transactions.
قضاء (qaḍā'): Satisfaction of a debt; fulfillment of the salam obligation.

Key Takeaway
For a salam settlement involving food, the buyer must first act as the seller's agent to take possession and measure, then measure again for himself, because each sale of food requires a separate measurement.

Disposal of Capital After Iqalah in Salam: The Analogy with Sold Items
Ruling with proof using qiyas jaliy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that after iqalah in salam, the capital cannot be used before possession, and explain the qiyas with a sold item (mabi').

Core Idea
After iqalah, capital becomes like an unsold item: cannot be used before possession.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses a practical question after rescinding a salam contract: can the buyer (rabb al-salam) immediately use the capital to buy something else from the same seller? The Hanafi ruling is clear – not before taking possession. The proof is a powerful analogy that reveals the underlying principle of avoiding debt-for-debt sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the Hanafi ruling: after iqalah, the capital (ra's al-mal) cannot be disposed of until possession is taken. This is the main point of the passage.
The ruling is a prohibition of disposal, analogous to the prohibition on selling a bought item before receiving it.
2
Understand the qiyas structure
Identify the analogy: asl (sold item before possession, mabi'), far' (capital after iqalah), illa (both become a debt in the liability of the other party). The ruling from the asl (impermissibility of disposal) is transferred to the far'.
The qiyas is jaliyy – clear analogy. The illa is extracted via tahqiq al-manat.
3
Analyze the objection
Consider the objection: if iqalah is a new sale for third parties, why is possession of capital not required in the iqalah session itself, as it would be in an initial salam?
The objection challenges the consistency of the ruling.
4
Examine the answer
The answer is that iqalah is not a new sale in every respect; the condition of possession in initial salam was to prevent bay' al-kali' bi'l-kali' (sale of debt for debt). Since iqalah removes the muslam fihi from liability, the danger of kali' bi'l-kali' is eliminated, so possession in the session is not required.
This shows careful distinction between the initial contract and the rescission.

So when it is not permissible to transact in the sold item before possession, then what resembles it, i.e., the capital, it will also not be permissible to transact in it before taking possession. The question is: When iqalah is a new sale for a third party other than the two contracting parties, then the iqalah of a salam sale will be a salam sale for the third party, and in a salam sale, taking possession of the capital in the session is a condition. So after iqalah, taking possession of the capital should also be a condition in the iqalah session, whereas after iqalah, taking possession of the capital in the iqalah session is not a condition? The answer to this is that iqalah is not in every respect in the ruling of an initial sale because the initial sale is a sale for all people, and iqalah is a sale for only the third party other than the contracting parties. And the contract that is initially a salam sale and is a salam sale for all people, imposing the condition of possession of capital in it does not necessitate that this salam contract also has possession as a condition which is the end, it is a salam sale and for a third person other than the contracting parties it is a salam sale. And the reason is that in the initial salam sale, the condition of possession of capital was to avoid bay' al-kali' bi'l-kali'. And because of iqalah, since the muslam fihi has fallen from the liability of the muslim ilayhi, therefore if possession of the capital is not taken in the iqalah session, then bay' al-kali' bi'l-kali' will not occur, and when bay' al-kali' bi'l-kali' does not occur, then possession will also not be a condition in that case.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from Ashraf al-Hidayah regarding the effect of iqalah (rescission) on a salam (advance payment sale) contract. The author establishes that after iqalah, the capital (ra's al-mal) becomes like a sold item (mabi') in the sense that it cannot be disposed of before taking possession. The proof is by analogy: just as it is impermissible to transact in a sold item before receiving it, similarly the capital, which has become a debt (dain) after iqalah, cannot be used to purchase something from the same muslim ilayhi before possession. The passage then addresses an objection: why is possession of the capital not required in the iqalah session itself if iqalah is considered a new sale from the third party's perspective? The answer is that iqalah is not a new sale in every respect; the condition of possession in the initial salam was to prevent bay' al-kali' bi'l-kali' (sale of debt for debt). Since the iqalah removes the original muslam fihi from liability, the danger of kali' bi'l-kali' does not arise, so possession in the session is not necessary. Thus, the ruling is that after iqalah, the rabb al-salam cannot use the capital to buy from the muslim ilayhi before taking actual possession, but the iqalah itself does not require immediate possession in the assembly.

Key Terms
اقالہ (iqalah): Rescission of a contract by mutual consent; in this context, it cancels the salam contract and returns the parties to pre-contract state.
راس المال (ra's al-mal): The capital paid in advance by the buyer (rabb al-salam) in a salam contract.
مسلم فیہ (muslam fihi): The commodity to be delivered in a salam contract; after iqalah, it is cancelled from the seller's liability.
مسلم الیہ (muslam ilayhi): The seller in a salam contract who receives the capital and is obligated to deliver the commodity.
بیع الکالی بالکالی (bay' al-kali' bi'l-kali'): Sale of debt for debt; prohibited in Islamic law. This is the reason possession of capital is required in salam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because the capital, like a sold item that has not been delivered, cannot be disposed of before possession.
C) Because the rabb al-salam has already paid it and cannot transact again.
D) Because iqalah is prohibited after the contract is concluded.

Key Takeaway
After iqalah in salam, the capital cannot be used before possession because it is analogous to a sold item not yet received, and doing so would resemble the prohibited sale of debt for debt.

Using Capital After Iqalah: Zufar and Shafi'i vs. Hanafi
Presents opposing view and refutes it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi prohibition on using salam capital after iqalah before possession and identify the conflicting views of Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
After iqalah, salam capital is not a free debt; it retains the resemblance of a sold item, making its use before possession invalid.

This lesson examines a nuanced dispute within the Hanafi school and between madhahib. The issue arises after a salam contract is rescinded (iqalah): can the buyer (rabb al-salam) use the capital to purchase something from the seller (muslim ilayhi) before actually taking possession of the capital? Imam Zufar, a major Hanafi jurist, and Imam al-Shafi'i argue yes, because the capital becomes a pure debt. However, the relied-upon Hanafi position says no, based on a hadith and the analogy that the capital still resembles a sold item. Understanding this disagreement sharpens your ability to apply proofs and recognize when a debt retains contractual peculiarities.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling according to Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad: it is not permissible to use the capital before possession. The transaction would be invalid (batil).
2
Identify the opposing view and its evidence
Imam Zufar (Hanafi) and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that after iqalah, the capital becomes a pure debt, and exchanging debt for goods is generally permissible. Therefore, the buyer may purchase from the seller using that debt without first taking possession.
Their analogy: just like any other debt, salam capital can be used for purchase.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school counters with two proofs: (1) a hadith ('Do not take except your salam') implying restricted use of salam capital, and (2) rational analogy: the capital resembles a sold item (mabi') because it originates from a sale contract, thus it cannot be disposed of before possession.
The hadith and analogy override the general permissibility of debt exchanges.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: according to Zufar and Shafi'i, the subsequent purchase is valid; according to the Hanafi school, it is invalid (batil) and must be rescinded.
5
Identify the tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of Abu Hanifa and the majority of Hanafis; Zufar's view is not adopted in fatwa.
This demonstrates that even within a school, a companion of the imam may hold a contrary opinion, but the school's established position prevails.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب ہدایہ و فيه خلاف زفر سے فرماتے ہیں کہ اصل مسئلہ میں امام زفر اور امام شافعی کا اختلاف ہے۔ حضرت امام زفر اور امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اقالہ کے قرب السلام رأس المال پر قبضہ کئے بغیر اگر مسلم الیہ سے اس کے عوض کچھ خریدنا چاہے تو خرید سکتا ہے، کیونکہ اقالہ کے بعد راس المال مسلم الیہ کے ذمہ دین ہو گیا ہے۔ پس جس طرح دوسرے دیون کے عوض خرید نا جائز ہے اسی طرح راس المال کے عوض خرید نا بھی جائز ہوگا۔ لیکن امام زفر اور امام شافعی کے خلاف وہ حدیث اور عقلی دلیل حجت ہوگی جس کو ہم نے اپنے مذہب کی تائید میں پیش کیا ہے یعنی " لا تأخذ الا سلمك الحديث " اور ” ولانه اخذ شبها بالمبيع“۔
The author of Hidayah says: 'And in it there is a difference of Zufar.' He says: In the original issue, there is a difference between Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i. Hadrat Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i say: After iqalah, if the rabb al-salam wants to buy something from the muslim ilayhi in exchange for the capital without taking possession of the capital, he may buy, because after iqalah the capital has become a debt in the liability of the muslim ilayhi. So just as it is permissible to buy in exchange for other debts, similarly buying in exchange for the capital will also be permissible. But against Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i, the hadith and rational proof that we have presented in support of our madhhab will be an argument, namely the hadith 'Do not take except your salam' and 'Because it takes resemblance to the sold item'.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute within the Hanafi discussion of salam. The author of Hidayah notes that Imam Zufar (a prominent Hanafi jurist) and Imam al-Shafi'i hold a contrary opinion: after iqalah, the capital becomes a pure debt, and since exchanging debt for goods is generally permissible (as long as not involving riba or kali' bi'l-kali'), the rabb al-salam may use that capital to buy something from the same muslim ilayhi without first taking possession of the capital. The Hanafi position, however, relies on two proofs: first, a hadith (referred to as 'la ta'khudh illa salamak' – 'Do not take except your salam') which implies that the capital in a salam transaction is not to be treated as a free debt but retains the status of a specific obligation; second, a rational analogy (qiyas) that the capital resembles a sold item (mabi') because it becomes a debt similar to the muslam fihi, and thus cannot be disposed of before possession. This shows that even within the Hanafi school, Zufar's view is distinguished from the main position, but the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the one that prohibits use before possession.

Key Terms
امام زفر (Imam Zufar): Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl, a major Hanafi jurist and companion of Abu Hanifa, known for his distinct opinions.
لا تأخذ الا سلمك (la ta'khudh illa salamak): A hadith quoted in context of salam, indicating that the capital of salam is not to be used for other purchases before taking possession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because they rely on a weak analogy.
B) Because the capital after iqalah is not a pure debt but resembles a sold item, supported by a hadith.
C) Because iqalah is not valid in salam contracts according to the majority.
D) Because the capital must be returned in cash, not used in another transaction.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits using salam capital after iqalah before possession because it retains the resemblance of a sold item, overriding the general permissibility of debt exchange.

Double Measurement in Salam Discharge via Third Party
Case study on measuring grain twice in salam repayment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on double measurement when discharging a salam debt via a third-party purchase and apply it to a similar scenario.

Core Idea
A salam debt is discharged only when the creditor measures the grain twice: once as agent for the seller, once for himself.

This lesson examines a nuanced case in salam (forward sale) where the seller (muslim ilayhi) buys the specified commodity from a third party to deliver to the buyer (rabb al-salam). The central question is whether simply directing the buyer to take possession suffices to discharge the debt. As we will see, Hanafi fiqh requires a careful double measurement to ensure each transaction is valid and free from prohibited elements like bay' al-kali' bi'l-kali'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is discharging a salam debt by having the muslim ilayhi purchase the commodity from a third party and instruct the rabb al-salam to take possession. The ruling: if the rabb al-salam takes direct possession, the debt is not discharged; if he first measures as agent for the muslim ilayhi and then measures again for himself, it is valid.
Double measurement is the crucial condition.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is the hadith: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade the sale of food until two saa' are exchanged in it.' This indicates that when two transactions involve the same food, two separate measurements are required.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'two saa'' implies that for each sale of food, a measurement must be made. In this case, there are two sales: (1) from the third party to the muslim ilayhi, and (2) from the muslim ilayhi to the rabb al-salam. Thus two measurements are necessary to avoid gharar and ensure proper delivery.
Each sale is an independent transaction requiring its own measurement.
4
Distinguish the case of qard
The passage contrasts salam with a loan (qard). In qard, the borrower can instruct the lender to take possession of an item purchased from a third party without double measurement because qard is treated as a return of the same item (like 'ariyah), not as a sale.
This distinction highlights the unique nature of salam as a sale of debt.

ایک گر گندم میں بیع السلم کی مدت آگئی تو مسلم الیہ نے ایک آدمی سے ایک گر گندم خرید کر رب السلم کو قبضہ کرنے کا حکم دیا تو قبضہ کرنے سے حق وصول ہو گیا یا نہیں؟
قال و من اسلم فى كُرّ حنطة فلما حل الاجل اشترى المسلم إليه من رجل كراً وامر رب السلم بقبضه قضاء لم يكن قضاء وان امره ان يقبضه له ثم يقبضه لنفسه فاكتاله ثم اكتاله لنفسه جاز لانه اجتمعت الصفقتان بشرط الكيل فلابد من الكيل مرتين لنهى النبي عليه السلام عن بيع الطعام حتى يجرى فيه صاعان وهذا هو
