باب السلم
اشرف البدایہ جلد- ضمیم محمل الحديث على مامر والسلم وان كان سابقا لكن قبض المسلم فيه لاحق وانه بمنزلة ابتداء البيع لان العين غير الدين حقيقة وان جعل عينه في حق حكم خاص وهو حرمة الاستبدال فيتحقق البيع بعد الشراء وان لم يكن سلما وكان قرضا فامره بقبض الكر جاز لان القرض اعارة ولهذا ينعقد بلفظ الاعارة فكان مردود عين الماخوذ مطلقا حكما فلا يجتمع الصفقتان
ترجمہ . اگر ایک شخص نے ایک گر گندم میں بیع سلم کی پھر جب ادائے مسلم فیہ کی میعاد آئی تو مسلم الیہ نے ایک آدمی سے ایک گر گندم خریدا اور رب السلم کو اپنے ادائے حق میں اسپر قبضہ کا حکم دیا تو یہ اس کا ادائے حق نہ ہو گا۔ اور اگر اس کو حکم دیا کہ مسلم الیہ کے واسطے قبضہ کر لے پھر اپنے واسطے قبضہ کر لے، پس رب السلام نے اس کو مسلم الیہ کے واسطے کیل کیا پھر اس کو اپنے واسطے کیل کیا تو جائز ہے۔ اس لئے کہ دو صفقہ بشرط الکیل جمع ہو گئے ۔ لہذا دو مرتبہ کیل کرنا ضروری ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اناج کی خرید وفروخت سے منع فرمایا ہے یہاں تک کہ اس میں دو صاع جاری ہوں۔ اور یہی حدیث کا عمل ہے جیسا کہ سابق میں گذر چکا ہے۔ اور مسلم اگر چہ پہلے تھی لیکن مسلم فیہ پر قبضہ بعد میں ہے اور مسلم فیہ پر قبضہ ابتدائے بیع کے مرتبہ میں ہے کیونکہ عین در حقیقت دین کے خلاف ہے اگر چہ ایک خاص حکم یعنی استبدال حرام ہونے میں مال عین ( مقبوض) کو عین دین قرار دیا گیا ہے پس خرید کے بعد فروخت کر نا حق ہو گا۔ اور اگر سلم نہ ہو ( بلکہ ) قرضہ ہو پھر قرضدار نے (خرید کر ) قرض خواہ کو گر پر قبضہ کرنے کا حکم دیا تو یہ جائز ہے اس لیے کہ قرض عاریہ دینا ہے اور اسی وجہ سے لفظ اعارہ سے قرض منعقد ہو جاتا ہے پس بحکم شرع جو واپس کیا گیا ہے وہ مطلقاً بعینہ وہ ہے جولیا گیا تھا لہذا د و صفقہ جمع نہ ہوں گے۔
کہ فیاد کر تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر ایک شخص نے دوسرے سے ایک گر گندم میں عقد سلم کیا پھر جب مسلم فیہ ادا کر نے کی میعاد پوری ہو گئی تو مسلم الیہ نے ایک آدمی سے ایک گر گندم خرید کر رب السلام کو حکم دیا کہ اپنا حق وصول کرنے کے لیے اس پر قبضہ کرلے پس رب اسلم نے مسلم الیہ کے حکم کے مطابق قبضہ کر لیا تو اس سے رب اسلم کا حق وصول نہ ہوگا۔ چنانچہ اگر مقبوض گندم رب السلام کے قبضہ میں ہلاک ہوگیا تو یہ مسلم الیہ کے مال سے ہلاک ہو گا اور رب اسلم کو اپنا حق وصول کرنے کے مطالبہ کا اختیار ہوگا اوراگر مسلم الیہ نے رب السلم کو یہ حکم دیا کہ پہلے وہ مسلم الیہ کی طرف سے وکیل بن کر قبضہ کر لے پھر اپنا حق وصول کرنے کیلئے قبضہ کرلے پس رب السلم نے مسلم الیہ کے حکم کے مطابق پہلے اس کو مسلم الیہ کے واسطے کیل کیا اور پھر اپنے واسطے کیل کیا تو یہ جائز ہے یعنی اس سے رب السلام کا حق وصول ہو جائے گا اور مسلم الیہ کا حق ادا ہو جائے گا۔
دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہاں کیل کی شرط کے ساتھ دو صفقہ جمع ہو گئے ایک صفقہ مسلم الیہ اور اس کے بائع کے درمیان اور دوسرا صفقہ مسلم الیہ اور رب السلم کے درمیان اور جب بشرط الکیل دو صفقہ جمع ہو جائیں تو دو مرتبہ کیل کرنا ضروری ہوگا اور ایک مرتبہ مسلم الیہ کا اپنے بائع سے خریدنے کی وجہ سے کیل کرنا ضروری ہوگا اور ایک مرتبہ مسلم الیہ کا رب السلم کو فروخت کرنے کی وجہ سے کیل کرنا ضروری ہوگا ۔ اور بشرط الکیل دو صفقہ جمع ہونے کی صورت میں دو مرتبہ کیل کرنا اس لئے ضروری ہے کہ ہادی عالم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اناج کی بیج سے منع فرمایا ہے یہاں تک کہ اس میں دو صاع جاری ہوں ایک صاع بائع کا اور دوسرا صاع مشتری کا یعنی جب بائع نے اپنے واسطے خریدا ہے تو اس کو ناپ کر لے اور جب دوسرے کو فروخت کرے گا تو وہ دوسرا ناپ کر لے گا۔ اس حدیث کا یہی محمل ہے جیسا کہ باب المرابحه والتولية
[Case] The maturity of a salam for one kurr of wheat came. The muslim ilayhi bought one kurr from a man and ordered the rabb al-salam to take possession. Did the right become collected or not? He said: And whoever gave salam in one kurr of wheat, then when the term came due, the muslim ilayhi bought a kurr from a man and ordered the rabb al-salam to take possession as repayment, it was not repayment. And if he ordered him to take possession for him (the muslim ilayhi) and then take it for himself, and he measured it and then measured it for himself, it is permissible, because the two transactions are combined with the condition of measurement, so measurement twice is necessary, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade the sale of food until two saa' are exchanged in it. And this is the application of the hadith as has passed. And the salam even though earlier, but the possession of the muslam fihi is later, and it is like a new sale because 'ayn (the specific item) is in reality different from dain (debt), even though it is considered as dain in a specific ruling, which is the prohibition of substitution. So sale after purchase becomes valid. And if it was not salam but a loan (qard), and the borrower ordered the lender to take possession of a kurr, it is permissible, because loan is a form of 'ariyah (borrowing), and for this reason it is concluded with the word 'ariyah. So what is returned is absolutely the same item as taken, so the two transactions do not combine. ... [The Urdu translation elaborates] The explanation of the issue: ...
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed case ruling on how a salam debt can be discharged when the muslim ilayhi buys the specified commodity from a third party to deliver to the rabb al-salam. The key ruling is that if the muslim ilayhi simply orders the rabb al-salam to take possession directly of the grain he bought, the rabb al-salam's debt is not discharged because the grain has not become the property of the muslim ilayhi in a manner that allows direct transfer. However, if the muslim ilayhi first appoints the rabb al-salam as his agent to receive the grain from the third party (i.e., measure it on behalf of the muslim ilayhi), and then the rabb al-salam measures it again for himself, the debt is discharged. The proof is the hadith that food cannot be sold until two measurements (saa' ) are performed: one for the buyer from the original seller, and one for the subsequent buyer. This ensures that each transaction is separate and valid. The passage also contrasts this with a loan (qard), where the borrower can directly instruct the lender to take possession of an item purchased from a third party without double measurement, because the loan is considered a return of the same item (the item is treated as an 'ayn, not a dain). This case illustrates the meticulousness of Hanafi fiqh in ensuring that transactions avoid prohibited elements like bay' al-kali' bi'l-kali' and that each sale is properly executed with measurement when the commodity requires it.

Key Terms
کیل (kayl): Measurement by volume, specifically for grain. It is a condition for valid sale of food items.
صاع (saa'): A standard measure of volume (approximately 2.5 kg); used in the hadith as a unit for measuring food.
قرض (qard): Loan; in this context, it is treated as a return of the exact item (like borrowing), so double measurement is not required when discharging a loan.
عاریہ (‘ariyah): Borrowing for use; the text says qard is like 'ariyah because it involves returning the same item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where a muslim ilayhi buys grain from a third party to deliver to the rabb al-salam, what is required for the rabb al-salam's debt to be discharged?
A) The rabb al-salam takes possession directly from the third party.
B) The muslim ilayhi first takes possession then gives it to the rabb al-salam.
C) The rabb al-salam first measures the grain as an agent for the muslim ilayhi, then measures it again for himself.
D) The muslim ilayhi signs a new contract transferring ownership.

Key Takeaway
Discharging a salam debt via a third-party purchase requires double measurement: first as agent for the seller, then for the creditor; otherwise the debt remains unpaid.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Delivery of Salam Goods: Two Measurements Required
Explains ruling on salam delivery when muslam ilayh buys from third party.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delivery of salam goods when the muslam ilayh purchases from a third party and apply the hadith requiring two measurements to determine the validity of delivery.

Core Idea
Two sales with measurement condition require two measurements; a single measurement makes delivery invalid.

In a salam contract, the seller may need to procure the commodity from the market. A common scenario: the muslam ilayh buys the exact commodity from a third party and tells the rabb al-salam to take possession. Is this valid delivery? The Hanafi school says no—unless two separate measurements are performed. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof, and the legal reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the muslam ilayh purchasing the muslam fihi from a third party and ordering the rabb al-salam to take possession for himself (without separate measurements). The ruling: delivery is invalid (ghayr sahih).
2
Locate the dalil
The Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited the sale of grain until two measures are applied. This hadith is the primary textual proof.
The source cites the hadith in its Urdu rendering.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith requires two measurements when grain is sold. In this scenario, two sale transactions are combined: the purchase from the third party and the sale to the rabb al-salam. Each transaction requires its own measurement, so two are necessary.
This ensures clarity and prevents gharar (uncertainty).
4
Apply the qiyas
The original case (asl) is a person buying grain and then selling it to another with measurement condition. The ruling of two measurements is applied to the far' (salam scenario) because the illa (effective cause) is the combination of two sales with measurement condition.
The Hanafi school uses this qiyas to extend the hadith ruling.
5
Note the consequence
Without two measurements, delivery is invalid. If the goods perish after a single measurement, the loss is borne by the muslam ilayh, and the rabb al-salam still has the right to demand his due.
This highlights the importance of proper measurement in grain sales.

باب السلم

کہ فیاد کر تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر ایک شخص نے دوسرے سے ایک گر گندم میں عقد سلم کیا پھر جب مسلم فیہ ادا کر نے کی میعاد پوری ہو گئی تو مسلم الیہ نے ایک آدمی سے ایک گر گندم خرید کر رب السلام کو حکم دیا کہ اپنا حق وصول کرنے کے لیے اس پر قبضہ کرلے پس رب اسلم نے مسلم الیہ کے حکم کے مطابق قبضہ کر لیا تو اس سے رب اسلم کا حق وصول نہ ہوگا۔ چنانچہ اگر مقبوض گندم رب السلام کے قبضہ میں ہلاک ہوگیا تو یہ مسلم الیہ کے مال سے ہلاک ہو گا اور رب اسلم کو اپنا حق وصول کرنے کے مطالبہ کا اختیار ہوگا اوراگر مسلم الیہ نے رب السلم کو یہ حکم دیا کہ پہلے وہ مسلم الیہ کی طرف سے وکیل بن کر قبضہ کر لے پھر اپنا حق وصول کرنے کیلئے قبضہ کرلے پس رب السلم نے مسلم الیہ کے حکم کے مطابق پہلے اس کو مسلم الیہ کے واسطے کیل کیا اور پھر اپنے واسطے کیل کیا تو یہ جائز ہے یعنی اس سے رب السلام کا حق وصول ہو جائے گا اور مسلم الیہ کا حق ادا ہو جائے گا۔

سے متصل فصل میں مذکور ہوا ہے۔
والسلم وان كان سابقاً الخ" سے ایک سوال مقدر کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ مسلم الیہ کا رب اسلم کو فروخت کرنا بہت پہلے ہے اور مسلم الیہ کا اپنے بائع سے خریدنا بہت بعد میں ہے پس مسلم الیہ اپنے بائع سے خریدنے کے بعد رب اسلم کو بیچنے والا نہ ہوگا اور جب مسلم الیہ خریدنے کے بعد رب السلام کو بیچنے والا نہ ہوا تو دو صفقہ بھی جمع نہ ہوئے اور جب دو صفتہ جمع نہ ہوئے تو دو مرتبہ کیل کرنا بھی ضرور کی نہ ہوگا اور جب دو مرتبہ کیل کرنا ضروری نہ ہوا تو جس صورت میں مسلم ایہ نے ایک گر گندم خرید کر رب اسلم کو اپنے ادائے حق کے لیے اس پر قبضہ کرنے کا حکم دیا ہے اس صورت میں مسلم الیہ کا حق ادا ہو جانا چاہیے تھا حالانکہ آپ نے فرمایا ہے کہ اس صورت میں مسلم الیہ کا حق ادا نہ ہو گا ؟
جواب اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ بیع سلم اگر چہ پہلے ہے یعنی مسلم الیہ کی خرید سے پہلے اگر چہسلم کا عقد ہو چکا تھا لیکن رب اسلم کا مسلم فیہ پر قبضہ کرنا مسلم الیہ کی خرید سے بعد میں ہے۔ اور مسلم فیہ پر قبضہ کرنا ابتدائے بیچ کے مرتبہ میں ہے۔ پس گویا رب اسلام اور مسلم الیہ دونوں نے اس مقبوضہ گندم پر از عصرنو عقد کیا ہے۔ اور مسلم فیہ پر قبضہ سے پہلے اس کے بدلے میں دوسری چیز کا لین لازم آتا ہے حالانکہ قبضہ سے پہلے مسلم فیہ کے جادلہ میں سی بھی چیز کالینا حرام ہے اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اس مخصوص کم یعنی یہ دونوں ایک ہی چیز میں ان دونوں میں کوئی غیریت نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اگر دین کو مال معین کا غیر مانا جائے گا تو مسلم فیہ کا تبادلہ کرنا لازم آئیگا حالانکہ استبدال با مسلم فیہ حرام ہے پس خاص طور پر استبدال حرام ہونے کے حق میں دین اور مال عین دونوں کو ایک مانا گیا ہے لیکن اس کے علاوہ باقی تمام جگہوں میں دین حقیقتاً مال عین کا غیر ہو گا اور جب دین یعنی مسلم فیہ مال معین یعنی مقبوضہ گندم کا غیر ہوا تو گویا مسلم الیہ نے ایک گر گندم خرید کر رب السلم کے ہاتھ مسلم فیہ یعنی دین کے عوض فروخت کیا ہے۔ اور اس صورت میں دو صفقوں کا جمع ہونا ظاہر ہے اور جب دو صفقہ جمع ہو گئے تو دو مرتبہ کیل کرنا بھی ضروری ہوگا۔ پس جس صورت میں فقط ایک مرتبہ کیل کیا گیا ہے اس صورت میں مسلم الیہ کی طرف سے ادا ئیگی معتبر نہ ہوگی ۔ اور رب السلم اپنا حق وصول کرنے والا شمار نہ ہو گا۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر بیع سلم نہ ہو بلکہ قرض ہو، یعنی جب ایک آدمی نے ایک گر گندم قرض لیا، پھر قرضدار نے خرید کر قرض خواہ کو قبضہ کرنے کا حکم دیا اور یہ نہیں کہا کہ پہلے میرے واسطے قبضہ کر لے پھر اپنے واسطے قبضہ کر پس قرض خواہ نے اس پر قبضہ کر لیا ، یعنی ایک مرتبہ کیل کر کے اپنے قبضہ میں لے لیا تو یہ جائز ہے کیونکہ قرضہ، عاریت پر دینے کا نام ہے۔ اور اگر قرضہ عاربیت پر دینے کا نام نہ ہو تو تملیک الشئی بجنسه نسيئة لازم آئے گا یعنی قرضدار نے جو چیز لی تھی قرض خواہ کو بنجنہ ادھار واپس کی گئی اور یہ ر بوا ہے پس ثابت ہوا کہ قرض عاریت پر دینے کا نام ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ لفظ اعارہ سے قرضہ منعقد ہو جاتا ہے چنانچہ اگر کسی نے کہا اعر تك هذا الدرهم تو اس سے قرض منعقد ہو جائے گا۔ چونکہ عاریہ میں میعاد لازم نہیں ہوتی بلکہ عاریت پر دینے والے کو ہر وقت شئی مستعار واپس لینے کا حق ہوتا ہے اس لیے قرضہ میں بھی میعاد لازم نہ ہوگی پس معلوم ہوا کہ قرض عاریت پر دینے کا نام ہے اور عاریہ میں عاربیت پر لینے والا جکم شرع بعینہ وہ چیز واپس کرتا ہے جو اس نے معیر سے لی تھی۔ پس قرض کی صورت میں قرضدار جو چیز واپس کرے گا وہ مطلقا اس چیز کا عین ہوگی جس پر قرضدار نے قبضہ کیا تھا یعنی استبدال کے حق میں بھی شئی مردود اور شئی مقبوض کے درمیان عینیت ثابت ہوگی اور استبدال کے
Chapter of Salam. Ashraf al-Hidayah volume - appendix. The interpretation of the hadith according to what has passed. And salam, even though it is earlier, but possession of the muslam fihi is later, and it is like the beginning of a sale because the specific commodity ('ayn) is different from a debt (dayn) in reality, even though it is treated as the same commodity in a specific ruling, which is the prohibition of substitution. So the sale takes place after the purchase. And if it is not salam but a loan, then his order to take possession of the kurr is permissible because a loan is a form of lending (i'arah); therefore it is concluded with the word of i'arah. So the returned item is absolutely the same as the taken item by ruling, so the two transactions are not combined. Translation: If a person made a salam contract for one kurr of wheat, then when the time for delivery of the muslam fihi came, the muslam ilayh bought one kurr of wheat from a person and ordered the rabb al-salam to take possession of it for his right, then this will not be his delivery of the right. And if he ordered him to take possession on behalf of the muslam ilayh, then take possession for himself, then the rabb al-salam measured it for the muslam ilayh, then measured it for himself, then it is permissible. Because two transactions with the condition of measurement are combined. Therefore two measurements are necessary. Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited the sale of grain until two measures are applied. And this is the application of the hadith, as has passed earlier. And even though the salam was earlier, but possession of the muslam fihi is later, and possession of the muslam fihi is in the rank of the beginning of a sale, because the commodity ('ayn) is in reality different from the debt (dayn), even though in a specific ruling, i.e., the prohibition of substitution, the possessed commodity is considered as the same as the debt. So after purchase, selling becomes valid. And if it is not salam but a loan, then the borrower bought and ordered the lender to take possession of the wheat, then this is permissible because a loan is giving as a loan, and therefore it is concluded with the word of i'arah. So by legal ruling, what is returned is absolutely the same as what was taken, so the two transactions are not combined. Explanation of the scenario: If a person made a salam contract with another for one kurr of wheat, then when the time for delivery of the muslam fihi was complete, the muslam ilayh bought one kurr of wheat from a person and ordered the rabb al-salam to take possession of it to receive his right. Then the rabb al-salam took possession according to the order. Then his right is not received. So if the possessed wheat perishes while in the possession of the rabb al-salam, it perishes from the property of the muslam ilayh, and the rabb al-salam has the right to demand his right. And if the muslam ilayh ordered the rabb al-salam to first take possession as his agent, then take possession for his own right, and the rabb al-salam measured it for the muslam ilayh and then measured it for himself, then this is permissible, i.e., the rabb al-salam's right is received and the muslam ilayh's obligation is fulfilled. The proof is that here two transactions with the condition of measurement are combined: one transaction between the muslam ilayh and his seller, and another transaction between the muslam ilayh and the rabb al-salam. And when two transactions with the condition of measurement are combined, two measurements are necessary: one measurement from the muslam ilayh buying from his seller, and one measurement from the muslam ilayh selling to the rabb al-salam. And in the case of combining two transactions with the condition of measurement, two measurements are necessary because the Guide of the Worlds (peace be upon him) prohibited the sale of grain until two measures are applied: one measure from the seller and one measure from the buyer. That is, when the seller has bought for himself, he should measure it, and when he sells to another, that other will measure it. This is the interpretation of this hadith, as mentioned in the connected chapter of the chapter of Murabahah and Tawliyah. The phrase "And salam even though it is earlier, etc." is an answer to an implied question. The question is: The muslam ilayh's sale to the rabb al-salam is much earlier, and the muslam ilayh's purchase from his seller is much later. So after purchasing from his seller, the muslam ilayh will not be the seller to the rabb al-salam. And when the muslam ilayh is not a seller to the rabb al-salam after purchase, then two transactions are not combined. And when two transactions are not combined, then two measurements are not necessary. And when two measurements are not necessary, then in the scenario where the muslam ilayh bought one kurr of wheat and ordered the rabb al-salam to take possession of it for his right, the muslam ilayh's obligation should be fulfilled, even though you said that in this scenario the muslam ilayh's obligation is not fulfilled? The answer is: Even though the salam sale is earlier, i.e., the salam contract had already taken place before the purchase, the rabb al-salam's possession of the muslam fihi is after the purchase. And taking possession of the muslam fihi is in the rank of the beginning of a sale. So it is as if the rabb al-salam and the muslam ilayh have performed a new contract on this possessed wheat. And before possession of the muslam fihi, taking something else in exchange for it becomes necessary, even though taking anything in exchange for the muslam fihi before possession is prohibited. The answer to this is that in this specific matter, there is no difference between the two; they are one thing. Because if the debt is considered different from the specific commodity, then exchanging the muslam fihi becomes necessary, even though substitution of the muslam fihi is prohibited. So specifically in terms of the prohibition of substitution, the debt and the specific commodity are considered one. But in all other places, the debt is in reality different from the specific commodity. And when the debt, i.e., the muslam fihi, is different from the specific commodity, i.e., the possessed wheat, then it is as if the muslam ilayh bought one kurr of wheat and sold it to the rabb al-salam in exchange for the debt. And in this scenario, the combination of two transactions is apparent. And when two transactions are combined, two measurements are necessary. So in the scenario where only one measurement is made, the delivery from the muslam ilayh is not valid, and the rabb al-salam is not considered as having received his right. The author of al-Hidayah says: If it is not a salam sale but a loan, i.e., when a person borrowed one kurr of wheat, then the borrower bought and ordered the lender to take possession without saying: first take possession for me, then for yourself, and the lender took possession after one measurement, then this is permissible. Because a loan is called giving as a loan (i'arah). And if a loan were not called giving as a loan, then it would necessitate giving ownership of a thing in exchange for its like on credit, i.e., the borrower returns the same type on credit, which is riba. So it is established that a loan is called giving as a loan. This is why a loan is concluded with the word i'arah. So if someone says: "I give you this dirham as a loan," a loan is concluded. Because in i'arah, a deadline is not necessary; rather, the lender has the right to demand the borrowed item back at any time. So in a loan, a deadline is also not necessary. Thus, it is known that a loan is called giving as a loan, and in i'arah, the borrower returns exactly the same item he took from the lender. So in the case of a loan, what the borrower returns is absolutely the same as the item he took possession of, i.e., even in terms of substitution, the returned item and the possessed item are the same entity.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah deals with a specific scenario in salam (forward sale) contracts. It is a ruling with proof, explaining the validity of delivery when the muslam ilayh (seller) purchases the same commodity from a third party and instructs the rabb al-salam (buyer) to take possession. The commentary begins by laying out two sub-scenarios. In the first, the muslam ilayh buys the wheat and tells the rabb al-salam to take possession for himself; this delivery is invalid because only one measurement occurs, whereas two measurements are required when two separate sale transactions are combined with the condition of measurement (bishart al-kayl). The hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibits the sale of grain until two measures have been applied—one by the seller to the original buyer, and one by that buyer to the subsequent purchaser. In the second sub-scenario, the muslam ilayh instructs the rabb al-salam to first take possession as his agent (measuring for the muslam ilayh) and then take possession for himself; this is valid because two measurements are performed. The passage then addresses a potential objection: since the salam contract precedes the purchase from the third party, how can the later purchase be considered a new sale to the rabb al-salam? The answer is that possession of the muslam fihi is treated legally as the beginning of a new sale, because the debt (dayn) owed in salam is distinct from a specific commodity ('ayn). However, for the specific ruling of prohibiting substitution of the muslam fihi before possession, the debt is treated as the same as the specific commodity. Therefore, after the purchase, it is as if a new sale occurs between the muslam ilayh and the rabb al-salam, necessitating two measurements. Finally, the text contrasts this with a loan (qard) scenario: if the transaction is a loan rather than salam, a single measurement suffices because a loan is legally analogous to a loan for use (i'arah). In i'arah, the borrower returns the identical item, so no second measurement is required. This distinction prevents riba (usury) that would arise if a loan were treated as a deferred exchange of like items. The passage thus carefully delineates the fiqh of salam delivery and reinforces the Hanafi principle that measurement is integral to grain sales to avoid uncertainty (gharar) and riba.

Key Terms
سلم (salam): A forward sale where the price is paid in advance for a specified commodity to be delivered at a future date.
مسلم الیہ (muslam ilayh): The seller in a salam contract, who receives the price and undertakes to deliver the commodity later.
رب السلم (rabb al-salam): The buyer in a salam contract, who pays the price in advance and is entitled to receive the commodity at the agreed time.
مسلم فیہ (muslam fihi): The commodity to be delivered in a salam contract.
کیل (kayl): Measurement by volume or weight, a condition in certain sales to determine quantity.
صاع (sa'): A standard measure for grain, used in the hadith to denote two separate measurements.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where the muslam ilayh buys grain from a third party and orders the rabb al-salam to take possession for himself (without separate measurements), why is the delivery invalid according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the muslam ilayh did not own the grain before selling it.
B) Because only one measurement is performed, whereas two are required when two sale transactions with measurement condition are combined.
C) Because the rabb al-salam did not pay the full price.
D) Because the grain was not of the specified quality.

Key Takeaway
In salam, when the seller procures the muslam fihi from a third party, a single measurement is insufficient; two measurements are required because two sales with measurement condition are combined.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Contrast with Qard: Why a Loan Requires Only One Measurement
Explains why a loan (qard) requires only one measurement in contrast to salam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school treats a loan (qard) differently from salam in terms of measurement, and identify the legal basis for allowing a single measurement.

Core Idea
A loan is legally a loan for use (i'arah); the identical item is returned by operation of law, so no second measurement is needed.

The previous lesson established that in a salam contract, two measurements are required when the seller procures goods from a third party. But what if the transaction is a simple loan (qard) rather than salam? The rule changes: a single measurement suffices. This lesson examines the Hanafi reasoning, which analogizes qard to i'arah (loan for use), thereby preventing the need for a second measurement and avoiding riba.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and its ruling
The scenario: a borrower (qard) of grain buys the same grain from a third party and tells the lender to take possession without two measurements. The ruling: it is valid (ja'iz) with one measurement.
2
Understand the basis: qard as i'arah
In Hanafi fiqh, a loan (qard) is treated as a form of i'arah (loan for use). This prevents riba that would occur if it were considered a sale of like for like on credit.
The text states: 'qard i'arah daina hai' (a loan is giving as a loan).
3
Apply the legal consequence
In i'arah, the borrower returns the identical item ('ayn al-makhudh). Hence, when the borrower buys and orders the lender to take possession, it is as if the borrower is returning the exact same item. No new sale occurs.
Thus, only one measurement (the purchase measurement) is needed; the return measurement is redundant.
4
Distinguish from salam
In salam, the debt (dayn) is distinct from the specific commodity, so a new sale occurs requiring a new measurement. In qard, the debt is considered the same as the specific commodity because of the i'arah analogy.
This distinction is crucial for correct fatwa.

باب السلم
اشرف البدایہ جلد- ضمیم محمل الحديث على مامر والسلم وان كان سابقا لكن قبض المسلم فيه لاحق وانه بمنزلة ابتداء البيع لان العين غير الدين حقيقة وان جعل عينه في حق حكم خاص وهو حرمة الاستبدال فيتحقق البيع بعد الشراء وان لم يكن سلما وكان قرضا فامره بقبض الكر جاز لان القرض اعارة ولهذا ينعقد بلفظ الاعارة فكان مردود عين الماخوذ مطلقا حكما فلا يجتمع الصفقتان
ترجمہ . اگر ایک شخص نے ایک گر گندم میں بیع سلم کی پھر جب ادائے مسلم فیہ کی میعاد آئی تو مسلم الیہ نے ایک آدمی سے ایک گر گندم خریدا اور رب السلم کو اپنے ادائے حق میں اسپر قبضہ کا حکم دیا تو یہ اس کا ادائے حق نہ ہو گا۔ اور اگر اس کو حکم دیا کہ مسلم الیہ کے واسطے قبضہ کر لے پھر اپنے واسطے قبضہ کر لے، پس رب السلام نے اس کو مسلم الیہ کے واسطے کیل کیا پھر اس کو اپنے واسطے کیل کیا تو جائز ہے۔ اس لئے کہ دو صفقہ بشرط الکیل جمع ہو گئے ۔ لہذا دو مرتبہ کیل کرنا ضروری ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اناج کی خرید وفروخت سے منع فرمایا ہے یہاں تک کہ اس میں دو صاع جاری ہوں۔ اور یہی حدیث کا عمل ہے جیسا کہ سابق میں گذر چکا ہے۔ اور مسلم اگر چہ پہلے تھی لیکن مسلم فیہ پر قبضہ بعد میں ہے اور مسلم فیہ پر قبضہ ابتدائے بیع کے مرتبہ میں ہے کیونکہ عین در حقیقت دین کے خلاف ہے اگر چہ ایک خاص حکم یعنی استبدال حرام ہونے میں مال عین ( مقبوض) کو عین دین قرار دیا گیا ہے پس خرید کے بعد فروخت کر نا حق ہو گا۔ اور اگر سلم نہ ہو ( بلکہ ) قرضہ ہو پھر قرضدار نے (خرید کر ) قرض خواہ کو گر پر قبضہ کرنے کا حکم دیا تو یہ جائز ہے اس لیے کہ قرض عاریہ دینا ہے اور اسی وجہ سے لفظ اعارہ سے قرض منعقد ہو جاتا ہے پس بحکم شرع جو واپس کیا گیا ہے وہ مطلقاً بعینہ وہ ہے جولیا گیا تھا لہذا د و صفقہ جمع نہ ہوں گے۔
کہ فیاد کر تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر ایک شخص نے دوسرے سے ایک گر گندم میں عقد سلم کیا پھر جب مسلم فیہ ادا کر نے کی میعاد پوری ہو گئی تو مسلم الیہ نے ایک آدمی سے ایک گر گندم خرید کر رب السلام کو حکم دیا کہ اپنا حق وصول کرنے کے لیے اس پر قبضہ کرلے پس رب اسلم نے مسلم الیہ کے حکم کے مطابق قبضہ کر لیا تو اس سے رب اسلم کا حق وصول نہ ہوگا۔ چنانچہ اگر مقبوض گندم رب السلام کے قبضہ میں ہلاک ہوگیا تو یہ مسلم الیہ کے مال سے ہلاک ہو گا اور رب اسلم کو اپنا حق وصول کرنے کے مطالبہ کا اختیار ہوگا اوراگر مسلم الیہ نے رب السلم کو یہ حکم دیا کہ پہلے وہ مسلم الیہ کی طرف سے وکیل بن کر قبضہ کر لے پھر اپنا حق وصول کرنے کیلئے قبضہ کرلے پس رب السلم نے مسلم الیہ کے حکم کے مطابق پہلے اس کو مسلم الیہ کے واسطے کیل کیا اور پھر اپنے واسطے کیل کیا تو یہ جائز ہے یعنی اس سے رب السلام کا حق وصول ہو جائے گا اور مسلم الیہ کا حق ادا ہو جائے گا۔
دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہاں کیل کی شرط کے ساتھ دو صفقہ جمع ہو گئے ایک صفقہ مسلم الیہ اور اس کے بائع کے درمیان اور دوسرا صفقہ مسلم الیہ اور رب السلم کے درمیان اور جب بشرط الکیل دو صفقہ جمع ہو جائیں تو دو مرتبہ کیل کرنا ضروری ہوگا اور ایک مرتبہ مسلم الیہ کا اپنے بائع سے خریدنے کی وجہ سے کیل کرنا ضروری ہوگا اور ایک مرتبہ مسلم الیہ کا رب السلم کو فروخت کرنے کی وجہ سے کیل کرنا ضروری ہوگا ۔ اور بشرط الکیل دو صفقہ جمع ہونے کی صورت میں دو مرتبہ کیل کرنا اس لئے ضروری ہے کہ ہادی عالم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اناج کی بیج سے منع فرمایا ہے یہاں تک کہ اس میں دو صاع جاری ہوں ایک صاع بائع کا اور دوسرا صاع مشتری کا یعنی جب بائع نے اپنے واسطے خریدا ہے تو اس کو ناپ کر لے اور جب دوسرے کو فروخت کرے گا تو وہ دوسرا ناپ کر لے گا۔ اس حدیث کا یہی محمل ہے جیسا کہ باب المرابحه والتولية
سے متصل فصل میں مذکور ہوا ہے۔
والسلم وان كان سابقاً الخ" سے ایک سوال مقدر کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ مسلم الیہ کا رب اسلم کو فروخت کرنا بہت پہلے ہے اور مسلم الیہ کا اپنے بائع سے خریدنا بہت بعد میں ہے پس مسلم الیہ اپنے بائع سے خریدنے کے بعد رب اسلم کو بیچنے والا نہ ہوگا اور جب مسلم الیہ خریدنے کے بعد رب السلام کو بیچنے والا نہ ہوا تو دو صفقہ بھی جمع نہ ہوئے اور جب دو صفتہ جمع نہ ہوئے تو دو مرتبہ کیل کرنا بھی ضرور کی نہ ہوگا اور جب دو مرتبہ کیل کرنا ضروری نہ ہوا تو جس صورت میں مسلم ایہ نے ایک گر گندم خرید کر رب اسلم کو اپنے ادائے حق کے لیے اس پر قبضہ کرنے کا حکم دیا ہے اس صورت میں مسلم الیہ کا حق ادا ہو جانا چاہیے تھا حالانکہ آپ نے فرمایا ہے کہ اس صورت میں مسلم الیہ کا حق ادا نہ ہو گا ؟
جواب اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ بیع سلم اگر چہ پہلے ہے یعنی مسلم الیہ کی خرید سے پہلے اگر چہسلم کا عقد ہو چکا تھا لیکن رب اسلم کا مسلم فیہ پر قبضہ کرنا مسلم الیہ کی خرید سے بعد میں ہے۔ اور مسلم فیہ پر قبضہ کرنا ابتدائے بیچ کے مرتبہ میں ہے۔ پس گویا رب اسلام اور مسلم الیہ دونوں نے اس مقبوضہ گندم پر از عصرنو عقد کیا ہے۔ اور مسلم فیہ پر قبضہ سے پہلے اس کے بدلے میں دوسری چیز کا لین لازم آتا ہے حالانکہ قبضہ سے پہلے مسلم فیہ کے جادلہ میں سی بھی چیز کالینا حرام ہے اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اس مخصوص کم یعنی یہ دونوں ایک ہی چیز میں ان دونوں میں کوئی غیریت نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اگر دین کو مال معین کا غیر مانا جائے گا تو مسلم فیہ کا تبادلہ کرنا لازم آئیگا حالانکہ استبدال با مسلم فیہ حرام ہے پس خاص طور پر استبدال حرام ہونے کے حق میں دین اور مال عین دونوں کو ایک مانا گیا ہے لیکن اس کے علاوہ باقی تمام جگہوں میں دین حقیقتاً مال عین کا غیر ہو گا اور جب دین یعنی مسلم فیہ مال معین یعنی مقبوضہ گندم کا غیر ہوا تو گویا مسلم الیہ نے ایک گر گندم خرید کر رب السلم کے ہاتھ مسلم فیہ یعنی دین کے عوض فروخت کیا ہے۔ اور اس صورت میں دو صفقوں کا جمع ہونا ظاہر ہے اور جب دو صفقہ جمع ہو گئے تو دو مرتبہ کیل کرنا بھی ضروری ہوگا۔ پس جس صورت میں فقط ایک مرتبہ کیل کیا گیا ہے اس صورت میں مسلم الیہ کی طرف سے ادا ئیگی معتبر نہ ہوگی ۔ اور رب السلم اپنا حق وصول کرنے والا شمار نہ ہو گا۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر بیع سلم نہ ہو بلکہ قرض ہو، یعنی جب ایک آدمی نے ایک گر گندم قرض لیا، پھر قرضدار نے خرید کر قرض خواہ کو قبضہ کرنے کا حکم دیا اور یہ نہیں کہا کہ پہلے میرے واسطے قبضہ کر لے پھر اپنے واسطے قبضہ کر پس قرض خواہ نے اس پر قبضہ کر لیا ، یعنی ایک مرتبہ کیل کر کے اپنے قبضہ میں لے لیا تو یہ جائز ہے کیونکہ قرضہ، عاریت پر دینے کا نام ہے۔ اور اگر قرضہ عاربیت پر دینے کا نام نہ ہو تو تملیک الشئی بجنسه نسيئة لازم آئے گا یعنی قرضدار نے جو چیز لی تھی قرض خواہ کو بنجنہ ادھار واپس کی گئی اور یہ ر بوا ہے پس ثابت ہوا کہ قرض عاریت پر دینے کا نام ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ لفظ اعارہ سے قرضہ منعقد ہو جاتا ہے چنانچہ اگر کسی نے کہا اعر تك هذا الدرهم تو اس سے قرض منعقد ہو جائے گا۔ چونکہ عاریہ میں میعاد لازم نہیں ہوتی بلکہ عاریت پر دینے والے کو ہر وقت شئی مستعار واپس لینے کا حق ہوتا ہے اس لیے قرضہ میں بھی میعاد لازم نہ ہوگی پس معلوم ہوا کہ قرض عاریت پر دینے کا نام ہے اور عاریہ میں عاربیت پر لینے والا جکم شرع بعینہ وہ چیز واپس کرتا ہے جو اس نے معیر سے لی تھی۔ پس قرض کی صورت میں قرضدار جو چیز واپس کرے گا وہ مطلقا اس چیز کا عین ہوگی جس پر قرضدار نے قبضہ کیا تھا یعنی استبدال کے حق میں بھی شئی مردود اور شئی مقبوض کے درمیان عینیت ثابت ہوگی اور استبدال کے
Chapter of Salam. Ashraf al-Hidayah volume - appendix. The interpretation of the hadith according to what has passed. And salam, even though it is earlier, but possession of the muslam fihi is later, and it is like the beginning of a sale because the specific commodity ('ayn) is different from a debt (dayn) in reality, even though it is treated as the same commodity in a specific ruling, which is the prohibition of substitution. So the sale takes place after the purchase. And if it is not salam but a loan, then his order to take possession of the kurr is permissible because a loan is a form of lending (i'arah); therefore it is concluded with the word of i'arah. So the returned item is absolutely the same as the taken item by ruling, so the two transactions are not combined. Translation: If a person made a salam contract for one kurr of wheat, then when the time for delivery of the muslam fihi came, the muslam ilayh bought one kurr of wheat from a person and ordered the rabb al-salam to take possession of it for his right, then this will not be his delivery of the right. And if he ordered him to take possession on behalf of the muslam ilayh, then take possession for himself, then the rabb al-salam measured it for the muslam ilayh, then measured it for himself, then it is permissible. Because two transactions with the condition of measurement are combined. Therefore two measurements are necessary. Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited the sale of grain until two measures are applied. And this is the application of the hadith, as has passed earlier. And even though the salam was earlier, but possession of the muslam fihi is later, and possession of the muslam fihi is in the rank of the beginning of a sale, because the commodity ('ayn) is in reality different from the debt (dayn), even though in a specific ruling, i.e., the prohibition of substitution, the possessed commodity is considered as the same as the debt. So after purchase, selling becomes valid. And if it is not salam but a loan, then the borrower bought and ordered the lender to take possession of the wheat, then this is permissible because a loan is giving as a loan, and therefore it is concluded with the word of i'arah. So by legal ruling, what is returned is absolutely the same as what was taken, so the two transactions are not combined. Explanation of the scenario: If a person made a salam contract with another for one kurr of wheat, then when the time for delivery of the muslam fihi was complete, the muslam ilayh bought one kurr of wheat from a person and ordered the rabb al-salam to take possession of it to receive his right. Then the rabb al-salam took possession according to the order. Then his right is not received. So if the possessed wheat perishes while in the possession of the rabb al-salam, it perishes from the property of the muslam ilayh, and the rabb al-salam has the right to demand his right. And if the muslam ilayh ordered the rabb al-salam to first take possession as his agent, then take possession for his own right, and the rabb al-salam measured it for the muslam ilayh and then measured it for himself, then this is permissible, i.e., the rabb al-salam's right is received and the muslam ilayh's obligation is fulfilled. The proof is that here two transactions with the condition of measurement are combined: one transaction between the muslam ilayh and his seller, and another transaction between the muslam ilayh and the rabb al-salam. And when two transactions with the condition of measurement are combined, two measurements are necessary: one measurement from the muslam ilayh buying from his seller, and one measurement from the muslam ilayh selling to the rabb al-salam. And in the case of combining two transactions with the condition of measurement, two measurements are necessary because the Guide of the Worlds (peace be upon him) prohibited the sale of grain until two measures are applied: one measure from the seller and one measure from the buyer. That is, when the seller has bought for himself, he should measure it, and when he sells to another, that other will measure it. This is the interpretation of this hadith, as mentioned in the connected chapter of the chapter of Murabahah and Tawliyah. The phrase "And salam even though it is earlier, etc." is an answer to an implied question. The question is: The muslam ilayh's sale to the rabb al-salam is much earlier, and the muslam ilayh's purchase from his seller is much later. So after purchasing from his seller, the muslam ilayh will not be the seller to the rabb al-salam. And when the muslam ilayh is not a seller to the rabb al-salam after purchase, then two transactions are not combined. And when two transactions are not combined, then two measurements are not necessary. And when two measurements are not necessary, then in the scenario where the muslam ilayh bought one kurr of wheat and ordered the rabb al-salam to take possession of it for his right, the muslam ilayh's obligation should be fulfilled, even though you said that in this scenario the muslam ilayh's obligation is not fulfilled? The answer is: Even though the salam sale is earlier, i.e., the salam contract had already taken place before the purchase, the rabb al-salam's possession of the muslam fihi is after the purchase. And taking possession of the muslam fihi is in the rank of the beginning of a sale. So it is as if the rabb al-salam and the muslam ilayh have performed a new contract on this possessed wheat. And before possession of the muslam fihi, taking something else in exchange for it becomes necessary, even though taking anything in exchange for the muslam fihi before possession is prohibited. The answer to this is that in this specific matter, there is no difference between the two; they are one thing. Because if the debt is considered different from the specific commodity, then exchanging the muslam fihi becomes necessary, even though substitution of the muslam fihi is prohibited. So specifically in terms of the prohibition of substitution, the debt and the specific commodity are considered one. But in all other places, the debt is in reality different from the specific commodity. And when the debt, i.e., the muslam fihi, is different from the specific commodity, i.e., the possessed wheat, then it is as if the muslam ilayh bought one kurr of wheat and sold it to the rabb al-salam in exchange for the debt. And in this scenario, the combination of two transactions is apparent. And when two transactions are combined, two measurements are necessary. So in the scenario where only one measurement is made, the delivery from the muslam ilayh is not valid, and the rabb al-salam is not considered as having received his right. The author of al-Hidayah says: If it is not a salam sale but a loan, i.e., when a person borrowed one kurr of wheat, then the borrower bought and ordered the lender to take possession without saying: first take possession for me, then for yourself, and the lender took possession after one measurement, then this is permissible. Because a loan is called giving as a loan (i'arah). And if a loan were not called giving as a loan, then it would necessitate giving ownership of a thing in exchange for its like on credit, i.e., the borrower returns the same type on credit, which is riba. So it is established that a loan is called giving as a loan. This is why a loan is concluded with the word i'arah. So if someone says: "I give you this dirham as a loan," a loan is concluded. Because in i'arah, a deadline is not necessary; rather, the lender has the right to demand the borrowed item back at any time. So in a loan, a deadline is also not necessary. Thus, it is known that a loan is called giving as a loan, and in i'arah, the borrower returns exactly the same item he took from the lender. So in the case of a loan, what the borrower returns is absolutely the same as the item he took possession of, i.e., even in terms of substitution, the returned item and the possessed item are the same entity.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah deals with a specific scenario in salam (forward sale) contracts. It is a ruling with proof, explaining the validity of delivery when the muslam ilayh (seller) purchases the same commodity from a third party and instructs the rabb al-salam (buyer) to take possession. The commentary begins by laying out two sub-scenarios. In the first, the muslam ilayh buys the wheat and tells the rabb al-salam to take possession for himself; this delivery is invalid because only one measurement occurs, whereas two measurements are required when two separate sale transactions are combined with the condition of measurement (bishart al-kayl). The hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibits the sale of grain until two measures have been applied—one by the seller to the original buyer, and one by that buyer to the subsequent purchaser. In the second sub-scenario, the muslam ilayh instructs the rabb al-salam to first take possession as his agent (measuring for the muslam ilayh) and then take possession for himself; this is valid because two measurements are performed. The passage then addresses a potential objection: since the salam contract precedes the purchase from the third party, how can the later purchase be considered a new sale to the rabb al-salam? The answer is that possession of the muslam fihi is treated legally as the beginning of a new sale, because the debt (dayn) owed in salam is distinct from a specific commodity ('ayn). However, for the specific ruling of prohibiting substitution of the muslam fihi before possession, the debt is treated as the same as the specific commodity. Therefore, after the purchase, it is as if a new sale occurs between the muslam ilayh and the rabb al-salam, necessitating two measurements. Finally, the text contrasts this with a loan (qard) scenario: if the transaction is a loan rather than salam, a single measurement suffices because a loan is legally analogous to a loan for use (i'arah). In i'arah, the borrower returns the identical item, so no second measurement is required. This distinction prevents riba (usury) that would arise if a loan were treated as a deferred exchange of like items. The passage thus carefully delineates the fiqh of salam delivery and reinforces the Hanafi principle that measurement is integral to grain sales to avoid uncertainty (gharar) and riba.

Key Terms
قرض (qard): A loan of a fungible commodity that is to be repaid in the same type and quantity.
عارہ (i'arah): A gratuitous loan of a specific item for use, after which the identical item must be returned.
ربا (riba): Usury or unjustified increase in a loan or sale, prohibited in Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does a loan (qard) require only one measurement when the borrower buys the same commodity from a third party and orders the lender to take possession?
A) Because the borrower is not required to measure at all.
B) Because the loan is treated as i'arah, so returning the identical item is assumed by law.
C) Because the lender can decide how many measurements are needed.
D) Because the hadith only applies to salam, not to loans.

Key Takeaway
In a loan (qard), a single measurement suffices because the loan is legally analogous to a loan for use (i'arah), where the identical item is returned by operation of law.

Why Salam Requires Two Measurements and Qard Only One
Explains the ruling with proof for salam and qard on the necessity of measuring twice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number of measurements required in salam and qard and explain the underlying distinction between dayn and 'ayn.

Core Idea
Salam requires two measurements because dayn and 'ayn are distinct; qard requires one because the returned item is the same 'ayn.

In the Hanafi fiqh of sales, a subtle but critical distinction exists between salam (advance sale) and qard (loan) when the seller purchases the commodity from a third party and directs the buyer to take possession. The question arises: does this discharge the debt with one measurement, or must the commodity be measured twice? The passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah unpacks this through the concepts of dayn (debt) and 'ayn (specific property), revealing why salam demands a double measurement while qard suffices with one.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting scenarios
First, understand the two scenarios: (1) salam where the muslam ilayh (seller) buys wheat and orders rabb al-salam (buyer) to take possession; (2) qard where the borrower buys wheat and orders the lender to take possession. The key difference is the nature of the obligation.
The question assumes the buyer takes possession after the seller purchases, not before.
2
Analyze the salam scenario
In salam, the muslam fih (commodity owed) is a debt (dayn) in the seller's liability. When the seller purchases specific wheat ('ayn), he is acquiring a new property. Directing the buyer to take that wheat as payment involves two transfers: first the seller's purchase from the third party, then the seller's constructive sale to the buyer. Because dayn and 'ayn are legally distinct, two sales occur, each requiring measurement.
The prohibition of istibdal (exchanging the muslam fih) is avoided by considering dayn and 'ayn identical only for that purpose.
3
Analyze the qard scenario
In qard, the obligation is to return the equivalent of what was borrowed, but Hanafi fiqh treats qard as a form of 'ariyah (borrowing for use). Therefore, the item returned is considered the very same 'ayn as what the lender originally gave. When the borrower purchases wheat and directs the lender to take it, no new sale occurs between them; it is simply a return of the same 'ayn. Only one transfer (the borrower's purchase) takes place, so only one measurement is needed.
The treatment of qard as 'ariyah prevents riba and simplifies the transaction.
4
Apply the principles to derive the ruling
From the above, the ruling is: in salam, two measurements are wajib; in qard, one measurement suffices. The underlying principle is the legal treatment of dayn versus 'ayn: for the purpose of the prohibition of exchange, they are considered identical only in salam to avoid istibdal, but otherwise they are distinct. In qard, they are always identical because the returned item is the same 'ayn.
This ruling is agreed upon within the Hanafi school (zahir al-riwayah).
5
Contrast with other schools
Other madhhabs, such as the Shafi'i, may not distinguish between dayn and 'ayn in this manner and may treat the delivery in salam as a single transaction, thus not requiring two measurements. This highlights the unique Hanafi reasoning based on the nature of the contract.
The passage itself does not discuss other schools, but the difference is implicit in the Hanafi position.

From 'Al-Salam even if it is previous...' is the answer to a presumed question. The question is: The muslam ilayh's sale to rabb al-salam is much earlier, and the muslam ilayh's purchase from his seller is much later. So after the muslam ilayh purchases, he would not be the seller to rabb al-salam. When two sales are not combined, two measurements are not necessary. So why did you say that in the case where the muslam ilayh bought a kurr of wheat and ordered rabb al-salam to take possession for payment of his right, the muslam ilayh's right is not discharged? The answer: the salam sale was earlier, but the rabb al-salam's taking possession of the muslam fih is after the muslam ilayh's purchase. Taking possession of the muslam fih is in the position of the beginning of the sale. So it is as if both concluded a new contract on that possessed wheat. Taking a substitute before possession of the muslam fih is necessary, but taking anything in exchange for the muslam fih before possession is prohibited. The answer is that for this specific matter, they are not different. If debt is considered different from specific property, then exchange of the muslam fih would be necessary, but exchange of the muslam fih is prohibited. So specifically for the prohibition of exchange, debt and specific property are considered the same. But elsewhere, debt is different from specific property. When debt (muslam fih) is different from the specific property (possessed wheat), then the muslam ilayh bought a kurr of wheat and sold it to rabb al-salam in exchange for the debt. Here two sales are combined, so two measurements are necessary. If only one measurement was done, the payment is not valid. The author of al-Hidayah says: if it is not salam but a loan, i.e., a person borrowed a kurr of wheat, then the borrower bought and ordered the lender to take possession, and the lender took possession with one measurement, it is permissible because qard is giving on the basis of 'ariyah. If qard were not 'ariyah, then tamlik al-shay' bi jinsihi nasi'ah would occur, which is riba. So qard is 'ariyah. For this reason, the word i'arah creates a qard contract. Since 'ariyah does not require a fixed term, qard also does not. Thus, qard is 'ariyah, and in 'ariyah, the borrower returns the exact same thing. So in qard, what the borrower returns is exactly the same 'ayn of what he possessed. In terms of exchange, the returned item and the possessed item have 'ayniyyah. And since the returned item is the same 'ayn, the borrower's order for the lender to take possession and the lender's taking possession are not in the position of a sale. So only one sale is found, and one measurement suffices. Thus, the lender's measurement is on behalf of the borrower as an agent, and no second measurement is needed.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the commentary on al-Hidayah, addressing a subtle point in salam (advance sale) versus qard (loan) regarding the necessity of measuring twice when the buyer (rabb al-salam) takes delivery of the commodity through the seller's purchase from a third party. The commentator begins by presenting a hypothetical objection: if the muslam ilayh (seller in salam) buys a kurr of wheat from a third party and then allows the rabb al-salam to take possession of it as payment of the debt (muslam fih), why would this not discharge the debt, given that the sale of the wheat to rabb al-salam occurred before the muslam ilayh's purchase? The answer explains that although the salam contract preceded the purchase, the actual delivery of the muslam fih to rabb al-salam occurs after the muslam ilayh's purchase. This delivery is treated as a new sale between the muslam ilayh and rabb al-salam. Since the muslam fih is a debt (dayn) in the muslam ilayh's liability, and the wheat purchased is a specific property ('ayn), they are considered different entities for most purposes. However, to avoid the prohibition of exchanging the muslam fih (istibdal), they are treated as identical only in that specific context. Because they are otherwise different, the transaction involves two sales: the muslam ilayh buying from the third party and selling to rabb al-salam, thus requiring two measurements (one for each sale). If only one measurement is performed, the payment is invalid. The passage then contrasts this with qard: in a loan, the borrower's purchase and delivery to the lender is treated as returning the same 'ayn (specific property) because qard is considered a form of 'ariyah (borrowing for use). The lender's right is to the same specific item, not a debt. Therefore, no separate sale occurs between the borrower and lender; only one measurement (on behalf of the borrower) is needed. The reasoning hinges on the Hanafi distinction between debt (dayn) and specific property ('ayn) and the nature of qard as 'ariyah. The commentary follows the author's order: first the question, then the answer for salam, then the distinction for qard.

Key Terms
دین (dayn): A liability or debt that is not specific to a particular item; it exists in the dhimmah (liability).
عین ('ayn): A specific, identifiable property, as opposed to a debt.
قرض (qard): A loan where the borrower returns the equivalent; treated as 'ariyah (borrowing for use) to avoid riba.
سلم (salam): An advance sale where the price is paid upfront and the commodity is delivered later.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, why does salam require two measurements while qard requires only one?
A) Because salam involves a sale, while qard is a loan.
B) Because in salam, the muslam fih is a debt (dayn), distinct from the specific property, requiring two transfers; in qard, the returned item is treated as the same 'ayn, so only one transfer.
C) Because salam is prohibited, so extra caution is needed.
D) Because the Hanafi school requires two witnesses for salam.

Key Takeaway
Salam requires two measurements because the muslam fih is a debt distinct from the specific property, creating two sales; qard requires one because the returned item is legally the same 'ayn, eliminating a second sale.

Invalidity of Delivery in Salam When Buyer's Bags Used in Absence
Ruling and proof on salam delivery in buyer's absence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delivery in salam when the buyer's bags are used in his absence and explain the proof based on the nature of debt.

Core Idea
In salam, the buyer's right is a debt (dayn) in the dhimmah, not in specific property; measuring into his bags in his absence does not discharge the seller.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a practical scenario in salam contracts. The buyer (rabb al-salam) orders the seller (muslam ilayh) to measure the wheat into the buyer's own bags, but the buyer is absent. The text rules that this does not constitute valid delivery, because the buyer's right is a debt, not attached to the specific bags. The seller remains liable. Let's unpack the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the seller measuring the commodity into the buyer's bags in the buyer's absence. The ruling is that it is not a valid discharge (qada') of the seller's obligation.
The ruling is 'batil' in the sense that the debt is not discharged.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is an analogy (qiyas) to a creditor giving a purse to a debtor to weigh coins. In both cases, the creditor does not gain possession.
The analogy is stated: 'like if someone owed dirhams...'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The effective cause ('illa) is that the right is a debt (dayn) in the dhimmah, not attached to a specific container. Just as the creditor's right is not in the purse, the buyer's right is not in the bags. Therefore, placing the wheat into the bags does not transfer possession.
The debt is an obligation, not a tangible property.
4
Note intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
No disagreement among the Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) on this ruling; it is unanimous from the zahir al-riwayah.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The wheat remains the seller's property. If it is destroyed, the loss falls on the seller, not the buyer. The seller must still deliver the wheat or its value.
Valid delivery requires buyer's presence or explicit agency.

کرنے والا نہ ہوگا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک آدمی نے ایک گر گندم کی بیع سلم کی پھر رب السلم نے مسلم الیہ کو حکم دیا کہ وہ ایک گر گندم ناپ کر میرے تھیلوں میں بھر دے پس مسلم الیہ نے رب اسلم کی عدم موجودگی میں (ایک گر گندم) ناپ کر اس کے تھیلوں میں بھر دیا تو ایسا کرنے سے مسلم الیہ کی طرف سے مسلم فیہ کی ادائیگی درست نہ ہوگی، چنانچہ اگر ابھی یہ گندم تلف ہو جائے تو مسلم الیہ کا مال ضائع ہو گا۔ رب اسما نقصان شمار نہ ہوگا۔ کا اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ رب السلام کا حق دین میں ہے نہ کہ کسی مال معین میں۔ اور دین ایک ایسا وصف ہے جو ذ مہ میں ثابت ہوتا ہے ایسے وصف کو رب السلم کے تھیلوں میں بھرنا ایک امر محال ہے پس رب السلم کے ناپنے کے حکم نے اس کی ملک کو نہیں پایا بلکہ مسلم الیہ کی ملک کو پایا ہے اور جب رب اسلم کے حکم نے اس کی ملک کو نہیں پایا تو اس کا یہ حکم کہ ناپ دے صحیح نہیں ہوا۔ اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا گویا مسلم الیہ نے رب اسلم سے ان تھیلوں کو عاریہ لیکر ان میں اپنی ذاتی چیز بھری ہے اور یہ ظاہر ہے کہ ایسا کرنے سے مسلم الیہ اپنا حق یعنی مسلم فیہ ادا
If someone makes salam in a kurr of wheat, then rabb al-salam orders the muslam ilayh to measure it and put it into my bags, and he does so in the absence of rabb al-salam, what is the ruling? He (al-Quduri) said: And whoever makes salam in a kurr, then rabb al-salam orders the muslam ilayh to measure it into the bags of rabb al-salam, and he does so while he (rabb al-salam) is absent, it is not a discharge, because the order to measure is not valid, as it did not encounter the property of the orderer, because his right is in the debt, not in the specific property. So the muslam ilayh becomes a borrower of the bags from him, and he has placed his own property in them. It becomes like if someone owed dirhams as a debt, and he gave him a purse to weigh the dirhams in it, he would not become a possessor. Translation: And if someone made salam in a kurr of wheat, then rabb al-salam ordered the muslam ilayh to measure it into his (rabb al-salam's) bags, and the muslam ilayh measured it while rabb al-salam was absent, then this is not a valid discharge (of the wajib) because rabb al-salam's order to measure is not valid. The reason is that the order of rabb al-salam did not encounter the property of the orderer, because rabb al-salam's right is in the debt (non-specific) and not in any specific property. So the muslam ilayh becomes a borrower of the bags from rabb al-salam, while he has placed his owned property in them. This is like if someone owed dirhams as a debt, and the creditor gave a purse to the debtor to weigh the dirhams in it, the creditor would not become a possessor of his debt. Explanation: The scenario is that a person made salam in a kurr of wheat, then rabb al-salam ordered the muslam ilayh to measure a kurr of wheat and fill his bags. The muslam ilayh measured it in the absence of rabb al-salam and filled his bags. Doing so, the payment of the muslam fih by the muslam ilayh is not valid. If the wheat is then destroyed, the muslam ilayh's property is lost, not rabb al-salam's loss. The proof is that rabb al-salam's right is in the debt, not in any specific property. Debt is an attribute established in the dhimmah; filling such an attribute into rabb al-salam's bags is impossible. So the order to measure did not encounter his property but rather the muslam ilayh's property. Since the order did not encounter his property, the order 'measure' is not valid. It becomes as if the muslam ilayh borrowed the bags from rabb al-salam and filled them with his own property. Clearly, this does not discharge the muslam ilayh's right (i.e., the muslam fih).
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the text of Al-Hidayah (and its commentary) addressing a specific scenario in salam contracts. The issue: when a buyer (rabb al-salam) orders the seller (muslam ilayh) to measure the commodity (muslam fih) into the buyer's own bags in the buyer's absence, does that discharge the seller's obligation? The text rules that it does not. The reasoning is grounded in the nature of the buyer's right, which is a debt (dayn) in the seller's liability, not a right to any specific property. Since the debt is not attached to the specific bags, the buyer's order to place the wheat into his bags does not effectively transfer ownership or create possession for the buyer. Instead, the seller is considered to have borrowed the bags from the buyer and filled them with his own property. Therefore, the wheat remains the seller's property, and if it is destroyed, the loss falls on the seller, not the buyer. The commentary illustrates this with an analogy: if a creditor gives a purse to a debtor to weigh coins, and the debtor does so, the creditor does not thereby take possession of the debt. The passage emphasizes that the buyer's right is in the dhimmah (liability) and cannot be physically placed into bags. The cure for validity would be for the buyer to be present or to explicitly authorize the seller to take possession on his behalf in a valid manner. This ruling underscores the Hanafi principle that in salam, the subject matter is a debt, not a specific commodity, so physical delivery requires explicit transfer of possession (qabd) with the buyer's consent and awareness.

Key Terms
غرائر (ghara'ir): Bags or sacks used for storing grain.
قضاء (qada'): Discharge or fulfillment of a debt or obligation.
دين (dayn): A debt or liability in the dhimmah, not a specific tangible asset.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, if the buyer in a salam contract orders the seller to measure the wheat into the buyer's bags in the buyer's absence, what is the ruling?
A) The seller's debt is discharged, and the buyer bears the risk.
B) The delivery is valid only if the buyer sends a representative.
C) The delivery is not valid; the seller remains liable for the debt.
D) It is valid if the buyer has previously taken possession of the bags.

Key Takeaway
In a salam contract, the buyer's right is a debt (dayn) in the seller's liability; physical delivery requires actual transfer of possession with the buyer's presence or explicit agency, and using the buyer's containers in his absence does not discharge the seller's obligation.

Possession in Salam: Ordering Measurement into Buyer's Bags in Absentia
Hidayah ruling on possession via qiyas: salam buyer's order invalid due to debt nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on possession when a salam buyer orders measurement into his own bags in absentia and explain the qiyas basis distinguishing dayn from 'ayn.

Core Idea
A salam buyer's right is in the debt, not the specific goods—placement into his bags does not create possession.

In salam contracts, the buyer pays in advance for a future delivery of specified goods. A key question is when the seller's delivery discharges the debt. This lesson examines a scenario from Al-Hidayah where the buyer orders the seller to measure the goods into the buyer's own bags while the buyer is absent. The ruling clarifies that such an action does not constitute valid delivery because the buyer's claim is on a debt (dayn), not specific property ('ayn).

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract and parties
Recognize that this is a salam contract where the buyer (Rabb al-Salam) orders the seller (Muslim ilayh) to measure the wheat into the buyer's bags.
2
State the ruling
The order does not constitute valid delivery (qada), so the buyer does not take possession, and the seller is not discharged.
The text says 'lam yakun qada' (it is not payment).
3
Analyze the legal cause (illa)
The key reason: the buyer's right is in the debt (dayn), not in the specific wheat. Therefore, his order to measure into his own bags is ineffective because it does not correspond to his property.
The author states: 'لان حقه في الدين دون العين'.
4
Apply the qiyas analogy
Compare to a creditor giving a bag to a debtor to weigh dirhams: the debtor does not thereby take possession. Hence, the same principle applies to salam.
The analogy shows the general rule for debts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن اسلم فى كرّ فامر رب السلم ان يكيله المسلم اليه في غرائر رب السلم ففعل وهو غائب لم يكن قضاء لان الامر بالكيل لم يصح لانه لم يصادف ملك الأمر لان حقه في الدين دون العين فصار المسلم اليه مستعيرا للغرائر منه وقد جعل ملك نفسه فيها فصار كما لو كان عليه دراهم دين فدفع اليه كيسا ليزنها المديون فيه لم يصر قابضا
He said: And if one makes a salam contract for a kurr (measure), then the buyer orders the seller to measure it into the buyer's bags, and he does so while the buyer is absent, this does not constitute payment. Because the order to measure is not valid, as it did not correspond to the property of the orderer, since his right is in the debt (dayn) and not in the specific article. Thus the seller becomes a borrower of the bags from him, and he placed his own property into them. This is like if someone owes dirhams as a debt, and the creditor gives him a bag to weigh the dirhams in it, the debtor does not become possessed.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from Al-Hidayah on possession in a salam contract. The scenario: A buyer (Rabb al-Salam) orders the seller (Muslim ilayh) to measure the salam commodity (here, wheat) into the buyer's own bags, but the buyer is absent. The seller does so. The ruling is that this does not constitute valid delivery (qada) by the seller, nor does the buyer take possession. The reason is that the buyer's right is a debt (dayn) in the seller's liability, not a specific article ('ayn). Therefore, the buyer's order to measure into his bags is ineffective because it does not apply to his own property. Instead, the seller effectively borrows the bags to store his own wheat. This is analogous to a debt of dirhams: if a creditor gives a bag to the debtor to weigh the dirhams, the creditor does not thereby take possession of the dirhams. The ruling illustrates the Hanafi principle that debt is not specific property, and mere placement into one's own containers does not create possession unless the right is in the specific article.

Key Terms
رب السلم (Rabb al-Salam): The buyer in a salam contract, who pays in advance for deferred delivery
مسلم اليه (Muslim ilayh): The seller in a salam contract, who receives advance payment and is obliged to deliver the commodity later
دين (dayn): A debt or liability that is not specific property; it is an obligation in the liability (dhimma)
عين ('ayn): Specific property or an individual object that can be possessed
قضاء (qada): Payment or discharge of a debt; fulfillment of the salam obligation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hidayah passage, why does the buyer's order to fill his own bags fail to constitute possession?
A) The buyer was absent and did not witness the measurement.
B) The seller did not measure correctly.
C) The buyer's right is in the debt, not the specific wheat.
D) The bags were not purchased from the seller.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a salam buyer's right is a debt, not specific property; thus, ordering measurement into his own bags does not transfer possession or discharge the seller.

Possession by Agent's Act in Purchase
Hidayah ruling on possession when buyer orders seller to measure purchased specific commodity into his own bags in absentia

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why in a purchase contract a buyer's order to the seller to measure the purchased good into the buyer's own bags effects possession, and distinguish this from the salam contract.

Core Idea
In purchase, ownership of the specific good makes the buyer's order valid and the seller his agent.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies a practical scenario: what happens when a buyer of specific wheat tells the seller to measure it into the buyer's bags while the buyer is absent. The ruling hinges on the buyer's ownership of the specific article ('ayn) from the moment of sale. Let's unpack the reasoning and contrast it with the earlier salam case.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is: buyer orders seller to measure purchased wheat into the buyer's own bags in the buyer's absence. The ruling: the buyer becomes a possessor (qabid) and the seller is discharged from liability.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is rational (qiyas): because the buyer owns the specific article ('ayn) by the sale, his order is valid and the seller acts as his agent.
The text states: 'لانه ملک العين بالبيع' (because he owns the specific article by the sale).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Ownership of the 'ayn means the buyer has property rights over that specific wheat. Therefore, any order concerning it (like measuring, grinding, or even destroying) is legally effective and attributed to the buyer.
This contrasts with salam where the seller still owns the specific wheat until delivery, so the buyer's order would not affect the seller's property.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf with salam
The text draws two analogies: grinding and throwing into the sea. In purchase, the flour or loss belongs to the buyer; in salam, to the seller. This shows that the practical consequence of ownership of the 'ayn is that risk and benefit pass to the buyer upon contract.
This distinction is critical for determining who bears loss and when possession is achieved.
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that possession is valid in purchase by the seller's act as agent, even without the buyer's physical presence.
This is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is the sound view (asahh).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو كانت الحنطة مشتراة والمسألة بحالها صار قابضا لان الامر قد صح حيث صادف ملکه لانه ملک العين بالبيع الا ترى انه لو امره بالطحن كان الطحين فى السلم للمسلم اليه وفى الشرى للمشترى لصحة الامر وكذا اذا امره ان يصبه في البحر في السلم يهلک من مال المسلم اليه وفى الشرى من مال المشترى ويتقرر الثمن عليه لما قلنا ولهذا يكتفى بذلك الكيل فى الشرى فى الصحيح لانه نائب عنه في الكيل والقبض بالوقوع في غرائر المشترى
And if the wheat were purchased (as a specific commodity) and the situation were the same, then the buyer becomes a possessor. Because the order is valid since it corresponded to his property, for he owns the specific article by the sale. Do you not see that if he ordered him to grind it, the flour in the salam case belongs to the seller, and in the purchase case belongs to the buyer, due to the validity of the order. Similarly, if he ordered him to throw it into the sea, in the salam case the loss is from the seller's property, and in the purchase case from the buyer's property, and the price is confirmed against him for what we said. For this reason, reliance is placed on that measurement in purchase according to the correct view, because he is his agent in measuring, and possession occurs by the falling into the buyer's bags.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage is the counterpart to the previous ruling, also from Al-Hidayah. It contrasts the salam case with a regular purchase (shira) of specific wheat. In a purchase, the buyer becomes owner of the specific commodity ('ayn) by the contract. Therefore, when the buyer orders the seller to measure the wheat into the buyer's bags in the buyer's absence, the order is valid because it applies to the buyer's own property (the wheat he now owns). The seller acts as the buyer's agent in measuring, and by placing the wheat into the buyer's bags, possession is achieved. The text draws a distinction: if the buyer ordered the seller to grind the wheat, the flour would belong to the buyer in a purchase, but to the seller in salam (since the seller still owns the specific wheat until delivery). Similarly, if ordered to throw it into the sea, the loss falls on the buyer in a purchase, but on the seller in salam. This illustrates that ownership of the 'ayn is key: in purchase, the buyer owns the specific article, so his orders regarding it are valid and possession is attained.

Key Terms
شراء (shira): Purchase of a specific (mu'ayyan) good, as opposed to salam which is for a debt
قابض (qabid): One who takes physical or constructive possession of a specific good
نائب (na'ib): Agent; the seller acts as the buyer's agent in measuring and placing

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a purchase contract, if the buyer orders the seller to measure the wheat into the buyer's bags in the buyer's absence, why does the buyer become possessor?
A) Because the buyer owns the specific wheat by the sale
B) Because the seller is always the buyer's agent
C) Because the buyer's order is a general permission
D) Because the bags are new

Key Takeaway
In a purchase of a specific good, the buyer's order to the seller to measure it into the buyer's containers effects possession because the buyer already owns the specific article, making the seller his agent.
